b'2019 American League Preview'
b'Last year\xe2\x80\x99s division champions \xe2\x80\x94 Boston, Cleveland and Houston \xe2\x80\x94 seem poised to repeat, but the Yankees, A\xe2\x80\x99s, Angels, Twins and Rays loom as challengers.'
b'By Tyler Kepner'
b'The Houston Astros blitzed through their first four playoff games last October, including the opener of the American League Championship Series at Fenway Park in Boston. Then they lost four in a row to the Red Sox, who went on to replace them as World Series champions.'
b'George Springer, the most valuable player of the 2017 World Series, did not watch a moment of Boston\xe2\x80\x99s triumph over the Los Angeles Dodgers. He was not despondent, though. He was simply taking time for himself after a largely satisfying season.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cA lot of people think when you lose you\xe2\x80\x99re sitting at home all destroyed for a long time, but a lot has to go right to get where we got the previous year,\xe2\x80\x9d Springer said this spring at the Astros\xe2\x80\x99 training complex in West Palm Beach, Fla. \xe2\x80\x9cWe just got beat. One of the things about this game is you\xe2\x80\x99ve got to be able to accept failure. We didn\xe2\x80\x99t have a bad year. We lost in the A.L.C.S. You move on.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'[M.L.B. Season Preview: Stuffed to Its Seams]'
b'The Astros never expected to string together championships. General Manager Jeff Luhnow, who often makes blackjack analogies, understands that sometimes, the cards will not flip his way. But the Astros keep getting a seat at the table and tipping the odds in their favor.'
b'They turned to the free-agent market to find an ideal fit for their lineup: Michael Brantley, the former Cleveland left fielder who signed a two-year, $32 million deal. Brantley is a lefty in a right-leaning lineup, and a premier contact hitter who accentuates what the Astros do best.'
b'Houston ranked sixth in the majors in runs last season, and only the Indians\xe2\x80\x99 hitters had fewer strikeouts. Brantley had 55 extra-base hits and the second-lowest strikeout percentage in the majors, trailing only the Los Angeles Angels\xe2\x80\x99 Andrelton Simmons.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cGood things happen when you put the ball in play,\xe2\x80\x9d said Brantley, who struck out only 60 times in 631 plate appearances. \xe2\x80\x9cRallies can start with an error or a miscommunication on a fly ball; you don\xe2\x80\x99t know how. You look around this locker room, not too many guys strike out in this lineup. We put the ball in play hard and take our chances.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Opponents could make up a bit more ground against Houston this season. The Astros\xe2\x80\x99 pitchers led the majors in strikeouts, but the team subsequently lost Charlie Morton to free agency and Lance McCullers Jr. to Tommy John surgery; both averaged at least 10 strikeouts per nine innings. To fill those spots \xe2\x80\x94 and the one left by the unsigned free agent Dallas Keuchel \xe2\x80\x94 the Astros will use Collin McHugh, Wade Miley and Brad Peacock or Framber Valdez, with power arms waiting in the high minors.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re a pretty complete team, and that sometimes brings questions,\xe2\x80\x9d Manager A.J. Hinch said. \xe2\x80\x9cI understand why they\xe2\x80\x99re there, but they don\xe2\x80\x99t necessarily have to be there. We have five really good starting pitching candidates and we have some youngsters that are coming fast. The rotation\xe2\x80\x99s not keeping me up at night.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Hinch can rest easy: There may be no clear favorite among the power teams in this league, but the Astros look like the safest bet to push through to the World Series.'
b'They have far more depth than their rivals in the A.L. West. The Oakland Athletics, who won 97 games last season, are like the buddy in your fantasy league who loads up on some categories but ignores others. In this case, the A\xe2\x80\x99s have lots of sluggers, relievers and star defenders, but no semblance of a rotation.'
b"The A\xe2\x80\x99s are good enough in those areas to at least contend, assuming a strong return by the Gold Glove-winning first baseman Matt Olson, who will miss six weeks after breaking a bone in his right hand on the team's trip to Japan. A rotator-cuff strain to Jesus Luzardo, their top pitching prospect, hurts their depth, but if the A\xe2\x80\x99s have a chance, they will find a way to make shrewd additions. One thing is certain: Designated hitter Khris Davis \xe2\x80\x94 the majors\xe2\x80\x99 home run leader since 2016 \xe2\x80\x94 will bat .247. It has been his precise average in each of the last four seasons."
b'The Los Angeles Angels have committed about $430 million to center fielder Mike Trout through 2030. That gives them plenty of time to find a way to finally win a playoff game with the game\xe2\x80\x99s best player on their roster. They think it could happen this fall.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re going to be a strong offensive club: We\xe2\x80\x99re going to increase our on-base percentage, and our home runs are going to be there again this year,\xe2\x80\x9d General Manager Billy Eppler said. \xe2\x80\x9cAs a lot of clubs can say, health is going to be very, very important to us. We\xe2\x80\x99ve been the example of what can happen to a club when you don\xe2\x80\x99t have good health. If we can get north of 26 starts out of our starters, we\xe2\x80\x99re going to be in a really, really good position.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'For the Angels, that could be asking too much. Their starters have a dubious health history, and adding Matt Harvey as a free agent most likely won\xe2\x80\x99t alter that trend. Andrew Heaney has had elbow inflammation in spring training, and Tyler Skaggs dealt with forearm fatigue. Shohei Ohtani will hit this season, but his recovery from Tommy John surgery will keep him off the mound.'
b'The team that truly taunted the pitching gods, though, is the Texas Rangers. All four of their new starters \xe2\x80\x94 Lance Lynn, Shelby Miller, Drew Smyly and Edinson Volquez \xe2\x80\x94 have had Tommy John surgery in the last three and a half years.'
b'[N.L. Preview: A Deep Talent Pool Should Keep the Dodgers Afloat]'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt helps, because we can lean on each other: \xe2\x80\x98Hey, do you feel this, what do you do between starts?\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d said Smyly, who spent the last two seasons with Seattle and the Chicago Cubs, yet never threw a pitch for either team. \xe2\x80\x9cBut at the same time, I think all of us are over talking about it. We just want to put it behind us and go play again.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Rangers, likewise, are eager to bury their recent past; their 95 losses last season matched their most since 1985. Their hopes for improvement rest on young hitters like Joey Gallo, Ronald Guzman, Nomar Mazara and Rougned Odor, who strike out too much but could break into stardom as the team prepares to move to a new Arlington ballpark \xe2\x80\x94 with a retractable roof \xe2\x80\x94 next season.'
b'The Seattle Mariners made a noble effort to end baseball\xe2\x80\x99s longest playoff drought (since 2001), but they should now replace the Rangers in the division cellar. They allowed 34 more runs than they scored last season but still finished 16 games over .500. Recognizing the anomaly, General Manager Jerry Dipoto spent the winter dumping Robinson Cano, Nelson Cruz, Edwin Diaz, James Paxton, Jean Segura, Mike Zunino and others.'
b'Some veterans, like Jay Bruce and Edwin Encarnacion, came back as part of salary swaps. But Dipoto, baseball\xe2\x80\x99s most active general manager, could trade them this summer in an effort to build a more stable foundation.'
b'Encarnacion came to Seattle in a trade with the Cleveland Indians, who shed 10 of the 21 players who appeared in their three-game division series loss to the Astros. Those 10 players will earn more than $95 million for their new teams this season, and the Indians added few veteran replacements besides Carlos Santana and Carlos Gonzalez.'
b'The Indians won\xe2\x80\x99t win the division without major contributions from shortstop Francisco Lindor, who was slowed this spring by a calf injury, and third baseman Jose Ramirez, who hit .154 from last Aug. 15 through the end of the playoffs. But their rotation is so dominant that they should still have enough offense to get by.'
b'Only 15 major leaguers worked 175 innings while recording 200 strikeouts last season, and four were Indians: Corey Kluber, Trevor Bauer, Carlos Carrasco and Mike Clevinger. With those starters and the All-Star closer Brad Hand, the Indians should win the Central for the fourth year in a row.'
b'The Minnesota Twins, under new manager Rocco Baldelli, are the only team that could catch them. The Twins added the veterans Nelson Cruz, Marwin Gonzalez, C.J. Cron and Jonathan Schoop to their lineup, and a progressive new pitching coach \xe2\x80\x94 Wes Johnson, who came from the University of Arkansas \xe2\x80\x94 should help them get more from their staff.'
b'To win, though, the Twins need more from their talented but erratic young core: Jose Berrios, Byron Buxton, Max Kepler, Jorge Polanco, Eddie Rosario and Miguel Sano. All should be in their primes, and the Twins would like to stop guessing how good they can be.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou can dream a lot on the potential upside of that group, and you see spurts of it,\xe2\x80\x9d said Derek Falvey, the Twins\xe2\x80\x99 president for baseball operations. \xe2\x80\x9cThe key, in my mind, is how do you get all those guys firing together at the same time? Because if you do, that\xe2\x80\x99s a really talented crew, and we haven\xe2\x80\x99t quite seen the potential of that entire group all working at the same time.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Even if they cannot catch Cleveland, the Twins could claim a wild card by feasting on the weak in the division. The bottom three teams each lost at least 98 games last season, and none have done much to improve.'
b'While the Chicago White Sox flirted with Bryce Harper and Manny Machado in free agency, they still have never given a free-agent contract richer than $68 million. They are deep in prospects, but some of the most promising ones from last spring \xe2\x80\x94 infielder Yoan Moncada and starter Lucas Giolito \xe2\x80\x94 were major disappointments in the summer. Eloy Jimenez, an electrifying rookie outfielder who signed a six-year, $43 million contract in late March, will try to change that.'
b'The Kansas City Royals should at least be interesting in the way they deploy the speedsters Whit Merrifield, Billy Hamilton and Adalberto Mondesi, three of the 11 major leaguers with more than 30 stolen bases last year. This will be a painstaking rebuilding process, but the last one resulted in two pennants and the 2015 World Series title.'
b'The Detroit Tigers owe Miguel Cabrera $162 million for the next five seasons, a staggering figure for a player who turns 36 in April and missed most of last season with a ruptured biceps tendon. He\xe2\x80\x99s a future Hall of Famer, and a renaissance season \xe2\x80\x94 35 home runs \xe2\x80\x94 would give Cabrera 500 for his career. But there\xe2\x80\x99s not much else to draw interest.'
b'The Tigers\xe2\x80\x99 former architect, Dave Dombrowski, is now the president for baseball operations for the Boston Red Sox and in 2018, he earned the championship he could never quite get in Detroit. It\xe2\x80\x99s fair to expect the Red Sox to repeat in the East, but no team has successfully defended a World Series title since the 2000 Yankees.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s a lot of reasons behind that, but first and foremost it\xe2\x80\x99s tough to win, period,\xe2\x80\x9d Dombrowski said. \xe2\x80\x9cYou get a lot of breaks when you win. Even having a good club, you need a break here or there. Sometimes, you just don\xe2\x80\x99t get as many.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Red Sox lost no significant players from the majors\xe2\x80\x99 best offense, and re-signed the postseason star Nathan Eovaldi to keep their rotation intact. Starters Chris Sale, David Price, Rick Porcello, Eovaldi and Eduardo Rodriguez cannot double as relievers in the regular season as they did last October, but the offense and rotation should make up for an imperfect bullpen.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cOn a nightly basis, the guy on the mound is going to go give us a chance to win the game,\xe2\x80\x9d Manager Alex Cora said. \xe2\x80\x9cThey go six or seven, and we know offensively who we are. It\xe2\x80\x99s a good feeling.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Unless the Yankees reach the World Series this year, the 2010s will be their first decade since the 1910s without at least one A.L. pennant. Their last was in 2009, when they won their 27th title.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt has flown by, man, but it\xe2\x80\x99s been way too long,\xe2\x80\x9d said outfielder Brett Gardner, the longest-tenured Yankee. \xe2\x80\x9cFrom the front office to the ownership, they go out of their way to put the best possible team on the field every year and it\xe2\x80\x99s been a disappointing 10 years.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Yankees very well could reach the World Series, but they might have to start by hosting the wild card game for the third year in a row. The volume of injuries this spring \xe2\x80\x94 Dellin Betances, Didi Gregorius, Aaron Hicks, C.C. Sabathia, Luis Severino \xe2\x80\x94 could be easier to handle because of a forgiving early schedule: The Yankees play 19 of their first 28 games against Baltimore, the White Sox, Detroit, Kansas City and San Francisco.'
b'The Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 lineup will be fearsome, and their bullpen, with Betances, Zach Britton, Adam Ottavino, Chad Green and Aroldis Chapman, will lock down 95 victories or more. Expect a back-and-forth pennant race with Boston all summer.'
b'Can the Tampa Bay Rays elbow into the chase? They won 90 games last season, partly by defying conventional pitching roles with their opener strategy, an innovation that sprang from a logical premise.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe whole goal is, how can we maximize the talent of our players and how can we put them in a position to succeed \xe2\x80\x94 and put us in a position to win as much as possible?\xe2\x80\x9d said Chaim Bloom, the Rays\xe2\x80\x99 senior vice president for baseball operations. \xe2\x80\x9cOur group in the clubhouse has really high expectations, and so do we.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Rays plan to use two openers every five days. They could follow the opener with a so-called \xe2\x80\x9cbulk guy\xe2\x80\x9d (one pitcher who works the bulk of the middle innings) or a parade of relievers. But they need their traditional starters \xe2\x80\x94 Charlie Morton, Tyler Glasnow and the Cy Young Award winner Blake Snell \xe2\x80\x94 to produce.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cReliable starters are the key to letting us do the opener,\xe2\x80\x9d Manager Kevin Cash said. \xe2\x80\x9cNot to put added pressure on them, but if we get good starting pitching, we can be a little bit more aggressive on the other days and mix and match a little bit more.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Fans of the Toronto Blue Jays will start the season pining for third baseman Vladimir Guerrero Jr. and shortstop Bo Bichette, whose fathers combined to play nearly 4,000 games in the majors. Guerrero and Bichette \xe2\x80\x94 Dante\xe2\x80\x99s son \xe2\x80\x94 have played none, but both are top-10 prospects on Baseball America\xe2\x80\x99s list.'
b'Guerrero, 20, was overweight at the start of spring training and then strained an oblique muscle. Bichette, 21, was hitting .417 in exhibition games when he was sent to minor league camp. When the new manager, Charlie Montoyo, can write both names on a lineup card in Toronto, this rebuild will accelerate.'
b'The Baltimore Orioles also have a new manager, Brandon Hyde, and a new general manager, Mike Elias. Hyde came from the Chicago Cubs and Elias from the Astros, so both have seen the payoff from patient roster makeovers. They\xe2\x80\x99ll need a lot of patience in Baltimore, where the Orioles just endured a franchise-record 115 losses. Elias understands the magnitude of the task.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a challenge I\xe2\x80\x99m looking forward to, but we do have titans in our division year in and year out,\xe2\x80\x9d Elias said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99ve got two really good farm systems and front offices in Toronto and Tampa Bay, as well, so all four of our division competitors are mighty. We\xe2\x80\x99re going to have to be very shrewd and draft and sign and develop very well.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Tyler Kepner has been national baseball writer since 2010. He joined The Times in 2000 and covered the Mets for two seasons, then covered the Yankees from 2002 to 2009.  @TylerKepner '

b'By James Wagner'
b'TAMPA, Fla. \xe2\x80\x94 When the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 young slugger Aaron Judge looks up and down the team\xe2\x80\x99s roster, he sees many players like him. There\xe2\x80\x99s the soon-to-be-24-year-old third baseman, Miguel Andujar, who was the runner-up for the American League Rookie of the Year Award last season \xe2\x80\x94 just ahead of a teammate, second baseman Gleyber Torres, 22.'
b'The opening day battery will most likely consist of 25-year-old Luis Severino, the staff ace, on the mound and Gary Sanchez, 26, crouched behind the plate. The heart of the lineup will include Judge, 26, already one of baseball\xe2\x80\x99s most recognizable stars after only two full seasons.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re going to be set for quite a few years to be doing a lot of good things in New York,\xe2\x80\x9d Judge said at the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 spring training base here.'
b'After years of being carried by older players or building rapidly through free agency, the Yankees now have their best core of young players since the days of Derek Jeter, Jorge Posada, Mariano Rivera, Andy Pettitte and Bernie Williams coming up through the team\xe2\x80\x99s system.'
b'And while Judge is understandably optimistic about his team\xe2\x80\x99s odds of competing for a World Series title, it is already fair to wonder how long this core group of players will remain together \xe2\x80\x94 and at what cost.'
b'The Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 decision makers, of course, have already been weighing these questions. The biggest hint the Yankees are already thinking ahead came this month: the four-year, $40 million extension, which could extend to five years, given to Severino. And they have approached other key players, like outfielder Aaron Hicks and relief pitcher Dellin Betances, about possible extensions \xe2\x80\x94 which will weigh much heavier on the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 payroll than their current deals.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s going to be paydays coming down, and we have to prepare for those,\xe2\x80\x9d said Brian Cashman, the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 longtime general manager.'
b'The Yankees did not seriously pursue the star free agent Manny Machado for many reasons: his asking price (he signed for 10 years and $300 million with the San Diego Padres), a desire to spend money in several areas of the roster instead of just a few, and the fact that they already possess a talented third baseman (Andujar) and a huge contract (most of Giancarlo Stanton\xe2\x80\x99s 13-year, $325 million deal).'
b'But one factor was the financial future of their own young standouts. To borrow Cashman\xe2\x80\x99s phrasing, every dollar affects somebody else\xe2\x80\x99s dollar.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cEverything is connected,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cOur payrolls continue to increase, and we\xe2\x80\x99re preparing and have been preparing for that as these players that we think are very special continue their journeys.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It might seem unusual for the Yankees, who are valued by Forbes at $4 billion and had a tradition of chasing the best free agents regardless of price under the former owner George Steinbrenner, to be concerned about the future salaries of their players. But since Steinbrenner\xe2\x80\x99s heyday, baseball has implemented rules that limit spending in the amateur draft or the international market and a luxury tax that teams generally treat as a hard cap.'
b'That is not to say the Yankees couldn\xe2\x80\x99t afford to pursue high-priced free agents and retain their young stars. But Jim Duquette, a former Mets general manager, said the highest luxury tax penalties could be a legitimate deterrent, even for teams as wealthy as the Yankees. (The Red Sox paid $12 million in penalties for their $240 million payroll in 2018 and will be penalized in the 2019 draft, but it helped them win last year\xe2\x80\x99s World Series.)'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cTo be able to handle the luxury tax penalties in these large markets, you have to grow your own players,\xe2\x80\x9d Duquette said. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd if you\xe2\x80\x99re competitive, you\xe2\x80\x99re picking at the low end of the draft. And it\xe2\x80\x99s hard to hit on the Aaron Judges of the world down at the 30s in the first round, where they drafted him.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cSo when you have a core like the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99, this strategy makes sense. They absolutely could afford to pay the tax, but the penalties is what makes it somewhat prohibitive.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Last year was the first time since the luxury tax was put in place in 2003 that the Yankees avoided penalties, having dropped under the $197 million threshold. After being first or second in end-of-year payroll rankings for decades, the Yankees had a $192 million payroll that ranked sixth in baseball, according to Cot\xe2\x80\x99s Baseball Contracts. '
b'The Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 estimated payroll for luxury tax purposes this season is $222 million, over the first tax threshold of $206 million, according to RosterResource.com \xe2\x80\x94 but some relief is on the horizon with hefty contracts, like Jacoby Ellsbury\xe2\x80\x99s, coming off the books in two years and C.C. Sabathia retiring after this season.'
b'But big payouts also loom. Judge and Sanchez, among others, will see big jumps in pay in 2020, when they become eligible for salary arbitration \xe2\x80\x94 hence the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 stated desire to consider multiyear deals for their arbitration-eligible players or pending free-agent players.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cFree agency is tough,\xe2\x80\x9d Duquette said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s hit or miss. If you like your player and know they fit in the organization and play well in New York, then why not try to keep them together?\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In a labor market that seems increasingly tilted toward the clubs, players no longer see free agency as the hallowed grounds they once dreamed about. Since drug testing began, teams are increasingly wary of players\xe2\x80\x99 production after age 30, and one effect has been an increasing number of players signing deals considered team-friendly before reaching free agency.'
b'The Yankees have broached extension talks with Betances and Hicks, both of whom are set to become free agents after this season. Both declined to elaborate on the level of the discussions but said they would be interested in remaining with the Yankees.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s an amazing place with a great future and, of course, it\xe2\x80\x99s something I\xe2\x80\x99d like to be a part of,\xe2\x80\x9d Hicks said.'
b'Both are intriguing cases. Hicks has blossomed in New York after being acquired in a 2015 trade, putting together the best seasons of his career the past two years. He had a career-high 27 home runs and 79 runs batted in despite only playing 137 games last season. But he has dealt with several injuries and will be a free agent at 30.'
b'Drafted and developed by the Yankees, Betances has been one of the best and most durable relievers in baseball. Since 2014, he has a 2.22 E.R.A., better than all but four relief pitchers. What may work against Betances is his age (he will be 32 during the 2020 season) and his workload (his surgically repaired arm has thrown a lot).'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNowadays, middle relievers are getting a lot of love,\xe2\x80\x9d Betances said. This off-season alone, setup men such as Jeurys Familia and Joe Kelly, as well as Betances\xe2\x80\x99 teammates Adam Ottavino and Zack Britton, all scored contracts of at least $25 million.'
b'Another pending free agent the Yankees like: shortstop Didi Gregorius, who has also improved since his trade to New York in 2014. To go along with stout defense, Gregorius has hit .277 and averaged 24 home runs over the past three years. But he will be 30 next season, and his recovery from Tommy John surgery will most likely cut his 2018 season in half.'
b'Judge and Sanchez will make at least the league minimum of $555,000 this season. The Yankees may wait until next winter to begin long-term contract talks with the two, as they did with Severino.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m focused on the season and I haven\xe2\x80\x99t heard anything,\xe2\x80\x9d Judge said last week when asked if the Yankees had approached about his contract future.'
b'Coming off a rough 2018 season, Sanchez would seem unlikely to entertain long-term offers now. But will Judge feel some impulse to cash in on his earning power relatively soon, given that he will not be a free agent until before his age-31 season in 2023? Or will he wait to see how the market changes when the current collective bargaining agreement, which has increasingly drawn the ire of players, expires in December 2021?'
b'In Severino\xe2\x80\x99s case, if the Yankees pick up his $15 million option for 2023, he will be a free agent entering his age-30 season. For the time being, Severino seems perfectly happy with having secured a new deal.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt gives me a lot of confidence,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cEvery time I got to the gym, I\xe2\x80\x99ll be smiling. It\xe2\x80\x99s a lot security for my family.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'2019 National League Preview'
b'Los Angeles has a strong chance to become the first team since the 1923 Yankees to lose two World Series in a row and return for a third try.'
b'By Tyler Kepner'
b'The final out of the last World Series exemplified the Los Angeles Dodgers\xe2\x80\x99 resourcefulness and torment. The year before, they had lost the World Series to the Houston Astros when their star shortstop, Corey Seager, grounded out to end Game 7. Last fall, long after Seager had been lost for the season to injury, his replacement, Manny Machado, struck out to clinch the title for the Boston Red Sox.'
b'The Dodgers simply excel at talent acquisition, loading their roster with more solid players \xe2\x80\x94 and the occasional superstar \xe2\x80\x94 than any other team in the majors. Yet they\xe2\x80\x99ve suffered the indignity of losing the last two World Series on their home field.'
b'Those defeats may obscure just how good the Dodgers really are. They have a strong chance to become the first team since the 1923 Yankees to lose two World Series in a row and return for a third try. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cLast year was probably the most talented team I\xe2\x80\x99ve ever been around, but it didn\xe2\x80\x99t necessarily perform like that on a nightly basis,\xe2\x80\x9d said Andrew Friedman, the Dodgers\xe2\x80\x99 president for baseball operations. \xe2\x80\x9cWe led the N.L. in runs scored, we led the N.L. in fewest runs allowed, but it was just kind of the choppiness of it. For us, a lot of it is how to be as consistent as we can be, bring our talent to the forefront as many nights as we possibly can.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'[M.L.B. Season Preview: Stuffed to Its Seams]'
b'Talent was everywhere on the roster last season, and this one should be no different. By Baseball Prospectus\xe2\x80\x99s calculations, the Dodgers had 18 players with at least two wins above replacement for them last season. No other team had more than 13 such players, and the average team had seven.'
b'That depth allows Manager Dave Roberts to aggressively exploit matchup advantages on offense, and to use his starting pitchers with extreme caution. The Dodgers are the only team that has not used a pitcher for 180 innings in any of the last three seasons.'
b'They will be tempted this season to unleash Walker Buehler, who sparkled last fall in a one-game playoff with Colorado for the National League West title; in Game 7 of the National League Championship Series clincher in Milwaukee; and in the Dodgers\xe2\x80\x99 only victory in the World Series, when he shut out the Red Sox for seven innings.'
b'Buehler, 24, is not the only young homegrown starter who could make a major impact this season. The left-hander Julio Urias, 22, showed in October that he was past the shoulder trouble that cost him nearly two seasons.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s really no pitch limit for Walker, but we\xe2\x80\x99re going to see how his body\xe2\x80\x99s reacting, how he feels and have that open line of communication,\xe2\x80\x9d Roberts said. \xe2\x80\x9cWith Julio, it\xe2\x80\x99s been abbreviated for him the last couple of years, so to say he has a clear runway I don\xe2\x80\x99t think is fair to him. But I do know that he\xe2\x80\x99s going to impact us this year.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Buehler and the veteran Clayton Kershaw have taken it slowly in spring training, but with the Dodgers, it is hard to tell the difference between hurt and injured. They play the long game in Los Angeles, where arriving at full strength in October is all that matters.'
b'The Dodgers lost a few contributors from last year\xe2\x80\x99s team, but added center fielder A.J. Pollock, who was a force for Arizona when healthy; reliever Joe Kelly, whom they plan to use in an expanded setup role that could stretch him to 90 innings; and the grizzled catcher Russell Martin, who had a .338 on-base percentage for Toronto last year. Martin\xe2\x80\x99s .194 batting average did not bother the Dodgers, Friedman said, because he consistently made hard contact.'
b'Martin, 36, has played in five league championship series without ever advancing to the World Series. This could be the year he gets there \xe2\x80\x94 and, with any luck, he just might leap into the arms of closer Kenley Jansen after the final out.'
b'Then again, the Colorado Rockies are conceding nothing in pursuit of their first division title. They signed Daniel Murphy to play first base and gave third baseman Nolan Arenado an eight-year, $260 million contract extension last month. The entire team surprised Arenado by attending the news conference announcing the deal.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI love playing with this group,\xe2\x80\x9d said Arenado, who fought back tears for a moment. \xe2\x80\x9cI really believe we can win. I wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t make this decision if I didn\xe2\x80\x99t believe that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Rockies\xe2\x80\x99 pitching carried them last season, setting club records for most strikeouts, lowest WHIP (walks-plus-hits per inning pitched) and fewest hits allowed in a nonstrike season. Kyle Freeland and German Marquez were rotation stalwarts, and Scott Oberg and Wade Davis (who allowed one run in the regular season after Aug. 9) stabilized a bullpen that will count on a full season from Seunghwan Oh  to offset the loss of Adam Ottavino to the Yankees.'
b'While Colorado kept its cornerstone, the Arizona Diamondbacks shed theirs, trading first baseman Paul Goldschmidt to St. Louis. They have not done much to replace the production of Goldschmidt and Pollock, but with Zack Greinke, Robbie Ray, Zack Godley and Luke Weaver in the rotation, they expect to compete.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re trying to make a shift here,\xe2\x80\x9d Manager Torey Lovullo said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re going to rely on the pitching and defense and we\xe2\x80\x99re going to make up for some offensive losses in other ways.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Reverse-engineer the Diamondbacks and you\xe2\x80\x99d get the San Diego Padres, who added a middle-of-the-order slugger with infielder Manny Machado but have a painfully inexperienced rotation led by Joey Lucchesi.'
b'The Padres will soon let loose a flood of prospects, so it is hard to predict how close they really are to contending. But starter Chris Paddack and shortstop Fernando Tatis Jr. offered tantalizing spring training glimpses of the kind of young, cheap talent that enabled the Padres to afford a 10-year, $300 million contract for Machado.'
b'[A.L. Preview: How Hard Will It Be for the Red Sox to Repeat? Ask the Astros]'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou need to have quality young players that are making major-league minimums, or prearbitration salaries, to enable you to go out and sign some bigger-dollar players, especially in our market, where it\xe2\x80\x99s not unlimited funds,\xe2\x80\x9d General Manager A.J. Preller said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe feel that we\xe2\x80\x99ve built up the talent base to enable us to get into conversations for Machado and some of the big-name free agents.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Speaking of Machado, Preller added: \xe2\x80\x9cYou see it in the energy here at the complex. It raises the level of competition for everybody.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Will it raise the Padres\xe2\x80\x99 place in the standings? They should at least move past the San Francisco Giants, who did not improve an offense that ranked 29th of 30 teams in runs last season, ahead of only Miami. This will be the final season for Giants Manager Bruce Bochy, who is 74 victories shy of 2,000 in his career. He will need a lot of luck to get there.'
b'Every N.L. Central team expects to contend, which makes this the most intriguing division in the majors. The Milwaukee Brewers won it last season \xe2\x80\x94 in a one-game playoff over the Chicago Cubs \xe2\x80\x94 before their joy ride ended in that Game 7 loss to the Dodgers in the N.L.C.S. They know they might have missed their best chance to bring the World Series to Miller Park.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s so difficult to put yourself in that position ever again,\xe2\x80\x9d outfielder Ryan Braun said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe could have a much better team, a much better regular season, but things have to go right to get to a place where you have a Game 7 to get to the World Series \xe2\x80\x94 at home, with the pitcher we want on the mound, after we had just won Game 6 and felt great about our chances. I\xe2\x80\x99m grateful for the opportunity, but it\xe2\x80\x99s not an easy thing to get over.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Brewers hope to get over it by finding an ace or two from a group of rookies who pitched mostly in relief in October: Corbin Burnes, Freddy Peralta and Brandon Woodruff. They will again lean heavily on a strong bullpen and slugging lineup that includes the Most Valuable Player Award winner, Christian Yelich, and a new catcher, Yasmani Grandal, who hit 24 home runs with an .815 on-base plus slugging percentage for the Dodgers last season.'
b'The Dodgers benched Grandal for most of the postseason after he struggled on defense in Game 1 of the N.L.C.S. in Milwaukee. That diminished Grandal\xe2\x80\x99s value but gave the Brewers an opportunity: a one-year, $18.25 million contract that could be a steal.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cLook, guys go into defensive slumps,\xe2\x80\x9d General Manager David Stearns said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe focused on the entirety of what we think he can contribute to our team, and we think it\xe2\x80\x99s meaningful: He\xe2\x80\x99s a very good receiver, he\xe2\x80\x99s a good framer, he handles a pitching staff well, and he can control the running game.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The St. Louis Cardinals went 41-28 last season for Manager Mike Shildt, who replaced the fired Mike Matheny in mid-July. It wasn\xe2\x80\x99t quite enough to lift them to the playoffs, but they should return this year after a three-year absence \xe2\x80\x94 an interminable gap for their regal brand.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a long time, I know,\xe2\x80\x9d said John Mozeliak, the president for baseball operations. \xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re very aware of it.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In Goldschmidt, Marcell Ozuna and Matt Carpenter, the Cardinals have three elite run producers to go with slick defenders like center fielder Harrison Bader, second baseman Kolten Wong and catcher Yadier Molina, who is 36 and just won his ninth Gold Glove. Jack Flaherty could be a breakout rotation star, and Jordan Hicks \xe2\x80\x94 who threw 41 pitches last season that hit 103 miles per hour or higher \xe2\x80\x94 will form an imposing relief duo with the newcomer Andrew Miller.'
b'The Chicago Cubs finally solved Miller in Game 7 of the 2016 World Series in Cleveland, when they completed a comeback and won their first championship since 1908. They have not returned to the World Series, and last season\xe2\x80\x99s wild-card flameout put the clubhouse on notice: Theo Epstein, the president for baseball operations, has vowed \xe2\x80\x9csweeping changes\xe2\x80\x9d if he does not see improvement.'
b'Manager Joe Maddon is working in the final year of his contract, surrounded by new coaches but a roster that still includes more than half of the players who appeared for the Cubs in the World Series. The core deserves one more chance, and another title would be no surprise. But given the strength of the division, neither would third place.'
b'The Cincinnati Reds are the only team in the majors with at least 90 losses in each of the last four seasons. That streak should end now, because the Reds can finally pair their solid offense with a respectable rotation: Luis Castillo, Anthony DeSclafani, Sonny Gray, Tanner Roark and Alex Wood. If they were in the A.L. Central, the Reds might be the favorites. The N.L. version is much different.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ll tell you right now, this is the best division in baseball,\xe2\x80\x9d said Reds reliever Jared Hughes, who has also played for Pittsburgh and Milwaukee. \xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re always incredibly competitive from top to bottom. The goal is to win the division, to win the World Series, and the vibe coming in is that we\xe2\x80\x99re capable of doing that. But there\xe2\x80\x99s no complacency in the N.L. Central.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Pittsburgh Pirates can also dream big because of five exceptional pitchers: starters Jameson Taillon, Chris Archer and Trevor Williams and relievers Felipe Vazquez  and Keone Kela. But their middling offense got few upgrades, and right fielder Gregory Polanco will spend at least the first month recovering from shoulder surgery.'
b'Across Pennsylvania, the Philadelphia Phillies were the clear winners of the off-season \xe2\x80\x94 a meaningless title, of course, but reason enough to consider them the East favorites, despite going 8-20 last September to spoil a promising season.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe had a lot of holes to fill, that was the conclusion,\xe2\x80\x9d said John Middleton, the Phillies\xe2\x80\x99 managing partner. \xe2\x80\x9cWhen you look at the rubble of the last six weeks of the \xe2\x80\x9918 season, we weren\xe2\x80\x99t a player away from being a good team. We were a bunch of players away.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'General Manager Matt Klentak started by acquiring shortstop Jean Segura from Seattle as part of a deal for Carlos Santana, a masterstroke that allowed Rhys Hoskins to move back to first base from left field, where Andrew McCutchen now plays after signing as a free agent. Klentak also signed reliever David Robertson and traded for the game\xe2\x80\x99s best catcher, J.T. Realmuto.'
b'It was a good winter \xe2\x80\x94 and then the Phillies signed Bryce Harper, the former Nationals star, for 13 years and $330 million.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cTo have him in this clubhouse is deflating for the teams in our division, so it\xe2\x80\x99s a great feeling to be on this side,\xe2\x80\x9d starter Jake Arrieta said. \xe2\x80\x9cNot that the teams in our division are scared, by any means, I don\xe2\x80\x99t think that\xe2\x80\x99s the case. But we definitely appreciate the organization signing a guy like Harper and bringing in the pieces we have.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Washington Nationals should still reach the playoffs, with Patrick Corbin joining Max Scherzer and Stephen Strasburg in an overpowering rotation. Their three best hitters \xe2\x80\x94 Anthony Rendon, Juan Soto and Trea Turner \xe2\x80\x94 have somehow never made an All-Star team, but that should change this summer.'
b'The reigning division champions, the prospect-rich Atlanta Braves, added third baseman Josh Donaldson and catcher Brian McCann but otherwise stood pat. That may prove to be wise in time, but for now it leaves them looking vulnerable as pitchers Mike Foltynewicz, A.J. Minter and Mike Soroka start the season on the injured list.'
b'Injuries also struck early for the Mets, who tried to build a deeper roster this winter but will open without infielders Jed Lowrie (knee) and Todd Frazier (oblique). Frazier is 33, Lowrie is 34, and second baseman Robinson Cano is 36. But the under-30 hitters look good, and with Jacob deGrom atop the rotation and Edwin Diaz as the closer, the Mets have a chance.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI truly believe that we can and will win,\xe2\x80\x9d said Brodie Van Wagenen, the new general manager. He has to say that, of course, and his moves have been encouraging \xe2\x80\x94 but probably not enough, given the persistent injury risks on the roster, to change the Mets\xe2\x80\x99 spot in the standings.'
b'The Miami Marlins will be picked for last place in every reasonable forecast. The chief executive, Derek Jeter, got his wish and had the team\xe2\x80\x99s mechanical  home run sculpture moved to the outside of Marlins Park. The display was whimsical and fun, but it would not have been used much, anyway \xe2\x80\x94 no player on this threadbare roster hit more than 13 homers last season.'
b'Tyler Kepner has been national baseball writer since 2010. He joined The Times in 2000 and covered the Mets for two seasons, then covered the Yankees from 2002 to 2009.  @TylerKepner '

b'By Liam Stack'
b'The mayor of San Francisco endorsed a call by civic groups on Monday for Major League Baseball to impose a serious penalty on the chief executive of the San Francisco Giants for a public altercation with his wife that was caught on video this month.'
b'A coalition of women\xe2\x80\x99s groups posted an open letter online Monday that called on Commissioner Rob Manfred to commit to \xe2\x80\x9cfirm and appropriate action in disciplining\xe2\x80\x9d the executive, Larry Baer.'
b'The letter said Mr. Baer \xe2\x80\x9ccannot be allowed to resume his high-profile role without significant consequences and accountability.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The mayor, London N. Breed, said in a statement that she agreed that \xe2\x80\x9cMajor League Baseball needs to send a message that any and all acts of violence against women is unacceptable.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cEvery little girl, every woman should be able to attend a Giants game with a clear sense of the organization\xe2\x80\x99s values,\xe2\x80\x9d Ms. Breed said. \xe2\x80\x9cI share in the call to action by the women who have written the commissioner calling for greater accountability.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The video clip, which was first posted by TMZ Sports, appeared to show Mr. Baer and his wife, Pam, arguing in a public plaza. Ms. Baer was sitting in a chair, and her husband was standing next to her.'
b'Mr. Baer was shown lunging for something in his wife\xe2\x80\x99s hand and then forcefully grabbing her, setting off a struggle that included her falling to the ground and screaming, \xe2\x80\x9cOh my God!\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'After the video of the episode, which occurred on March 1, became public, Mr. and Ms. Baer released statements that day denying that a physical altercation had taken place.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cRegrettably today we had a heated argument in public over a family matter,\xe2\x80\x9d the couple said in a statement. \xe2\x80\x9cWe are deeply embarrassed by the situation and have resolved the issue.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Ms. Baer later released a statement that said she fell accidentally when her chair \xe2\x80\x9cbegan to tip.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cDue to an injury I sustained in my foot three days ago, I lost my balance,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cI did not sustain any injury based on what happened today. Larry and I always have been and still are happily married.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The San Francisco Police Department said Monday that it had investigated the episode and submitted its findings to the office of District Attorney George Gasc\xc3\xb3n. Max Szabo, a spokesman for Mr. Gasc\xc3\xb3n\xe2\x80\x99s office, confirmed that the matter was under review.'
b'A spokesman for Major League Baseball did not immediately respond to a request for comment on Monday. But after the video became public, the league said it was aware of the episode and would "immediately begin to gather the facts.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'A spokesman for the Giants said Monday that Mr. Baer was unavailable for comment. In a statement, the team said it appreciated \xe2\x80\x9cthe sentiments and perspectives expressed\xe2\x80\x9d by the mayor and the civic groups that wrote the open letter.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe have worked closely with the mayor and with many of the women who authored the letter and we deeply respect them and their work in the community,\xe2\x80\x9d the statement said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe take this matter very seriously and we appreciate their concerns. Because it is currently under review, we have no further comment at this time.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The open letter was signed by a half-dozen local groups and several civic leaders, including the president of the San Francisco Commission on the Status of Women, a past president of the organization and a member of the board of directors of Bay Area Rapid Transit.'
b'The letter did not specify how its signatories would like to see Mr. Baer punished, but it did provide a list of suggestions, including a strong public statement from the league and the requirement that Mr. Baer undergo treatment, pay a "substantial financial penalty\xe2\x80\x9d or face a \xe2\x80\x9csignificant suspension\xe2\x80\x9d from activities involving the Giants or the league.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhile Mr. Baer has expressed regret for his behavior, we believe this incident represents more than an embarrassing private quarrel that spilled into public view,\xe2\x80\x9d the letter said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is a test of how seriously Major League Baseball views its responsibility to hold its leaders, as it does with its players, to the highest standards of personal conduct.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'Sports of The Times'
b'By Michael Powell'
b'Just for kicks I listened as Brodie Van Wagenen, the Mets\xe2\x80\x99 general manager, went on about signing the oft-injured 35-year-old second baseman Jed Lowrie and reporters sounded entranced by his jive.'
b'Have you, they asked, thought of bidding on outfielder Bryce Harper or infielder Manny Machado, the two young star free agents who improbably have attracted not much attention this winter?'
b'Van Wagenen, a smooth-talking agent who has become a smooth-talking general manager, smiled genially. \xe2\x80\x9cLet\xe2\x80\x99s be candid here,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cThe outfield is probably not our top priority at this point.\xe2\x80\x9d Jeff McNeil, a career minor leaguer until last July, was going out to the outfield, Van Wagenen said, and \xe2\x80\x9che gives us another really good weapon.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'That the Mets, a little market club hard by Flushing Bay, will play it cheap is a well-established fact. But Van Wagenen speaks the management palaver of choice this parsimonious winter. No one wants to spend money.'
b'The Cubs, the Yankees, the Dodgers, the Giants, the Cardinals, the Braves, the Rangers and the Angels \xe2\x80\x94 all have apparently passed on making a bid for Harper and Machado. Each franchise is owned by a wealthy man (or family) in a wealth-laden sport and all could presumably find a place in the lineup for one of these young stars. And yet for the second season in a row, at a time of the off-season when the best free agents typically would have already signed handsome new contracts, most owners have tucked away their wallets and claimed to need no more talent.'
b'Candidly, Van Wagenen\xe2\x80\x99s reasoning for the Mets\xe2\x80\x99 disinterest is good for a giggle. McNeil is a late-blooming minor league second baseman who in a few nice months in the majors hit three home runs and knocked in 19 runs. He\xe2\x80\x99s a career infielder without a career to speak of.'
b'Harper, by way of no comparison, last season hit 34 home runs, walked 130 times, scored 103 runs and knocked in 100. He is a former rookie of the year and league M.V.P., and he\xe2\x80\x99s all of 26. To suggest you will pass on Harper in hopes that McNeil finds his outfield legs is \xe2\x80\x94 with no offense intended to the McNeil family \xe2\x80\x94 whacked.'
b'Machado and Harper are not the only quality free agents left flapping in the wind. Dallas Keuchel, a good starting pitcher, and Mike Moustakas, a fine third baseman who hit 28 homers last year, have elicited little interest. Craig Kimbrel, that world champion Red Sox closer with 42 saves? Give him a call, he\xe2\x80\x99d probably like to chat. Yasmani Grandal, the best catcher on the market, was expected to command a multiyear contract. He could scrounge up no better than a one-year, $16 million deal with the Milwaukee Brewers.'
b'The Major League Baseball Players Association projects at least 12 of baseball\xe2\x80\x99s 30 teams will start 2019 with a \xe2\x80\x9csubstantially lower payroll\xe2\x80\x9d than 2018. Only four or five are expected to show a significant increase. \xe2\x80\x9cPlayers are well past \xe2\x80\x98concerned,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d Bruce Meyer, the union\xe2\x80\x99s director of collective bargaining, told me. \xe2\x80\x9cAt a time when industry revenues and club valuations are growing for the second straight off-season, an alarming number of clubs are declining to compete for the many talented players.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Major League Baseball officials claim to see no problem. The deputy commissioner, Dan Halem, helped negotiate the last collective bargaining agreement with the players union, and he says labor\xe2\x80\x99s portion of nearly $11 billion in baseball revenues has held steady. His estimate includes players in baseball\xe2\x80\x99s vast minor league system, though, none of whom are in the union and some fair number of whom \xe2\x80\x94 thanks to baseball\xe2\x80\x99s lobbying with Congress \xe2\x80\x94 make less than the minimum wage.'
b'Baseball drove down a road that looked suspiciously like this one between 1985 and 1987 and that ended in a multicar collision with three separate findings that its owners had engaged in illegal collusion to hold down player salaries. The owners paid penalties of $280 million plus interest to the players, and in the 1990s the sport weathered brutal strikes that owed to the residual bitterness.'
b'The former baseball commissioner Fay Vincent, appointed by the owners and no Marxist, was moved at that time to remark to the owners: \xe2\x80\x9cThe single biggest reality you guys have to face up to is collusion. You stole $280 million from the players, and the players are unified to a man around that issue, because you got caught and many of you are still involved.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'I possess no proof the current generation of extremely rich owners have acted as stupidly as their predecessors. For now the flaccid free-agent market is simply \xe2\x80\xa6 odd.'
b'The management of this column readily acknowledges the best of the marooned free agents will not be left to scratch nickels together. Harper seeks a contract north of $300 million for 10 years, and Machado entered free agency entranced by similar sugarplum visions. It is all but assured that one day their descendants will decant a fine Bordeaux and offer a heartfelt Thanksgiving toast to dear old grandpa Bryce and Manny.'
b'And so what? Megawatt talents in many professions profit handsomely, a point lost on a writer from Bleacher Report who loosened an ancient grouse: These free agents are paid \xe2\x80\x9csilly\xe2\x80\x9d money to \xe2\x80\x9cplay a children\xe2\x80\x99s game.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Yes, and playing pretend as a child can lead to movie stardom and an adolescent\xe2\x80\x99s toe-shoed spin can lead to the City Ballet \xe2\x80\x94 provided you have great talent and a work ethic to match.'
b'I digress.'
b'Baseball officials justify the new parsimony with a bow to analytics. We will not sign this or that star because we or some other team once paid out a bad contract. This player became too old, this one too slow, that one too bald, and the thought of a bad contract gives us a stomachache.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cGeneral managers are extremely analytical, and they tend as a group to make the most efficient decisions possible,\xe2\x80\x9d M.L.B.\xe2\x80\x99s Halem told me.'
b'Six years ago, the Angels gave Albert Pujols a 10-year, $254 million contract and that indeed edged to frontiers of nuttiness. He was 32 when he signed it and already past his prime. His once-fabulous eye for balls and strikes slowly deserted him, and a man who once led the league in hitting has not surmounted .250 the past two seasons. With years to go, Pujols\xe2\x80\x99s contract is a mothball special.'
b'Harper and Machado are not Pujols. Each man is entering his golden prime and with a reasonable expectation they will produce at a high level for many seasons to come.'
b'The owners have perhaps snookered a baseball union grown a touch complacent. They regularly manipulate the service time of young players, which works this way: Teams control players for six seasons before they become eligible for free agency. So clubs put thumb to scale and wait to bring up even their very best players until late May or early June. This pushes back the rookie\xe2\x80\x99s service time and saves the club many millions of dollars.'
b'The difference when a player reaches free agency is grand. In 2015, Harper led the league with 42 homers and a .460 on base percentage and was voted the National League\xe2\x80\x99s Most Valuable Player. He earned $2.5 million. Next year, he is likely to pull down close to $30 million.'
b'The union has tended to tolerate service manipulations, figuring its members would recoup any lost money in free agency. Unlike football and basketball, baseball has no salary cap. It also has no floor, though, and now owners are squeezing players on either end like so many papayas in a juicer.'
b'Baseball owners and the abacus boys would do well not to grow self-satisfied. Attendance took a decided drop last year, and the lack of a competitive market has set players in pro sports\xe2\x80\x99 most powerful union to grumbling. Christian Yelich, this year\xe2\x80\x99s National League M.V.P., stopped by The New York Times last week and said players are talking about the strange sloth in the free-agent market.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThey\xe2\x80\x99re two of the best players that we have in the game,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cThe process hasn\xe2\x80\x99t played out.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Last winter, amid another slow free-agent market, Dodgers closer Kenley Jansen tossed a high fastball at the chin of owners. \xe2\x80\x9cMaybe we have to go on strike, to be honest with you,\xe2\x80\x9d he said then.'
b'Perhaps a knockdown pitch is the best way to wake up a team of complacent billionaires.'
b'An earlier version of this article misstated the number of teams in Major League Baseball. There are 30, not 32.'

b'Mets 7, Marlins 3'
b'By Kevin Armstrong'
b'MIAMI \xe2\x80\x94 After he blasted a 95-mile-per-hour fastball more than 400 feet to center field in the ninth inning of the Mets\xe2\x80\x99 7-3 win on Monday night, Pete Alonso was the last player into the clubhouse.'
b'Teammates held Bud Lights in their hands and shouted for Alonso, the rookie first baseman, to hurry. They were ready to celebrate the first home run of his major league career.'
b'He jumped into a laundry cart at Marlins Park, and they wheeled him into the shower. He was doused with beer, barbecue sauce, ketchup, mustard, eggs and relish. He kept his mouth shut the whole time as his eyes started to burn.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThat was really cool,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI didn\xe2\x80\x99t know that was a thing.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Mets and the rest of Major League Baseball have quickly learned that Alonso, 24, is the real thing. After stroking hard-hit doubles against the Nationals over the weekend, Alonso delivered his first long ball when the Mets, with a fresh one-run lead in the ninth inning, needed some insurance. One at-bat earlier, Amed Rosario\xe2\x80\x99s run-scoring single had broken a 3-3 tie.'
b'Though the Mets trailed early and committed two errors, Alonso\xe2\x80\x99s strength on his three-run homer allowed them to finish off the Miami Marlins to improve to 3-1.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThat was a crush job,\xe2\x80\x9d said the Mets\xe2\x80\x99 clubhouse manager, Kevin Kierst, as he bumped fists with Alonso in the hallway afterward.'
b'With the Mets fresh off a series victory over the Washington Nationals, Manager Mickey Callaway urged his players to remain focused. While the Marlins had managed a four-game split with the Colorado Rockies over the weekend, most of Miami\xe2\x80\x99s new lineup lacked name recognition.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThey\xe2\x80\x99re a little bit of the unknown,\xe2\x80\x9d Callaway said.'
b'Caleb Smith, a Miami left-hander, introduced himself by striking out the side in the top of the first. His second baseman, Starlin Castro, followed with a two-run home run to left field in the bottom of the inning.'
b'The Mets made mistakes early. One day after Tomas Nido, the reserve catcher, was charged with a throwing error, the starting catcher Wilson Ramos allowed a passed ball on a third strike to the first batter. Three batters later, Castro delivered his home run.'
b'Left fielder Jeff McNeil also committed his first error of the season, overrunning the ball while chasing a foul pop. He followed that with a strikeout in the top of the sixth. Callaway removed him from the game when he took out starter Steven Matz in the sixth. Matz surrendered three runs, but only one was earned.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe have to take care of business,\xe2\x80\x9d Callaway said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe have to execute the way we know we can.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Alonso did just that in the ninth. Closer Edwin Diaz then collected three strikeouts in the bottom of the inning to preserve the win.'
b'Alonso was the person teammates waited for in the clubhouse, though.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s excitement there in this room,\xe2\x80\x9d Callaway said. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd there should be for a long time.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'Advertisement'
b'Supported by'
b'By Claire Smith'
b'As an African-American woman who has written about baseball for decades, the question I am most asked about my career choice is: \xe2\x80\x9cWhy?\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The answer is really as succinct as the question: Jackie Robinson.'
b'He was the man who, born 100 years ago, successfully took on the challenge of transforming baseball and, by extension, the entire country by becoming the first African-American to play in the modern era. By stepping onto a major league diamond as a Brooklyn Dodger 72 years ago, he allowed a sport that thought of itself as the national pastime to finally be just that.'
b'What Robinson did, what he stood for, what he conveyed not only to black America, but to all of America, has resonated with me for as long as I can remember, and nothing else played as big a role in fueling my desire to be a writer, a recorder of history, a storyteller.'
b'[On Jackie Robinson\xe2\x80\x99s 100th Birthday, 100 Photos of an Icon]'
b'[George Vecsey: How Jackie Robinson Changed the Game]'
b'I did not personally feel the tectonic shift that took place on April 15, 1947, when Robinson made his Dodgers debut. Alas, I did not see Robinson\xe2\x80\x99s first game, nor even his last, a decade later. I came of age years after he played his final game for Brooklyn.'
b'But I wish I could say, with a straight face, that I actually heard Robinson\xe2\x80\x99s name while still in the womb. He was, in fact, still on the Dodgers then. And yes, my mother was that big a fan of Robinson and the Dodgers and surely was urging him on out loud while she was pregnant with me. Indeed, tales of the lengths to which she and other family members went in order to listen to Dodgers games on the radio were among my favorite bedtime stories as a child.'
b'Back then, I sensed the reverence that was still reserved for Robinson in my household, even though he had by then retired. After all, what African-Americans who were adults in the middle of the last century, as my mother and father were, could resist being drawn to him? In an era of ongoing repression, African-Americans wanted heroes of their own. So, as a child, you would hear of the exploits of Joe Louis, Jesse Owens, Paul Robeson. And Jackie Robinson.'
b'It did help that, by the time I reached third grade, I had something more than an oral history to reference when it came to worshiping him. And that\xe2\x80\x99s because the nuns at St. James Elementary School in Elkins Park, Pa., decided one day to break the rote and routine of our structured school life and spirit all of us to a first-floor sanctuary in the school. They did so in order to show us a film, a grainy, 76-minute biopic entitled \xe2\x80\x9cThe Jackie Robinson Story.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The movie was pure Hollywood, and never destined to be an epic. Still, for this one child, the black-and-white rendering brought color and depth to the Robinson story. And playing opposite the great Ruby Dee (who portrayed Rachel Robinson in the movie) was none other than Jackie Robinson, portraying himself.'
b'All these years later, I can still remember how intensely I watched Robinson on the screen, giving life to his own story. There, in the sanctuary, I could see the man as well as the athlete, could hear his voice, could sense that sprinkled in among all the Tinsel Town touches were more than a few hints of truth.'
b'When Jackie Robinson spoke in the movie, it was as if he were speaking to me. And that mattered. It was the early 1960s and as the lone African-American child sitting in the pews that afternoon, and in my classroom every single day, I didn\xe2\x80\x99t often see anyone on the big screen or on television who looked like Mom and Dad, or my relatives. In this one modest movie, Dee and Robinson came as close to mirroring us as anything I\xe2\x80\x99d ever seen before.'
b'It would, of course, take years for me to fully realize what Hollywood dared not show at the time. It would take years of growth to realize that my worst day could never possibly compare to the things Jackie Robinson went through.'
b'And yet, by Jackie Robinson entering my life the way he did, by way of my mother\xe2\x80\x99s tales and that memorable day watching him in a movie bearing his name, I began to understand what the battle for civil rights \xe2\x80\x94 one that my own parents and grandparents were fighting valiantly \xe2\x80\x94 was all about.'
b'In the decades that followed, as I pursued the career I had chosen, I was able to get to know Rachel Robinson, an outright national treasure who was and is as integral to the legend of No. 42 as Jackie himself. As well, I got to meet their daughter, Sharon, who, with her philanthropic efforts, has made her own valuable impact in keeping the Jackie Robinson story alive.'
b'It is, at heart, the story of the man who, at his best and bravest, showed us all how to be strong enough not to fight back but rather to fight on and on and on, even now on the 100th anniversary of his birth. And I\xe2\x80\x99m proud, in my own small way, to have helped tell it.'
b'Claire Smith, a former sports columnist for The New York Times, is a news editor for ESPN. She was the first woman to win J.G. Taylor Spink Award for meritorious contributions to baseball writing.'

b'By Victor Mather'
b'In this era of new and complex baseball statistics, a venerable one still pops up frequently in conversations among even the geekiest of stat-heads: batting average.'
b'It\xe2\x80\x99s one of the easiest to understand: .300 is good.; .200 is the Mendoza line \xe2\x80\x94 you don\xe2\x80\x99t want to drop below that. If you want to praise a player, you\xe2\x80\x99re likely to get more mileage with most fans by saying, \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s hitting .280\xe2\x80\x9d than by citing his WAR or BABIP.'
b'But as even some statistical Neanderthals know, batting average is a seriously flawed measure of offensive performance. It is great for evaluating a player\xe2\x80\x99s ability to hit singles, but batters get no credit for their power, speed or batting eye.'
b'What if there were a statistic as easy to understand as batting average that accounted for the things that batting average does not?'
b'Well, there is: It\xe2\x80\x99s called secondary average, and it was invented by the influential statistician Bill James in the 1970s. Unlike many of James\xe2\x80\x99s innovations, it has not caught on heavily with fans \xe2\x80\x94 you can\xe2\x80\x99t find it in most stats websites or on the back of baseball cards.'
b'But secondary average is a useful tool to quickly evaluate a player\xe2\x80\x99s offense, identifying players who are underrated or overrated by batting average.'
b'Secondary average looks and works a lot like batting average does. But rather than focusing on hit totals, it adds up the batter\xe2\x80\x99s other offensive skills \xe2\x80\x94 extra bases, walks and stolen bases \xe2\x80\x94 and then divides by at-bats. (Some formulas for secondary average also include hit-by-pitch, and others reduce the total for being caught stealing. We\xe2\x80\x99re using the simplest formula here.)'
b'Let\xe2\x80\x99s use Dee Gordon of the Seattle Mariners as an example. He had a .268 batting average last season, 20 points higher than the league average (.248). But his secondary average was a mere .151 because he had very few extra-base hits and even fewer walks.'
b'Here\xe2\x80\x99s how it works:'

b'JOHN FROSCHAUER'
b'ASSOCIATED PRESS'
b'You don\xe2\x80\x99t really have to learn a new scale to understand secondary average. It looks and works a lot like batting average: .300 is good, and .200 is not. Major leaguers collectively had a .248 batting average last season, and their overall secondary average was .271.'
b'One difference is that the spectrum is much wider. While almost every player falls into the .200s or .300s in batting average, there are plenty of regular major leaguers with secondary averages in the .100s, and others over .400 or even .500.'
b'Here are the players who had the largest increase from their traditional batting average to their secondary average last season:'
b'Of the players who qualified for the batting title last season, the leader in secondary average was Mike Trout of the Los Angeles Angels, with an eye-opening .626. Trout had a solid .312 batting average, but that hardly summed up his offense. He had a healthy number of extra-base hits, including 39 home runs; led the league in walks with 122; and stole 24 bases. Jose Ramirez of Cleveland (.524), and Mookie Betts of Boston (.508) were just behind him at the top of the secondary average list.'
b'Some historical context makes Trout\xe2\x80\x99s season look even more impressive: Babe Ruth\xe2\x80\x99s career secondary average was .608; Barry Bonds\xe2\x80\x99s was .621.'
b'At the other end, it reveals how some players, like Gordon, bring little beyond an ability to hit singles:'
b'The Chicago White Sox\xe2\x80\x99 Jon Jay, who spent last season with Kansas City and Arizona, had only three home runs, drew only 33 walks and stole four bases. These rather anemic extra contributions led to a sad .150 secondary average \xe2\x80\x94 compared with a .268 batting average \xe2\x80\x94 one point behind Gordon. Miguel Rojas of Miami was at .156.'
b'Unsurprisingly, Bryce Harper\xe2\x80\x99s .249 batting average from last season sells his contributions short. He hit 34 home runs and led the majors with 130 walks, for a secondary average of .507. Mention that the next time someone dismisses him as \xe2\x80\x9cjust a .250 hitter.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'A less heralded example is Joey Gallo of Texas. His .206 batting average might make it seem as if he is ready for a demotion to Class AAA Nashville. But his 40 home runs, and his doubles (24) and walks (74) gave him a robust secondary average of .446, keeping his slot in the Rangers\xe2\x80\x99 outfield secure.'
b'While the Phillies landed one high-secondary-average player in Harper this off-season, the rest of their winter haul didn\xe2\x80\x99t necessarily follow that trend. Philadelphia also traded with the Mariners for Jean Segura, whose .304 batting average seemed to plant him among the game\xe2\x80\x99s best shortstops. But secondary average reveals it to be something of an empty .304: Although Segura hit 29 doubles and 10 home runs, his walk total was a shaky 32. That adds up to a secondary average of .200.'
b'Mario Mendoza (career batting average .215, career secondary average .095) might approve.'

b'Extra Bases'
b'By Tyler Kepner'
b'Based on the way they have started this season, Collin McHugh, C.C. Sabathia and Trevor Williams should be in high demand for interviews. The three starting pitchers \xe2\x80\x94 McHugh for the Houston Astros, Sabathia for the Yankees and Williams for the Pittsburgh Pirates \xe2\x80\x94 had combined to make nine starts before Friday\xe2\x80\x99s games, with a 2.08 E.R.A.'
b'But McHugh, Sabathia and Williams enjoy asking questions, too. All three pitchers double as podcasters \xe2\x80\x94 a natural hobby, perhaps, for players who perform only once every five games.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe have way more time,\xe2\x80\x9d Sabathia said on Wednesday after recording his latest episode with the bullpen coach Mike Harkey. \xe2\x80\x9cPlenty of time to do stuff like that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Sabathia and his co-host, Ryan Ruocco, a broadcaster for ESPN and the YES Network, release a new episode of \xe2\x80\x9cR2C2 Is Uninterrupted\xe2\x80\x9d every Thursday, speaking mostly with baseball, football and basketball players. Sabathia said his dream guest was the entertainer Will Smith, but lately he has settled for teammates like Gleyber Torres, J.A. Happ and James Paxton.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s less of an interview, I feel like, just more of a conversation,\xe2\x80\x9d said Sabathia, who is also working for ESPN in his final year as a player. \xe2\x80\x9cYou get people to relax a little more, you get better stories. People are just more comfortable in that setting.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'McHugh once kept a blog but transitioned to a new medium after listening to podcasts by the N.B.A. veteran JJ Redick of the Philadelphia 76ers, who regularly interviews players for a broadcast hosted by The Ringer.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m not a huge basketball fan, but it was just the idea of hearing league insiders talk about things that maybe you\xe2\x80\x99ve thought about but never were really able to know if it was true or put a real voice to it,\xe2\x80\x9d McHugh said. \xe2\x80\x9cTo hear two basketball players talking about what life on the road is like, what traveling is like, all these different things and just getting to hear their voices, that made basketball more interesting to me.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAnd I started thinking about: What is baseball missing? We\xe2\x80\x99re missing this fan/human interaction. Everything\xe2\x80\x99s getting really disconnected in terms of analytics, the fans and the players, there\xe2\x80\x99s more of a gap than there\xe2\x80\x99s ever been before. So what would be a way to bridge that?\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'McHugh is the lone host of \xe2\x80\x9cThe Twelve Six,\xe2\x80\x9d named for the curveball, which breaks from 12 to 6 on a clock face. McHugh \xe2\x80\x94 whose recent episode with Washington Nationals closer Sean Doolittle was especially compelling \xe2\x80\x94 combines the probing questions of a good reporter with the credibility of a fellow major leaguer, in a casual, one-on-one setting.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAs soon as you get more than one camera on a person, the honesty curve just goes way down, because guys are very reticent to say things that might be perceived the wrong way,\xe2\x80\x9d McHugh said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut when it\xe2\x80\x99s just two dudes sitting around, having a bottle of wine or a couple of beers and just talking, you\xe2\x80\x99re way more likely to get more honest answers \xe2\x80\x94 which I think is a treasure, and a lot of capital in this day and age.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'As for Williams, he and his co-host, Pirates reliever Steven Brault, have recorded most of their episodes during the off-season and thrive on topics far afield: favorite candy bars, Christmas songs, Pixar movies and so on.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cOurs is more the fun side of players, reminding fans that we\xe2\x80\x99re human beings, we\xe2\x80\x99re not just baseball players and all we think about is baseball,\xe2\x80\x9d Williams said. \xe2\x80\x9cWhen we have guests on \xe2\x80\x94 other teammates or whoever \xe2\x80\x94 we first ask, \xe2\x80\x98What are you passionate about, what\xe2\x80\x99s a hobby that you have that isn\xe2\x80\x99t baseball?\xe2\x80\x99 So if it\xe2\x80\x99s cooking: What\xe2\x80\x99s your favorite food? If it\xe2\x80\x99s sandwiches: What\xe2\x80\x99s your favorite sandwich? Everyone has an opinion on their favorite things.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Williams, 26, has helped lead a Pirates rotation that entered Friday\xe2\x80\x99s games with a 2.09 E.R.A., easily the best in the National League. Like the Hall of Fame pitchers Tom Seaver and Don Sutton, who each started broadcasting while they were still playing, to prepare for life after baseball, Williams enjoys his current profession while planning for his next.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cEvery time I\xe2\x80\x99m in an interview, every time I\xe2\x80\x99m in front of a TV camera, I feel like I\xe2\x80\x99m trying out for my next job,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99d love to be on TV, I\xe2\x80\x99d love to do color commentary. But right now I\xe2\x80\x99m a baseball player, and I\xe2\x80\x99d like to do that for as long as I can.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Everyone knew why Brad Keller drilled Tim Anderson with a fastball to the hip on Wednesday afternoon in Chicago. Anderson, the White Sox\xe2\x80\x99 shortstop, had earlier homered off Keller, the Kansas City Royals\xe2\x80\x99 pitcher, and flung his bat triumphantly toward his dugout as the ball sailed to the seats. Keller delivered his displeasure at 92 miles per hour, well below the head.'
b'That should have been the end of it; Anderson did not charge the mound, and Keller\xe2\x80\x99s message only served to put another runner on base for the White Sox. But the benches cleared and the umpire Joe West ejected four people, including Keller and Anderson, who were both suspended by Major League Baseball on Friday.'
b'Keller was given a five-game suspension and Anderson one, for using racially charged language directed at Keller in the immediate aftermath. (Keller is white and Anderson is black.) But the incident seemed to undercut M.L.B.\xe2\x80\x99s #LetTheKidsPlay advertising campaign, which is meant to encourage the kind of self-expression that provoked the Royals to retaliate.'
b'Most players do not punctuate home runs with bat flips. But if some choose to celebrate that way, Anderson said, it should be a good thing. Anderson, 25, said younger players and fans can relate.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re in a new generation, a new wave, and this is the new school,\xe2\x80\x9d he said in an interview Thursday morning. \xe2\x80\x9cI get the old-school vibe, but this is the new school. We\xe2\x80\x99re going to try and switch the vibe. The kids look up to us, and if we go out and play with a lot of energy and play to have fun, I think the kids would enjoy the game a lot more.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Anderson, who was hitting .422 through Thursday, said his reaction to the home run had nothing to do with the Royals. He was simply trying to inspire his team, which is built around young players like Eloy Jimenez and Yoan Moncada. He cited an N.B.A. player, Russell Westbrook of the Oklahoma City Thunder, as a model for how to act while in uniform.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI want to be the Westbrook of baseball,\xe2\x80\x9d Anderson said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe goes out and plays with a high level every night and couldn\xe2\x80\x99t care less what anybody else has to say. It\xe2\x80\x99s really just bringing that energy and that positive vibe to the squad. That\xe2\x80\x99s what I like to do, and I\xe2\x80\x99m going to continue to do it. I\xe2\x80\x99m not going to change.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Anderson has a charity \xe2\x80\x94 Anderson\xe2\x80\x99s League of Leaders \xe2\x80\x94 that promotes community service and youth outreach in Chicago and his hometown, Tuscaloosa, Ala. Inspired by the death of his best friend, Branden Moss, to gun violence in 2017, Anderson tries to show leadership on the field by staying true to himself, even at the cost of a fastball to the hip.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI like to have fun,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, \xe2\x80\x9cand I\xe2\x80\x99m not going to let anybody stop that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'When the Cincinnati Reds last won the World Series, in 1990, they clinched the title on a foul popout to first base by Carney Lansford of the Oakland Athletics. Lansford was a former batting champion, but hitting a popout was no reason to be ashamed. For most players, it is routine.'
b'Joey Votto, of course, is not like most players. Votto, the Reds\xe2\x80\x99 first baseman, popped out to first base on Wednesday for the very first time in his career \xe2\x80\x94 in his 6,829th plate appearance. That leaves the Arizona Diamondbacks\xe2\x80\x99 Alex Avila as the current leader in most career plate appearances without popping out to first, at a mere 3,285 through Thursday.'
b'Votto, a six-time All-Star, was hitting just .228 after the popout, which came in Los Angeles against the Dodgers\xe2\x80\x99 Pedro Baez. C. Trent Rosecrans, the Reds\xe2\x80\x99 beat writer for The Athletic, waited for Votto for 56 minutes after the game.'
b'Votto was not simply lingering in the lunchroom. To Votto, the popout was a sign that his technique was badly off.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s a reason I just spent an hour hitting after a day game after a night game,\xe2\x80\x9d Votto said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s not good. It\xe2\x80\x99s definitely not a good thing. I rarely do that. That\xe2\x80\x99s why when I saw it, I was like, \xe2\x80\x98Ugh, I\xe2\x80\x99ve got a lot of work to do.\xe2\x80\x99 But I\xe2\x80\x99m going to put in the work. I\xe2\x80\x99m confident it\xe2\x80\x99s going to come.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'One major leaguer actually hits into fewer pop-ups than Votto. According to MLB.com, Votto has popped up in 1.3 percent of his career plate appearances (almost always to the left of second base). Impressive, but not the best. Among hitters with at least 1,000 career trips to the plate, the Milwaukee Brewers\xe2\x80\x99 Christian Yelich, at 1.2 percent, is the least likely to pop out.'
b'For Votto, at least, the post-pop-out-to-first phase of his career could not have started any better. After his long practice session on Wednesday, he started Thursday\xe2\x80\x99s game in San Diego with a leadoff home run.'
