b'Sports of The Times'
b'By Michael Powell'
b'Can we talk starting pitchers or, more to the point, their ritual sacrifice on the altar of Major League Baseball analytics?'
b'I put this question to Leo Mazzone, the former pitching coach for the Atlanta Braves and the custodian of one of baseball\xe2\x80\x99s greatest rotations of starting pitchers: Greg Maddux, John Smoltz and Tom Glavine, Hall of Famers all.'
b'The 2018 playoffs and World Series offered a parade of twitchy managers yanking their starting pitchers after four innings, summoning a parade of faceless relievers to throw one mind-numbing fastball after another for fractions of an inning.'
b'This is spectacular for the radar gun industry, but is it watchable and good baseball?'
b'I heard Mazzone snorting on the other end of the phone line, no, no and no. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is an embarrassment and insults the intelligence,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cThey are abusing pitchers and calling it smart.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Mazzone imparted this gospel to his pitchers: Trying to heave balls as fast as you can is for muscle-beach dolts. A good pitcher throws at 85 to 90 percent of effort and makes the pitch move and hit its location. Varies speeds, too. As for the notion a pitcher can last but five or six innings before batters grow wise and clobber him?'
b'Please.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cA high school coach asked me, \xe2\x80\x98Leo what do you think of analytics showing that pitchers struggle the third time through a lineup?\xe2\x80\x99 I\xe2\x80\x99ll tell you want that is, that\xe2\x80\x99s the manager covering his (you know what),\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'The equation guys who run most major league teams bow to holy verities: No starting pitcher should throw more than 100 pitches. Some starters should not throw as many as 70. To admire the number of wins a pitcher accumulates or to encourage him to toss a complete game is to expose yourself as a Paleolithic hunter-gatherer. Pitching is all about WHIP and FIP (I\xe2\x80\x99d explain the definitions, but then our heads would hurt) and a conga line of relief pitchers.'
b'Look, on a good day I don\xe2\x80\x99t drag my knuckles along the sidewalks of Flatbush, Brooklyn. I dig sabermetrics and back in the day treated Bill James annuals as religious text. I keep a three-foot-high stack of the analytics-obsessed Baseball Prospectus at home. But at risk of registering as a get-off-my-lawn crank: So much of the wisdom about pitchers is dubious.'
b'I set to thinking about this after watching my Mets spend much of November and December in a modestly lunatic attempt to trade Noah Syndergaard, one of the National League\xe2\x80\x99s best starting pitchers. They appear to have failed at this self-mutilation. Now that they have retained two true aces \xe2\x80\x94 Syndergaard and Jacob deGrom, the Cy Young Award winner \xe2\x80\x94 why not stretch them out and push them to go deeper into games? What is the point in allowing an ace to pitch six innings before turning the ball over to a committee of anonymous relievers?'
b'Game 4 of the 2018 World Series presented something of a nadir when Los Angeles Dodgers Manager Dave Roberts, a bright fellow no doubt, pulled his starting pitcher after he had yielded a single hit through six and a third innings and was ahead, 4-0. The Dodgers ended up marching six relievers into that game, lost, 9-6, and exited the World Series the next day.'
b'Mazzone pulled out a few of his remaining hairs.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe greatest teacher for a pitcher is starts,\xe2\x80\x9d he says. \xe2\x80\x9cPitch and pitch and pitch. Let a pitcher find himself.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe problem is that so many pitching coaches and managers are yes-men and don\xe2\x80\x99t want to challenge their front offices.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'There\xe2\x80\x99s a sizable mound of statistical evidence to back such assertions. At risk of giving the quadratic dudes a seizure, I turned to Baseball Reference and selected 40 pitchers from the past half-century, men who ran the gamut from solid to superb. These are the sort of pitchers you\xe2\x80\x99d expect to see in the postseason, and my list included Bobby Ojeda, Mike Torrez, Steve Avery, Tom Browning, Tom Seaver, Steve Carlton, Ferguson Jenkins and Mazzone\xe2\x80\x99s troika of Hall of Famers. I examined their performances across games, from beginning to end.'
b'For most good pitchers, their worst inning was the first. Once they found a rhythm and once pitches began to crackle, they became progressively more difficult to hit. Tom Seaver\xe2\x80\x99s career earned run average in the first inning was 3.75. His E.R.A. for the last three innings of a game, that dreaded third and fourth time through the batting order, stood at 2.75.'
b'So current analytic wisdom does a headstand.'
b'(By way of insane outlier, Seaver won 25 games in 1969 and helped pitch the Miracle Mets to a World Series championship. He pitched the ninth inning 17 times that season and surrendered not a single run.)'
b'This is a familiar pattern. Mike Mussina gave up fewer runs on average in the seventh, eighth and ninth innings than he did in the first three. He was at his best in the ninth inning. The best inning for Ron Darling and David Wells was the eighth. (Requisite caveat: By definition, these pitchers were having a good outing if they made it to the late innings.)'
b'If you hoped to beat Dodgers pitcher Fernando Valenzuela, you were advised to start hacking early. He had a career E.R.A. of 4.25 in the first inning. When Valenzuela was still pitching in the ninth inning, and he got there roughly 127 times in his career, his E.R.A. was 2.19.'
b'Luis Tiant, the Red Sox and Cleveland ace, was nearly as tough. He pitched just over 206 times in the ninth inning and had an E.R.A. of 2.40.'
b'Greg Maddux had a 3.23 E.R.A. in his first three innings and a 2.86 from the seventh inning through the ninth. And while he possessed a good fastball, it was not a three-digit express train. One spring training in the mid-1990s, Maddux, who in a 23-year career piled up 355 fairly meaningful wins, asked to speak with the team\xe2\x80\x99s young pitchers.'
b'Mazzone nodded. Sure thing, Mad Dog, whatever you want. The coach lined up the young guys and Maddux walked over.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou know why I am a millionaire? Because I can put my fastball wherever I want to,\xe2\x80\x9d Maddux told them. \xe2\x80\x9cDo you know why I own beachfront property in L.A.? Because I can change speeds. O.K., questions?\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Mazzone was not enraptured by pitch counts. He would not push pitchers to stupid extremes, but he refused to hew to limits without basis in medical fact. He had pitchers run and throw every day in between starts, and they had remarkably few injuries. In one three-year stretch, his pitchers missed a single start.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe kept track of pitches and I had a clicker,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, \xe2\x80\x9cbut if Tommy Glavine gets a pop-up on a changeup, hell, I\xe2\x80\x99m not counting that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He recalled a Braves vice president by the name of Henry Aaron who offered advice about the dangers of radar gun intoxication. \xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t worry about pure speed,\xe2\x80\x9d Aaron said. \xe2\x80\x9cYou can run a jet airliner through the strike zone, and I will figure out how to rope it down the line. Locate a ball that moves at my knees, and I\xe2\x80\x99m out.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'All of which brings me back to the Mets, a team I\xe2\x80\x99ve followed for many, often hapless, decades. Their manager, Mickey Callaway, sounds as enamored of pitch counts as his peers are. All of this seeps into the brainpans of young pitchers who labor under the impression that five or six innings constitute a day\xe2\x80\x99s work.'
b'Syndergaard is a fine pitcher and susceptible to the idiocies of the age. A year ago he pumped iron in the off-season in hopes of throwing even harder than 100 miles per hour, and that season he blew a muscle in his side. He appears to accept the notion that pitching through the seventh inning lies beyond the limit of human exertion, and last season he posted a 7.88 E.R.A. in that inning.'
b'His rotation mates are no different. On the rare occasions they pitched into the seventh inning, Zack Wheeler and Steven Matz posted calamitous E.R.A.s of 5.65 and 6.35.'

b'Glavine looked at him, smiled thinly and replied, \xe2\x80\x9cMazz, we were going to have a fight on that mound.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'By David Waldstein'
b'BOSTON \xe2\x80\x94 The cleats on Steve Pearce\xe2\x80\x99s gray New Balance model 4040v4 baseball shoe are about 1.27 centimeters long. It is roughly that distance by which the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 season ended last year in the Bronx.'
b'That fraction of an inch is what ultimately separated the Red Sox from the Yankees in their divisional playoff series, which Boston won in four games. If Pearce had not anchored the toe of his right foot to first base, as he did, if the plastic cleats on the bottom of his shoe were a tiny bit shorter, or if the throw to him was slightly more off target, the Yankees might have won Game 4 and carried a plane-load of momentum into a do-or-die Game 5 at Fenway Park, potentially changing the course of the postseason.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a Game 5 and anything can happen at that point,\xe2\x80\x9d Andrew Benintendi, the Red Sox left fielder, said in Boston last week. \xe2\x80\x9cLuckily, we\xe2\x80\x99ll never find out.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'On Tuesday night, in the Bronx, Pearce and the rest of the Red Sox will meet up with the Yankees for the first time since that crucial play, although the encounter will come with both teams stumbling through the early part of the 2019 season.'
b'The Red Sox, baseball\xe2\x80\x99s defending champions, are just 6-11 after Monday\xe2\x80\x99s Patriots\xe2\x80\x99 Day loss to Baltimore at Fenway. The Yankees, meanwhile, are just 6-9 and have lost three straight series at home.'
b'But back on Oct. 9, 2018, the Yankees and Red Sox were two of the best teams in baseball and were sweating out a tense, and chaotic, bottom of the ninth in Game 4 of an American League division series, with Boston securing the final out only when part of Pearce\xe2\x80\x99s right shoe stuck \xe2\x80\x94 just barely \xe2\x80\x94 to the base while he snared a throw from third baseman Eduardo Nunez in the webbing of his glove.'
b'For an instant, time froze. Pearce was splayed on the dirt with the ball still in his glove, his body\xe2\x80\x99s momentum having tugged his foot off the base. The Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 Gleyber Torres, who had raced desperately to first after hitting a weak grounder to Nunez, planted his left foot on the bag just as Pearce fell. On the other side of the diamond, the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 Adeiny Hechavarria, the tying run, had turned third base and was headed for home.'
b'Had this been the previous century, or the early part of this one, when fortune almost always favored the Yankees over the Red Sox, perhaps Pearce\xe2\x80\x99s foot would have disconnected prematurely from first base, or the throw would have skidded away. b'\xe2\x80\x9cOh yeah,\xe2\x80\x9d said Aaron Boone, the Yankees manager, who once authored a classic Yankees-Red Sox ending of his own with a walkoff home run against Boston in Game 7 of the 2003 American League Championship Series. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s the perfect game-of-inches play in such a big spot.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x99'
b'But this historic rivalry has been turned on its head over the last 15 years and when first-base umpire Fieldin Culbreth pumped his fist to signal that Torres was out, the Red Sox were on their way to the A.L.C.S. and, from there, to their fourth World Series title in this century. b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m not the tallest first baseman in the world,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x99 Pearce acknowledged last week as he recalled the ending to Game 4. \xe2\x80\x9cI have to use every bit of Steve Pearce I can find to get to the baseball. I was anchored to the bag and nothing \xe2\x80\x94 nothing \xe2\x80\x94 was going to pull me off until I caught the ball.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Pearce, who turned 36 over the weekend and has played for seven teams over the course of a 13-year major league career, said he does not do yoga. But he does stretch a lot and demonstrated enough agility that night to catch the ball and clamp his foot to the base, if only for an instant.'
b'When Culbrin made the out call, Red Sox players charged out of the dugout to celebrate. But Boone, with nothing more to lose, requested a replay review, hoping that Pearce\xe2\x80\x99s foot had indeed come off the bag before he caught the ball.'

b'By Jay Schreiber'
b'On July 20, 1969, men walked on the moon in what became the centerpiece of one of the more indelible years in American history.'
b'That same day, 50 years ago, the New York Mets split a doubleheader with the Montreal Expos. You could say, so what? But the Mets, until then a baseball punch line, had suddenly become a team to reckon with in the eighth year of their existence. The two games against the Expos gave them a 53-39 record, which meant they were a big, fat 14 games over .500. Considering everything that had come before for the Mets \xe2\x80\x94 the initial buffoonery, the occasional lunacy, the lopsided losing records \xe2\x80\x94 it seemed that they, too, were now defying gravity.'
b'A month later, on the same weekend as the Woodstock music festival, the Mets really took flight. They swept four games from the San Diego Padres and began a surge that carried them into first place in September and all the way to the World Series in October \xe2\x80\x94 which they proceeded to win, in five games, against the heavily favored Baltimore Orioles.'
b'When it was over, after the Mets had been drenched in ticker tape in a parade up Broadway \xe2\x80\x94 a feat that had been unimaginable when the season started \xe2\x80\x94 it took a while for people to regain their senses.'
b'Just how had this happened? Yes, the Mets had excellent pitching, solid defense at key positions and some very good young players, but their lineup was hardly overwhelming. And yet, that didn\xe2\x80\x99t matter in the regular season, when the Mets won a whopping 100 games and, in the process, beat out a Chicago Cubs team that played three future Hall of Famers every day.'
b'Nor did it matter in the National League Championship Series, when the Mets swept an Atlanta Braves club led by Henry Aaron, one of the best players in the sport\xe2\x80\x99s history. Or in the World Series, when the Mets went up against a mighty Orioles team anchored by the two Robinsons, Frank and Brooks. The Orioles, winners of 109 games in the regular season, seemed unbeatable until the Mets quickly proved otherwise.'
b'Making this all the more remarkable is that the 1969 Mets did not represent the beginning of a dynasty. In the seasons that followed, the Mets won considerably fewer games and while they did make it back to the World Series in 1973, they did so almost by accident, having finished the regular season with a thoroughly mediocre 82-79 record.'
b'But none of that diminishes what occurred in 1969. Here was a group of players who stumbled all over the place in 1962, with fans who embraced them almost in defiance. A team that slowly improved in the years that followed, but only slowly. And yet a team that proceeded to figure it all out for one intensely memorable season.'
b'It is not easy to explain, but 50 years later, it is worth revisiting. Time has taken its toll on this team; a half-dozen players who had significant roles have died, and others, including Tom Seaver, are now struggling with serious health issues. But what endures through all the bittersweetness is what they accomplished together. From the depths of the standings they soared right into space.'
b'NEXT UP: 1962: The Bumbling Beginning'

White. Additional material in this section was written by Jay Schreiber. Research was provided by Fred Bierman, Elena Gustines, Wayne Kamidoi, Dolores Morrison and Joe Ward.'

b'Baseball\xe2\x80\x99s Hall of Fame shouldn\xe2\x80\x99t continue to overlook someone whose influence on the game has been profound.'
b'By Jamie Malanowski'
b'Mr. Malanowski, a former Little League player with a .125 batting average over 18 games, is a speechwriter.'
b'This week, the Baseball Hall of Fame will announce a new class of inductees, setting off rounds of celebrations \xe2\x80\x94 and debates. Fans will argue over whether Mariano Rivera deserves unanimous approval, or whether the use of performance-enhancing drugs should permanently block the enshrinement of Barry Bonds.'
b'Oddly, amid these debates, one of the Hall of Fame\xe2\x80\x99s key omissions is likely to be overlooked. How is it that it has left out \xe2\x80\x94 and perhaps not even discussed \xe2\x80\x94 the man who has had the greatest influence on baseball in the last 40 years, who has changed how the game is understood, how it is enjoyed and even how it is played? I\xe2\x80\x99m talking about the statistician and historian Bill James.'
b'A graduate of the University of Kansas, James began his professional involvement with baseball in the late \xe2\x80\x9970s, while working nights as a security guard at a cannery. When not foiling pork-and-bean burglaries, he used his free time to record and analyze baseball statistics. He had a quirky curiosity that led him to ask offbeat questions, whose answers he extracted from the numbers he kept. He wasn\xe2\x80\x99t afraid to deflate reputations or debunk conventional wisdom. He turned his findings into articles, and eventually best-selling books. His writing was smart, funny, contentious, and unlike anything fans had ever read.'
b'It may be hard for younger fans to grasp how innumerate baseball was. There were homers and R.B.I.s and batting averages for hitters; wins and losses and E.R.A.s for pitchers. Teams had winning and losing streaks. Instead of analysts, broadcasts had color commentators.'
b'As a result, fans had little understanding of the game\xe2\x80\x99s subtleties. Suddenly, here was James, unearthing hidden explanations, revealing lame assumptions, uncovering the value of overlooked variables. How much did it cost the Cubs to play day games in Wrigley Field? Did Ted Williams lose more homers playing in Fenway Park than Joe DiMaggio lost playing in Yankee Stadium? '
b'James did his best work re-evaluating reputations. He showed that the infielder famous for diving catches actually lacked range, that the genius manager who strategically bunted was actually squandering outs, that more of your favorite slugger\xe2\x80\x99s homers could be ascribed to close fences than to his prodigious power.'
b'James revealed a game in which your eyes deceived you. A banjo-hitting second baseman who walked a lot was a bigger offensive asset than the long-ball threat who struck out a lot. The wily catcher who knew how to frame pitches might be more responsible for strikeouts than the pitcher who threw them.'
b'James did not invent analytics \xe2\x80\x94 other students of the game formed the Society for American Baseball Research years before he began his studies. But his lively, provocative writing helped him elevate the field at just the right time. The new network ESPN integrated stats into its programming. Players of the new pastime, fantasy baseball, hungered for stats. Agents and general managers alike gobbled up stats to justify free-agent contracts. Numbers enriched the whole show.'
b'I met James once, at a corporate event in the early \xe2\x80\x9980s. We were part of a group that attended an ordinary game at Shea Stadium between a poor New York Mets team and the first-place Los Angeles Dodgers. James was a typical fan; he drank a beer, he did the wave. But he also carried a bedraggled notebook, in which he recorded the lineups and the game conditions, drew stick figures showing the pitchers\xe2\x80\x99 windups, and noted every pitch that was thrown.'
b'We were in the middle of a scoreless game when James did something astounding. The Dodgers pitcher had just recorded out No. 1 for the inning, and James said, \xe2\x80\x9cThe Mets are going to score this inning.\xe2\x80\x9d Yeah, right, I thought. One out, nobody on, average hitters coming up. But then, yes, the Mets scored, and again, and again.'
b' \xe2\x80\x9cThe Dodgers\xe2\x80\x99 starter took 11 pitches to retire the first hitter," James explained. \xe2\x80\x9cPitchers usually need 15 pitches to get through a whole inning.\xe2\x80\x9d With the pitcher faltering, he said, \xe2\x80\x9cthe Mets\xe2\x80\x99 chances dramatically increased.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'This year, watch any game, and you will almost certainly hear the announcers discuss spin ratio, exit velocity, wins above replacement and other analytical concepts. Teams will shift defenders, arrange lineups, substitute players and choose pitches all based on the numbers. You may even gripe about the preponderance of strikeouts and homers \xe2\x80\x94 another stat-derived trend. James did not uncover all these findings, but his analytics revolution pervades baseball \xe2\x80\x94 and all major sports are now influenced by analytics. Did you know goalies who start on back-to-back nights record save percentages on average 11 points lower on the second night? N.H.L. general managers do.'
b'Fundamentally, baseball is the same game it has always been \xe2\x80\x94 hit, throw, catch. But thanks to Bill James, there have been changes. For one thing, James is now an executive with the Boston Red Sox. But more important, a new era of fans knows that inside good old country hardball there\xe2\x80\x99s a deeper, richer game. Cooperstown, the next move is yours.'
b'Jamie Malanowski is a speechwriter for Gov. Andrew Cuomo of New York.'
b'Follow The New York Times Opinion section on Facebook, Twitter (@NYTopinion) and Instagram.'
b'An earlier version of this article misstated the name of a research organization. It is the Society for American Baseball Research, not the Society for Advanced Baseball Research.'

b'By Victor Mather'
b'When Bryce Harper hit a powerful eighth-inning home run on Tuesday night, it wrapped up a dramatic homecoming narrative. But getting almost as much buzz was his top-notch bat flip.'
b'It was Harper\xe2\x80\x99s first game back in Washington after leaving the Nationals to join the Philadelphia Phillies as a free agent in the off-season. Before the game, he made a magnanimous statement on Instagram thanking Nationals fans and saying he would \xe2\x80\x9calways remember the cheers.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Nonetheless, he faced a predictable deluge of boos throughout the game from the home fans. (Perhaps they took their cue from the mayor, Muriel Bowser, who tweeted and then deleted a picture of Harper as Benedict Arnold.)'
b'Parked in right field, where Harper plays, was a group of noisy Phillies fans, and Harper took a moment to salute them.'
b'He started slowly, with two strikeouts. But then he had a double and a run-scoring single. In his final at-bat, he powered a shot into the second deck in right, fittingly just above those Phillies fans.'
b'That brought the bat flip. The typical home run flip comes immediately after the swing and tends to be horizontal. Sometimes it is performed with enthusiasm and sometimes with arrogance.'
b'But Harper took his time. He switched hands, then heaved it up one-handed. The toss had good height and tremendous speed, completing several rapid rotations.'
b'That was followed by the home run trot and a complex series of fist bumps and poses with his teammates in the dugout.'
b'Bat flips can cause hard feelings, as some opposing players tend to feel it violates an unwritten code of the game. Some flips have cleared the benches.'
b'Nationals Manager Davey Martinez was more concerned with his shortstop Trea Turner\xe2\x80\x99s broken finger after the game. \xe2\x80\x9cI try not to watch,\xe2\x80\x9d he said when asked about his thoughts on bat flips. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s the way the game\xe2\x80\x99s evolved.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Flips are unlikely to become a disciplinary issue like steroids or beanballs. Major League Baseball can\xe2\x80\x99t be too upset, considering it has posted a video highlighting the top 50 bat flips of all time.'
b'And those unwritten codes do not really translate to other baseball cultures. In South Korea, flamboyant flips draw shrugs, not scorn.'
b'Some more memorable flippery:'
b'The nonchalant flip. Junior Lake\xe2\x80\x99s slow, deliberate flip in 2015 prompted an on-field brouhaha.'
b'The disdainful flip. Albert Pujols dripped derision with a delayed toss in 2009.'
b'The historic flip. Barry Bonds tied the home run record with 70 in 2001, then executed a soft, high, looping flip that seemed as if it would never come down.'
b'The long-delayed flip. Jose Ramirez annoyed the Twins in 2015 with a flip that came halfway to first base.'
b'The famous flip. Jose Bautista\xe2\x80\x99s flip from the 2015 division series has yet to be bettered. His homer broke a tie in the deciding game of the series. After the swing, Bautista stood immobile at the plate watching the ball, then performed a muscular hurl that sent his bat deep into foul territory.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s doing stuff kids do in Wiffle ball games,\xe2\x80\x9d Rangers reliever Sam Dyson groused.'
b'That\xe2\x80\x99s a Wiffle ball game many people might like to see.'

b'Supported by'
b'By Victor Mather'
b'Here comes the baseball season, which means, in more and more of the United States, here comes the baseball betting season.'
b'In Europe, where sports betting thrives, wagering on N.F.L. and N.B.A. games has been fairly popular for years, but baseball, mostly unknown on the continent, has not made a huge impact. With the American market opening up after a Supreme Court ruling that struck down a gambling ban, baseball betting could be ready to take its place alongside hot dogs and apple pie.'
b'So if sports betting is legal in your jurisdiction, peruse these odds and try to find a bet that will keep you in peanuts and Cracker Jack.'
b'Sorry to bore you, but it\xe2\x80\x99s the Boston Red Sox and the Yankees again. The Red Sox won 108 regular-season games and the World Series last year, losing only three postseason games. They are 6-to-1 favorites to repeat. Many bookmakers are putting the Yankees up at the same odds, and some are hedging even further by making the Houston Astros 6-1 as well. Just behind are the World Series runners-up, the Los Angeles Dodgers, at 7-1 or so.'
b'Want to make the big bucks? The Baltimore Orioles were 47-115 last season. If you think that adding Nate Karns and Jesus Sucre will somehow allow them to emulate the Miracle Mets, you can get a price of as much as 500- or 600-1.'
b'A couple of the races seem like locks. The Astros are 1-6 to win the American League West (that means you must put up $6 to win a buck). The Dodgers in the National League West and the Indians in the A.L. Central are 1-4. Not a lot of moneymaking opportunities there. The Red Sox and the Yankees should finish 1-2 in some order in the A.L. East.'
b'But the two remaining races seem like barnburners. In the N.L. East, the Philadelphia Phillies and their big acquisition, Bryce Harper, are favorites along with the Washington Nationals at 2-1. The Atlanta Braves, the defending division champions, are getting a little less respect this year at 3-1. And the Mets, at 7-2, are far from out of the race. Only the Miami Marlins (150-1) are given no hope.'
b'In the N.L. Central, it\xe2\x80\x99s a three-way race, with the Chicago Cubs, the St. Louis Cardinals and the Milwaukee Brewers closely matched at 2-1 or slightly above. Depending on where you bet, any one of them might be a slight favorite.'
b'Even if you don\xe2\x80\x99t like to wager, the odds can be revealing about which teams have a good chance of surprising, or slumping, at least according to the prevailing wisdom.'
b'It probably isn\xe2\x80\x99t too shocking to see the Orioles and the Marlins as long shots. But three teams that had discouraging seasons last year seem to be attracting some betting interest. The Chicago White Sox (62-100) and the Cincinnati Reds (67-95) would seem to have a long way to go. But each is about 10-1 to win its division, a real puncher\xe2\x80\x99s chance. So are the San Diego Padres (66-96), but the reason here is a lot clearer: the arrival of Manny Machado.'
b'It\xe2\x80\x99s unlikely that all three of these teams will turn it around this season, but the odds seem to be telling us that at least one will.'
b'If betting on teams isn\xe2\x80\x99t enough, most bookies are happy to take your action on the players as well.'
b'The players expected to hit the most home runs this year are the Yankees sluggers Giancarlo Stanton (7-1) and Aaron Judge (8-1). That leaves last year\xe2\x80\x99s home run king, Khris Davis of the Athletics, at 10-1.'
b'Davis hit 48 homers last season, while Stanton had 38 and Judge 27 (in 112 games), so the odds might well be testament to the legion of Yankees fans eager to support their favorites.'
b'Mookie Betts of the Red Sox and Jose Altuve of the Astros are favorites in the hits category, while last year\xe2\x80\x99s leader, Whit Merrifield of the Royals, is given little chance of a repeat: 25-1.'
b'The predicted runs batted in champ is J.D. Martinez of the Red Sox at 6-1 after a season with a major-league-leading 130.'
b'Pitching wins can be an unpredictable category. No one has repeated as the majors\xe2\x80\x99 leader since C.C. Sabathia in 2009 and 2010, and bettors have to weigh the quality of the pitcher and of his team. The odds reflect that. Chris Sale of the Red Sox is the favorite, but plenty of other aces \xe2\x80\x94 including Max Scherzer of the Nationals, Corey Kluber of the Indians and Justin Verlander of the Astros \xe2\x80\x94 are given a good shot.'
b'Season-long bets are all well and good, but they certainly take time to resolve. Action-hungry gamblers will be heading for more traditional fare and betting on the opening day games.'
b'The result of any single baseball game is unpredictable, of course, and many of the opening day contests seem like tossups.'
b'Well, except one. The Yankees, playing at home behind Masahiro Tanaka, are 3\xc2\xbd-1 favorites over, yes, the hapless Orioles.'

b'Extra Bases'
b'By Tyler Kepner'
b'The Tampa Bay Rays arrived in Toronto this weekend with the only winning record in the American League East. They were 10-3 entering Friday\xe2\x80\x99s games, with a 1.98 team earned run average that was easily the best in the major leagues.'
b'And they had used an opener only twice. Creating the position of opener \xe2\x80\x94 essentially a reliever who starts the game and works only an inning or two \xe2\x80\x94 helped the Rays surge to 90 victories last season. But the notion that Tampa Bay intended to blow up pitching as we know it was always misguided.'
b'The Rays, after all, had the A.L. Cy Young Award winner last season, Blake Snell, and signed him to a five-year, $50 million contract extension in March. Their No. 2 starter, Charlie Morton, signed as a free agent in December and will earn $15 million this season and next, the highest salary in team history.'
b'Their third and fourth starters, Tyler Glasnow and Yonny Chirinos, both 25, combined to go 5-0 in their first five starts, allowing two runs in 29 innings, with 32 strikeouts and four walks.'
b'So, yes, the Rays believe in elite starting pitching. They do not believe in mediocre pitching of any kind, and have not had much of it so far.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe tried to put ourselves in a position to have a lot of interesting depth,\xe2\x80\x9d said Chaim Bloom, the Rays\xe2\x80\x99 senior vice president for baseball operations. \xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s a lot of guys with great upside.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Morton, 35, took years to realize his upside as a young pitcher with Atlanta and Pittsburgh. He finally discovered it with the Houston Astros, when he learned to attack hitters with curveballs and high fastballs instead of trying to induce contact with sinkers. He won Game 7 of the American League Championship Series and of the World Series in 2017, and earned his first All-Star selection last season.'
b'Morton, too, loves the traditional role of a starting pitcher.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI grew up idolizing starting pitchers, so from a fan\xe2\x80\x99s standpoint, and from someone that\xe2\x80\x99s been a starter his whole career, essentially, I would like to see starting pitchers always have a place in the game,\xe2\x80\x9d Morton said. \xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s a balance between the poetic nature of the game \xe2\x80\x94 the nostalgic part of it, how the game flows, the mystical part of it \xe2\x80\x94 and the win/loss part, that you have to win. We\xe2\x80\x99re trying to find a balance in that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Last summer \xe2\x80\x94 after trading Chris Archer to Pittsburgh (for Glasnow and outfielder Austin Meadows) and Nathan Eovaldi to Boston \xe2\x80\x94 the Rays found that balance with regular use of the opener, allowing pitchers like Chirinos and Ryan Yarbrough to work the bulk of a game after a reliever had gone through a few tough hitters to start.'
b'Chirinos pitched four to seven innings in each of his last 10 appearances last season, without starting any of those games. His E.R.A. in those games was 3.04. Yarbrough went 16-6 over all but started only six times. The Rays will adjust their roles this season based on matchups, to maximize their chance of success and avoid that dreaded mediocrity.'
b'The Yankees and the Boston Red Sox will always have a significant financial edge on the Rays, whose $60 million payroll is less than the combined 2019 salaries of the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 Giancarlo Stanton, Masahiro Tanaka and Jacoby Ellsbury.'
b'But Tampa Bay is supplementing its major league roster with products from a farm system that Baseball America ranked No. 2 in the game, after San Diego\xe2\x80\x99s. Shortstop Wander Franco, pitcher Brent Honeywell and the two-way player Brendan McKay all rank among MLB.com\xe2\x80\x99s top 30 prospects.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s where we have to be,\xe2\x80\x9d Bloom said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99ve put a lot of effort over the last few years into making sure the system was as deep and robust as possible. We need depth, we need top-end talent, and we need to have a steady flow of championship-caliber players, so we put a lot of energy and focus on that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It is very early, of course, but those young players have helped the Rays open their biggest lead in the A.L. East since mid-May 2011, when they led by two and a half games.'
b'Their only current player who was on a major league roster then: Morton, naturally. With a home in Bradenton, Fla., and four young children, he has found the perfect spot for a contract he said would be the last of his career.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI didn\xe2\x80\x99t know what to expect, just because, historically, the Rays haven\xe2\x80\x99t spent a lot of money on free-agent starting pitching, ever,\xe2\x80\x9d Morton said. \xe2\x80\x9cSo I wasn\xe2\x80\x99t thinking, \xe2\x80\x98I\xe2\x80\x99m the guy.\xe2\x80\x99 When they called and we got the impression they were going to be pretty aggressive, I started to get excited and my wife got excited. We tried not to get our hopes up, because we knew that this was an ideal situation. But for it to work out the way it did, it\xe2\x80\x99s kind of unbelievable.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Kramer Robertson was 10 years old in 2005, the first time he cut down a basketball net to celebrate an N.C.A.A. championship for the Baylor Lady Bears. The second time, in 2012, he was 17.'
b'Last Sunday, though, he was all grown up and playing for the Springfield Cardinals, a Class AA team in the St. Louis farm system. Robertson could not be in Tampa, Fla., for the national title game with his mother, Kim Mulkey, the Baylor coach, and his sister, Makenzie Fuller, the associate director of team operations.'
b'Instead, Robertson was on the Cardinals\xe2\x80\x99 team bus, about halfway between Fayetteville, Ark., and Tulsa, Okla., huddled with teammates around a phone that was streaming the broadcast. Just minutes before tipoff, Mulkey had sent him a text message about his game. Now he was watching hers, exulting from afar as the Lady Bears beat Notre Dame in a thriller, 82-81.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe were in the middle of nowhere, we barely had service, but I was fired up,\xe2\x80\x9d Robertson, a shortstop, said by phone the other day. \xe2\x80\x9cThe first thing I thought to do was FaceTime my brother-in-law. I was not expecting him to answer, I was just so excited and I wanted to be there so bad. But then it said, \xe2\x80\x98Connecting,\xe2\x80\x99 and the first face I saw was my mom\xe2\x80\x99s. I didn\xe2\x80\x99t know what to say, so I just started screaming.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Robertson\xe2\x80\x99s brother-in-law, Clay Fuller, is a former minor leaguer with the Los Angeles Angels. His father, Randy Robertson, is a former quarterback for Louisiana Tech, where Kim Mulkey was an All-American point guard. She has coached at Baylor since 2000, turning around a team that went 7-20 the season before she arrived and setting a powerful example for her son.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve seen how she\xe2\x80\x99s handled failure and success with humility and never wavered in her morals,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cShe always taught me, \xe2\x80\x98Nothing great ever gets done without enthusiasm.\xe2\x80\x99 I\xe2\x80\x99ve remembered that throughout my baseball career, especially in the minor leagues, where it can get monotonous and it\xe2\x80\x99s easy to get complacent.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'There was little chance of that on Tuesday against the Tulsa Drillers, who started Clayton Kershaw, a three-time Cy Young Award winner making a rehabilitation start as he recovers from shoulder soreness. Kershaw, who is scheduled to start for the Los Angeles Dodgers on Monday, pitched five shutout innings before Robertson led off the sixth with a home run off a high fastball.'
b'It was the first homer of the season for Robertson, and it gave him his own highlight in a memorable week for his family. Back home in Texas, his mother was watching.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI got to my phone, and my mom was so excited,\xe2\x80\x9d Robertson said. \xe2\x80\x9cShe was like, \xe2\x80\x98No you didn\xe2\x80\x99t!\xe2\x80\x99 Normally I would try to play it off, but in a situation like that, I was going to embrace the moment, not try to be too cool. That was special.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Groundskeepers of the Atlantic League can stand down. There will be no movement of the pitchers\xe2\x80\x99 mounds this season \xe2\x80\x94 and, if common sense prevails, not anytime soon.'
b'With strikeout rates rising every season since 2006, Major League Baseball has been searching for ways to stimulate action on the field. The independent Atlantic League will be a testing ground for some experimental playing rules. The most radical proposal was scheduled to take effect at midseason, with the distance between the pitching rubber and home plate moved back by two feet, to 62 feet 6 inches.'
b'On Wednesday, the Atlantic League announced that this change would be delayed until the second half of the 2020 season, and that another change \xe2\x80\x94 the use of radar tracking technology to help umpires call balls and strikes \xe2\x80\x94 would be introduced gradually this season, not on opening day in late April.'
b'Given the fragile nature of pitchers\xe2\x80\x99 arms, moving back the mound for the first time since 1893 would seem to invite even further injury risk. The change could also discourage pitchers from joining the Atlantic League, because of possible injury and because the distance in affiliated ball \xe2\x80\x94 where the athletes aspire to be \xe2\x80\x94 remains 60-6.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAny pitcher that has significant major league time, I think, would be very apprehensive to try to make that change at that stage of his career,\xe2\x80\x9d said the agent Tom O\xe2\x80\x99Connell, whose client Jon Niese signed with the Long Island Ducks on Wednesday. \xe2\x80\x9cThankfully, we\xe2\x80\x99re not going to have to make that decision. But I would be very concerned next year if I\xe2\x80\x99m a former major league player that\xe2\x80\x99s trying to make a comeback \xe2\x80\x94 very concerned.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Niese, 32, pitched in the majors from 2008 through 2016 before missing the last two seasons recovering from knee surgery. He is one of two members of the Mets\xe2\x80\x99 2015 World Series team to sign with the Ducks for this season, with outfielder Kirk Nieuwenhuis.'

b'Yankees 15, Orioles 3'
b'By James Wagner'
b'BALTIMORE \xe2\x80\x94 Gary Sanchez stepped to the plate in the ninth inning on Sunday with a chance at history. Four-homer games are more rare than perfect games, and Sanchez had already gone long three times on Sunday as part of an offensive explosion by the wounded Yankees that produced 14 home runs against the Baltimore Orioles this weekend.'
b'With the goal of the at-bat so clear, and with Hanser Alberto, an infielder, on the mound, Sanchez was under enormous pressure to go deep a fourth time.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI tried to do what everyone was thinking about,\xe2\x80\x9d Sanchez said, smiling. \xe2\x80\x9cBut some anxiety didn\xe2\x80\x99t let me hit it.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It did not matter that Sanchez flew out to left field. With seven home runs on Sunday, the Yankees still drubbed the Orioles, 15-3, to improve their record to 5-4 and cap a three-game sweep in which 26 of their 29 runs came via the long ball.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThat would\xe2\x80\x99ve been a way to top off,\xe2\x80\x9d left fielder Clint Frazier, who clubbed two home runs himself, said of Sanchez. \xe2\x80\x9cBut three homers isn\xe2\x80\x99t too bad, either.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Fault Sanchez, the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 primary catcher, for certain aspects of his game; he has made a handful of baserunning and defensive miscues a week and a half into the season. But do not fault him \xe2\x80\x94 or, for that matter, the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 depleted lineup \xe2\x80\x94 for a lack of power.'
b'Serving as the designated hitter on Sunday, Sanchez produced career highs in home runs and runs batted in (six). The four hits and four R.B.I. by Frazier, who missed most of last season because of a concussion, were also career bests.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI just feel healthier this year, and I feel better,\xe2\x80\x9d said Sanchez, who endured the worst all-around season of his career in 2018 along with off-season surgery on his nonthrowing shoulder. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd I hope to keep doing that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'After the game, Sanchez grinned while describing how thrilled he was with his performance at the plate. His six home runs over all pace a Yankees squad that has 11 players on the injured list. Although the injured hitters Miguel Andujar, Didi Gregorius, Giancarlo Stanton and Aaron Hicks accounted for 119 of the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 major-league-record 267 homers last season, the lineup still showed off its firepower against the Orioles, who are rebuilding after posting the worst record in baseball in 2018.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cSometimes, it takes the whole 40-man roster,\xe2\x80\x9d Frazier said, adding later, \xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re someone to still be worried about whenever we come to town.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The power display, which also featured home runs by shortstop Gleyber Torres and catcher Austin Romine, supported the stout pitching of Domingo German, who did not allow a hit until the sixth inning. German has pitched well in two starts for a rotation lacking the ace Luis Severino and C. C. Sabathia, who might return from the I.L. next weekend.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNow I have the opportunity, I\xe2\x80\x99m doing everything I can to show all my work on the field,\xe2\x80\x9d German said. \xe2\x80\x9cEvery start I want to execute like it\xe2\x80\x99s my last.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'At the plate last year, the Yankees led baseball with 51 percent of their runs coming via homers. They were second entering Sunday.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNever too much for us,\xe2\x80\x9d Yankees Manager Aaron Boone said. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m always good with us hitting as much as we need to.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Yankees needed Sanchez now, and on Sunday he reinforced the team decision makers\xe2\x80\x99 faith in him \xe2\x80\x94 previous defensive and baserunning miscues and all.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s a great player that\xe2\x80\x99s still growing, and it\xe2\x80\x99s our job to help him continue to reach his peak in every facet of the game,\xe2\x80\x9d Boone said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s making strides in a lot of areas of the game. b'FORT MYERS, Fla. \xe2\x80\x94 The Boston Red Sox ran away with the American League East last summer, then stormed through the postseason with only one loss in each round. It was one of the most emphatic championship runs in recent history \xe2\x80\x94 but only in the retelling.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cPeople generalize and they\xe2\x80\x99ll say, \xe2\x80\x98O.K., the Red Sox won 108 games and went 11-3 in the postseason, look how easy it was,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d said Dave Dombrowski, the president of baseball operations, from his office at JetBlue Park this week. \xe2\x80\x9cWell, it wasn\xe2\x80\x99t easy. It really wasn\xe2\x80\x99t. During the regular season, even with 108 wins, the Yankees won 100.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAnd I know people say, \xe2\x80\x98Oh, that\xe2\x80\x99s an eight-game difference,\xe2\x80\x99 which I understand can be quite a bit. But it sure didn\xe2\x80\x99t feel that way.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The season essentially hinged on Boston\xe2\x80\x99s four-game sweep of the Yankees at Fenway Park in early August. Had the Yankees won those games instead, both teams would have finished with 104 victories. That is how close the old rivals were.'
b'They diverged this winter, though, with revealing approaches to the off-season. The Red Sox are prepared to rely heavily on their starting rotation, while the Yankees reinvested significantly in their bullpen.'
b'The Yankees gave three-year deals to two free-agent relievers: Zack Britton ($39 million) and Adam Ottavino ($27 million). The Red Sox, who will face the Yankees for the second and final time this spring at Steinbrenner Field on Friday, spent about the same amount to retain starter Nathan Eovaldi for four years and $68 million. But they lost two relievers \xe2\x80\x94 Joe Kelly, who signed for three years and $25 million with the Los Angeles Dodgers, and closer Craig Kimbrel, who is unsigned \xe2\x80\x94 without replacing them.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThey wanted me back, I wanted to be back here and we were able to make that work,\xe2\x80\x9d Eovaldi said Wednesday, after his first start of the exhibition season. \xe2\x80\x9cWe kept on that same game plan with that goal in mind to be able to come back and win a World Series. We\xe2\x80\x99re taking the little steps now to be able to do that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Red Sox will again have baseball\xe2\x80\x99s highest payroll, at more than $220 million. But they still had to make choices, especially with several important players facing free agency within the next two years.'
b'They chose to keep their sturdy rotation together \xe2\x80\x94 at a cost of about $83.5 million for Chris Sale, David Price, Rick Porcello and Eovaldi. Those four and Eduardo Rodriguez, who earns $4.3 million, went 68-28 for Boston last season, including October.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIn my opinion, it\xe2\x80\x99s just good baseball,\xe2\x80\x9d said Porcello, the 2016 A.L. Cy Young Award winner. \xe2\x80\x9cMost of the teams that are competing for a World Series year-in and year-out have good starting rotations, and almost all of the teams that have won have had ace-type guys, and guys that fill out the rotation to give them the foundation they need.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cFor us as starting pitchers, we want to chew up the most innings as possible and give the team a chance to win as frequently as we can.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Boston starters actually did not throw very many innings last season. Porcello led the staff with 191\xe2\x85\x93, with Price at 176, Sale at 158, Rodriguez at 129\xe2\x85\x94 and Eovaldi at 111 including his time with Tampa Bay. But the Yankees got even fewer innings from their starters, and their newcomer, James Paxton, never threw more than 160\xe2\x85\x93 innings in his six seasons with Seattle.'
b'Several teams have shifted to a model that emphasizes quality over bulk from their starters\xe2\x80\x99 outings \xe2\x80\x94 fewer innings but more effective ones, a plan that relies on a procession of reliable relievers. The Yankees should have that luxury this season, with Britton and Ottavino to go with Chad Green, Dellin Betances and closer Aroldis Chapman.'
b'The Red Sox bullpen is far less imposing: Matt Barnes, Ryan Brazier, Heath Hembree, Brian Johnson, Tyler Thornburg, Hector Velazquez and another spot to be determined. Dombrowski said he was confident in the group, and in the team\xe2\x80\x99s ability to identify other options if it fails.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou can find relievers, and relievers have a tendency to come from anywhere,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cHistory shows you that right now, short of the premium guys, there\xe2\x80\x99s a lot of inconsistency in relievers from year to year. Part of it is they get used so much when they\xe2\x80\x99re pitching well that one season. For me, I just choose to go with the starting pitchers, assuming they\xe2\x80\x99re of quality nature.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Red Sox\xe2\x80\x99s trick last fall was in letting their elite starters double as dominant relievers. Manager Alex Cora brought along the starters slowly last spring training \xe2\x80\x94 as he is doing again now \xe2\x80\x94 and the sweep of the Yankees in August allowed him to carefully manage their workloads down the stretch.'
b'The result was a mostly fresh rotation, as Sale, Price, Porcello, Eovaldi and Rodriguez all appeared as both starters and relievers in the postseason. Eovaldi pitched in a setup role to help win Games 1 and 2 of the World Series in Boston, then threw 97 pitches in relief at Dodger Stadium in Game 3, an 18-inning Red Sox loss.'
b'That was the rare moral victory that also had tangible benefits, galvanizing the Red Sox clubhouse around Eovaldi and crystallizing the starters\xe2\x80\x99 selfless approach \xe2\x80\x94 even if they still don\xe2\x80\x99t buy the hoopla.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cEver since I was watching baseball as a kid, I\xe2\x80\x99m watching Randy Johnson run out of the bullpen and pitch the eighth inning or whatever,\xe2\x80\x9d Porcello said. \xe2\x80\x9cAs far as I\xe2\x80\x99m concerned, I actually don\xe2\x80\x99t understand the big deal around it, because that\xe2\x80\x99s our job, and if we\xe2\x80\x99re not here to sell out when we have the opportunity to win a World Series, then what are we doing?\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Cora absorbed the starters-as-relievers strategy in 2017 as the bench coach for Houston\xe2\x80\x99s championship team. The Astros and Red Sox showed that the bullpen listed on a regular-season lineup card is not always the same as the one a team will use to win a title.'
b'Dombrowski said it was presumptuous, with a long season ahead and the Yankees always looming, to plan on reprising that plan this October. But Cora is eager for an encore \xe2\x80\x94 knowing, perhaps, that it represents this roster\xe2\x80\x99s best chance to repeat.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt was fun to get text messages: \xe2\x80\x98Hey, give me the ball tomorrow,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d Cora said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a testament to who they are, how they felt and what they wanted. b'TAMPA, Fla. \xe2\x80\x94 If the San Diego Padres had stayed away from elite free agents this winter, people would have understood. They gave out the richest contract on last year\xe2\x80\x99s free-agent market, yet finished with their worst record in a decade.'
b'But the Padres could not resist the allure of Manny Machado, and on Tuesday they established a new standard for free agency to get him. They agreed with Machado on a 10-year contract worth $300 million, the most ever guaranteed to a free agent.'
b'The Padres did not announce the agreement, because Machado must first pass a physical, but the deal \xe2\x80\x94 which includes an opt-out clause after 2023 \xe2\x80\x94 was confirmed by a person in baseball with direct knowledge of it.'
b'Machado, a four-time All-Star at third base and shortstop, spent last season with the Baltimore Orioles and the Los Angeles Dodgers, hitting .297 with 37 homers and 107 R.B.I. He joins first baseman Eric Hosmer \xe2\x80\x94 who signed with the Padres last February for eight years and $144 million \xe2\x80\x94 in an effort to revive a team that went 66-96 last season, its eighth losing record in a row.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s not that many guys who get to free agency at that superstar level at 26 years old,\xe2\x80\x9d Dodgers starter Clayton Kershaw told reporters in Glendale, Ariz., when asked about Machado. \xe2\x80\x9cTen years seems fair, for sure, and getting that 30 a year is great. I can\xe2\x80\x99t say I\xe2\x80\x99m happy for him \xe2\x80\x94 he\xe2\x80\x99s on the Padres now \xe2\x80\x94 but it\xe2\x80\x99s good to maybe get that market going a little bit, for sure.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Until Machado\xe2\x80\x99s agreement, only one free agent, Patrick Corbin of the Washington Nationals, had signed for more than $68 million this off-season. Outfielder Bryce Harper, a former National League most valuable player for Washington, surely hopes to break Machado\xe2\x80\x99s mark soon. Harper has drawn interest from the Philadelphia Phillies and the San Francisco Giants, among others.'
b'Machado had met in person with the Chicago White Sox, the Phillies and the Yankees, who never made a formal offer. The Yankees instead signed four free agents to two- or three-year deals worth a combined $124 million \xe2\x80\x94 pitchers Zack Britton, J.A. Happ and Adam Ottavino, and second baseman DJ LeMahieu \xe2\x80\x94 while trading for starter James Paxton and retaining C.\xe2\x80\x89C. Sabathia and outfielder Brett Gardner.'
b'As good as Machado is, the Yankees \xe2\x80\x94 who lost to Boston in a division series last fall \xe2\x80\x94 believe they did not need him.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe lineup and team that we have is pretty darn good,\xe2\x80\x9d outfielder Aaron Judge said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe won 100 games, so we weren\xe2\x80\x99t in a position, I felt like, that we needed to go out there and grab too many big pieces. We were already set.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Yankees have baseball\xe2\x80\x99s other $300 million player, outfielder Giancarlo Stanton, who is entering the fifth year of a 13-year, $325 million contract extension he signed with his previous team, the Miami Marlins. Stanton said Machado\xe2\x80\x99s deal was \xe2\x80\x9cgreat for him,\xe2\x80\x9d but it did not seem to quell his dismay at the state of free agency in baseball.'
b'Indeed, Tuesday\xe2\x80\x99s news is unlikely to stifle the rhetoric from players, who always expected Machado and Harper to get lucrative contracts. Players are more concerned about the rank-and-file free agents who have struggled to find jobs as several teams field threadbare rosters.'
b'Stanton cited infielder Mike Moustakas, who hit 38 homers for Kansas City in 2017 and then turned down a one-year qualifying offer for $17.4 million. He lingered on the open market, returned to the Royals for one year and $6.5 million, then signed another one-year deal with Milwaukee for $10 million on Sunday.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou\xe2\x80\x99ve got guys hitting 30-plus homers who have to settle for one year, below their grade of pay, going year to year,\xe2\x80\x9d Stanton said, referring to Moustakas. \xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99ve got to figure it out. It\xe2\x80\x99s not good. Not good on the players\xe2\x80\x99 side.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Baseball\xe2\x80\x99s collective-bargaining agreement clearly encourages teams to rebuild with prospects \xe2\x80\x94 that is, to accept losing for a while \xe2\x80\x94 by baking in so many incentives to help the worst teams get the best amateur talent. But not all unsigned free agents are unwanted.'
b'One factor we rarely know is the value of the offers free agents reject. Pitchers like Dallas Keuchel and Craig Kimbrel have not found suitable contracts yet, but it is possible they have priced themselves out. The data revolution has changed how teams evaluate players, and those who refuse to accept this can be left out.'
b'For Machado, his youth and performance prevailed in the end, leading to a record deal. The Padres should have plenty of cheap labor around him \xe2\x80\x94 they have seven of the game\xe2\x80\x99s top 50 prospects, as ranked by MLB.com \xe2\x80\x94 and hope to finally win a World Series for a city with no other major pro sports teams.'
b'For most of their 50 seasons, the Padres have been better known for helping other teams win. All of those players won championships with their new teams.'
b'Machado struck out against Boston\xe2\x80\x99s Chris Sale to end the World Series last October, but at least he got there. The Padres have not been since 1998. They remain a long way from contention \xe2\x80\x94 quick, name two Padres pitchers \xe2\x80\x94 but took an important step on Tuesday with a deal that shows there is plenty of money to go around in this sport.'

b'Sandy Alderson, who left his post as the Mets\xe2\x80\x99 general manager last summer because of a cancer recurrence, will return to his baseball roots now that his health has improved.'
b'The Oakland Athletics announced on Tuesday that Alderson, 71, would rejoin the club as a senior adviser in the baseball operations department, two decades after he left the team in the hands of Billy Beane.'
b'Alderson announced on Saturday at the New York Baseball Writers\xe2\x80\x99 Awards dinner, where he received an award honoring his career, that he had been cancer-free for four months. He received a standing ovation.'
b'Alderson began his baseball career with the A\xe2\x80\x99s in 1981 and was one of the sport\xe2\x80\x99s pioneers in sabermetrics. Back then, he counseled Beane, his successor, whose reliance on advanced statistics kept the small-market team competitive and was famously documented in the book \xe2\x80\x9cMoneyball.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHis mentorship and friendship have been invaluable to me over the course of my career, and I look forward to the expertise and perspective he will add at every level of the organization,\xe2\x80\x9d Beane, the A\xe2\x80\x99s executive vice president of baseball operations, said of Alderson in a statement issued by the team.'
b'Referring to David Forst, the current A\xe2\x80\x99s general manager, Beane added, \xe2\x80\x9cDavid and I couldn\xe2\x80\x99t be more excited to bring him back to Oakland.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Alderson was the architect of the A\xe2\x80\x99s teams that won three straight American League pennants from 1988 to \xe2\x80\x9990, as well as the 1989 World Series. He left in 1998.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI am really excited to return to the A\xe2\x80\x99s and the Bay Area,\xe2\x80\x9d Alderson said in the team\xe2\x80\x99s statement. \xe2\x80\x9cI look forward to being as helpful as I can to Billy, David and the rest of the baseball operations staff.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'After his 17-season stint with the Athletics, Alderson spent seven years working in Major League Baseball headquarters and four years as the chief executive of the San Diego Padres, before going back to the M.L.B. commissioner\xe2\x80\x99s office for a year.'
b'From October 2010 until June 2018, Alderson served as the Mets\xe2\x80\x99 general manager, guiding them from a period of financial austerity to the 2015 World Series, during which he dealt with his initial cancer diagnosis, and to a 2016 wild-card game.'
b'Then came a 92-loss season in 2017, a rough first half in 2018 and the cancer recurrence. Alderson took an indefinite leave of absence, with the expectation that the Mets would find a replacement. The team hired Brodie Van Wagenen as their new general manager in October.'
b'In other front-office news, the Mets announced that their longtime assistant general manager, John Ricco, had moved into a newly created position with the title of senior vice president, senior strategy officer. Ricco, 50, joined the Mets in 2004 and served as a right-hand man to four general managers.'
b'Ricco will now oversee special business projects involving the Mets, while continuing to advise Van Wagenen in baseball matters, such as overseeing salary arbitration, budget and payroll.'

b'TAMPA, Fla. \xe2\x80\x94 Over the winter, there was an unusual sight in the offices of Yankee Stadium. For a few days, amid the busy period as front-office employees reshaped rosters with trades and signings, Carlos Beltran was sitting among them, learning how to use the club\xe2\x80\x99s internal networks to view video and file scouting reports.'
b'In December, a year after considering him for their managerial vacancy, the Yankees hired Beltran, a nine-time All-Star who spent two and a half seasons with the Yankees, as a special adviser to General Manager Brian Cashman. While front-office positions like special adviser or special assistant can often be nebulous roles handed to former managers, coaches or players who assist at their leisure \xe2\x80\x94 Alex Rodriguez, Mariano Rivera and David Wright, to name a few \xe2\x80\x94 Cashman said Beltran was approaching his job with a full-time student\xe2\x80\x99s mind-set.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cSome parachute in and out, which is great,\xe2\x80\x9d Cashman said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut some are heavily invested, and he is heavily invested.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Beltran, 41, retired in 2017 after finally winning a World Series, with the Houston Astros. The title capped what some believe is a career with Hall of Fame credentials: 435 home runs (fourth most by a switch-hitter), 2,725 hits and three Gold Glove awards in addition to his All-Star selections.'
b'And after earning more than $220 million over 20 years in the major leagues, Beltran could be doing anything now, such as sitting on the beach in his native Puerto Rico. But he has chosen to work in the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 front office, writing his version of scouting reports and counseling the younger players throughout the organization.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI had a career in baseball, I played at a high level, and I made a lot of money in the big leagues, but man, I want these kids to accomplish their dreams,\xe2\x80\x9d he said in Spanish during spring training at the team\xe2\x80\x99s facility in Tampa, Fla. \xe2\x80\x9cThose were my dreams, too.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Before the Yankees settled on Aaron Boone as their replacement for Joe Girardi before the 2017 season, Cashman asked Beltran to interview for the manager opening. Beltran had just finished playing, and thus had no background in management, but Cashman admired Beltran for his experience, his commanding presence and his genuine personality.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s passion and joy he brings every day,\xe2\x80\x9d Cashman said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s capable of anything he wants to do.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'So Cashman contacted Beltran again, this time about a front-office position. Beltran, who lives in New York, told Cashman what he was interested in working on, and Cashman gave him the freedom to do so. For Beltran, the chance to learn the intricacies of the front office from Cashman, who has won four World Series during his two decades as the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 general manager, was enticing.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNow it\xe2\x80\x99s my turn to ask a lot of questions, see what interests me and knock on the needed doors to learn baseball from another point of view,\xe2\x80\x9d Beltran said.'
b'For Beltran, that view is from the stands, where the scouts sit and analyze the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 minor league teams during the season. It\xe2\x80\x99s a different perspective, but Beltran gave himself plenty of training for his new job during his playing days. On road trips, he often spent traveling time watching video of the opposing team\xe2\x80\x99s pitchers and hitters on his iPad and then shared his written notes with teammates and coaches. If his team was trading for a new teammate, he would call friends on the player\xe2\x80\x99s former team to get the lowdown on the new acquisition and his personality.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m passionate about this,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cSince I lived the game, I don\xe2\x80\x99t just talk about the visual aspects, but the feelings of the player or what he might be thinking in difficult situations that sometimes analytics cannot see. The front office looks a lot at the numbers, but I\xe2\x80\x99m talking about the mental side that has value. It\xe2\x80\x99s a cool combination.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Beltran spent the winter writing and filing notes on several dozen players, mostly on prospects in the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 system but also some major leaguers. It took him 90 minutes to watch video on a player and write up his thoughts, he said. He averaged two per day.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s breaking swings down and he\xe2\x80\x99s breaking down the pitching mechanics,\xe2\x80\x9d said Matt Daley, the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 assistant director of pro scouting. \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s getting pretty detailed. It\xe2\x80\x99s good information.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Beltran has also given the Yankees his perspective on how prospects can be helped to develop, particularly those from Latin America. As a player, Beltran encouraged clubs to hire Spanish-language interpreters to prevent messages from getting lost in translation between players and the team or reporters. Language barriers still persist today, he said, and can be factors in players\xe2\x80\x99 growth.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s speaking from the perspective of a guy who\xe2\x80\x99s just off the field and sees it through a player\xe2\x80\x99s lens, which is a unique aspect,\xe2\x80\x9d said Tim Naehring, the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 vice president for baseball operations. \xe2\x80\x9cWe don\xe2\x80\x99t have many other guys writing reports or putting their opinions down coming from a teammate\xe2\x80\x99s side of things.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Beltran will also counsel players throughout the season, as he did during two trips to the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 spring training this year. He will juggle that plus time at home with his wife and three young children and his baseball academy in Puerto Rico.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNow, it\xe2\x80\x99s about how I can impact the younger players,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cIf they can get something out of one conversation or one bit of advice, then at the end of the day, that\xe2\x80\x99s your legacy.\xe2\x80\x9d'
