b'A-Rod on doping, getting therapy and no longer being the villain.'
b'Alex Rodriguez has, in retirement, fashioned a comeback that far exceeds any reversals he engineered on a baseball field. It wasn\xe2\x80\x99t all that long ago that the former Yankee was one of professional sports\xe2\x80\x99 biggest bad guys, and not without reason. He was suspended for the 2014 season for violating the league\xe2\x80\x99s antidoping rules. Even aside from that, he was widely considered to be vain and disingenuous, especially in his hometown. (The New York Post honored him with \xe2\x80\x9cA-Hole\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9cA-Rat\xe2\x80\x9d cover lines, following allegations that he used performance-enhancing drugs.) But three years after his last game, Rodriguez, newly engaged to Jennifer Lopez, is a respected baseball broadcaster, a warm and self-deprecating presence on social media and a deferential businessman. You couldn\xe2\x80\x99t exactly call his image rehabilitation organic, given how hard he\xe2\x80\x99s worked at it, but it has no doubt been successful. \xe2\x80\x9cI tried to build a certain image while I was playing,\xe2\x80\x9d Rodriguez said, \xe2\x80\x9cand that plan failed miserably.\xe2\x80\x9d Now, he explained simply, \xe2\x80\x9cI have more clarity.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'What have you learned that would have made dealing with the press1 easier as a player? What I\xe2\x80\x99ve learned is that a lot of it was self-inflicted.'
b'What specifically? I represented myself the wrong way. Coming out of the suspension,2 I wanted to be honest, be accurate and be fair with the media \xe2\x80\x94 and mix in levity. I could not wait to make fun of myself. Doing that made everybody relax about me. I\xe2\x80\x99d wake up the next morning thinking I was going to get crushed by them for a mistake I\xe2\x80\x99d made. But then I\xe2\x80\x99d see that they\xe2\x80\x99d barely be talking about my [expletive] up because I\xe2\x80\x99d beat them to the punch. I still think that, for the most part, I had a good relationship with the media, but it became excellent postsuspension.'
b'Did the depiction of you as a villain feel like a misrepresentation? I would have booed me, too. I felt that being the tough guy who had all the answers and being robotic was the right thing to do. I was wrong, and now I think it\xe2\x80\x99s O.K. if I say, \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t know the answer.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'This is almost more of a philosophical thing, but baseball has a long history of players using performance enhancers \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9cBall Four\xe2\x80\x9d3 talks about guys gobbling amphetamines before games. And I\xe2\x80\x99m thinking of that in conjunction with a point Malcolm Gladwell once made4 in The New Yorker, about how players aren\xe2\x80\x99t allowed to take P.E.D.s, but it\xe2\x80\x99s O.K. for them to get Tommy John surgery, which is also a completely unnatural method of aiding your career. Does it seem at all arbitrary that baseball says P.E.D.s are cheating but certain other things aren\xe2\x80\x99t? I don\xe2\x80\x99t know. I think, with time, we\xe2\x80\x99ll be able to determine what\xe2\x80\x99s what.'
b'Of all the big-time baseball players who were implicated during the steroids era, you seem to have done the best \xe2\x80\x94 better than guys like Barry Bonds or Roger Clemens \xe2\x80\x94 at coming out of that controversy in a positive way. Why is that? I cannot speak about anybody else. If you\xe2\x80\x99re asking about me, I think it started with taking full responsibility for my missteps. I paid a huge price: the longest suspension in the history of M.L.B. for P.E.D. use. And while I was away, I took that year to reflect. I wanted to understand why I kept shooting myself in the foot. I wish it was in the foot, actually.'
b'What understanding did you arrive at? I\xe2\x80\x99m still a work in progress, but one thing I learned was that I was good enough. I did not need to overreach. And when I turned the lens inward, I found this incredible amount of gratitude and appreciation and respect for others and myself in a way that perhaps was not there in the past. With that attitude, I was able to enjoy life better. It made me a nicer person to be around; it made me a better father.'
b'Before making the personal realizations you\xe2\x80\x99ve described, how distorting was fame to your self-conception and decision-making?  I went to my high school prom, and several months later I was playing at Fenway Park. I was good enough physically to be there, but mentally, I was still in high school. I never make excuses for myself, but not benefiting from being on a college campus for four years and having the time to evolve \xe2\x80\x94 I lost my way somewhere along the line.'
b'How aware were you of any emotional disconnects in the moment? You know when something doesn\xe2\x80\x99t feel right. What you find is that \xe2\x80\x94 and I\xe2\x80\x99ve never thought about it this way before \xe2\x80\x94 you suppress that voice that\xe2\x80\x99s telling you not to do the wrong thing.'
b'This is maybe a shot in the dark, but did the suspension really cause this 180-degree epiphany for you? Or was it maybe more that it \xe2\x80\x94 and its aftermath \xe2\x80\x94 gave you a way of understanding your own story that allowed you to move forward emotionally and publicly? Well, when the suspension first happened, I was pissed off at everyone. I was blaming everyone. It wasn\xe2\x80\x99t until I got deeper into it that I said: No, it\xe2\x80\x99s not their fault. It\xe2\x80\x99s your fault.'
b'Were you in therapy at the time? That\xe2\x80\x99s when I got into it.'
b'Is there any culture of therapy in major-league baseball? What\xe2\x80\x99s more common in baseball is performance coaches. That\xe2\x80\x99s totally different than deep therapy, which is serious business. It was the hardest thing I\xe2\x80\x99ve ever had to do. In many ways, it\xe2\x80\x99s rewiring the brain.'
b'Before your suspension, did you or your advisers ever discuss just coming clean about P.E.D.s? Or was the strategy always deny, deny, deny? This part, I want you to make sure that we\xe2\x80\x99re superclear. Because I want this to be a story that\xe2\x80\x99s about the facts, and it\xe2\x80\x99s not me trying to [expletive] you. I think I didn\xe2\x80\x99t have the tools that I have today. Let\xe2\x80\x99s go to the next one, David, and we\xe2\x80\x99ll come back to this, because that\xe2\x80\x99s real important. I want to make sure that I address that in a clear way.'
b'How consciously, as you\xe2\x80\x99ve transitioned out of playing, have you tried to build a new brand or persona for yourself? Today I showed up here with you, and I didn\xe2\x80\x99t know anything you\xe2\x80\x99d want to talk to me about, and I\xe2\x80\x99d rather have it be that way. Before, I would have studied for six months before sitting down with you. I wanted to be more buttoned-up and have done due diligence and seen what your angle was. Now I just trust we\xe2\x80\x99re going to have a good conversation, and I go for it.'
b'What persona or brand were you trying to build back then? Robotic, tough. Very serious.'
b'How did that Details photo shoot where you were kissing your reflection in a mirror fit in with that image? I cringe at that.5 We were ending the photo shoot, and I wanted to run out of there. I think Steven Klein was the photographer, and he was like, Let\xe2\x80\x99s just shoot one more. And I\xe2\x80\x99m like, What? I just want to eat a burger. Let me get out of here.'
b'Were burgers part of your diet back then? No, but I was probably starving. Yeah, I just kissed the mirror, not even thinking. But I did a lot of things like that. I took my shirt off at Central Park and decided to get sun in the middle of the day.6'
b'Knowing that people would see you and take photographs, right? In Central Park?'
b'Yes. No. Because you think you\xe2\x80\x99ll just do this for 15 to 20 minutes and get some sun. I\xe2\x80\x99m pale as hell. Again, even those situations, if I would have handled them with some levity and more humility, I would have defused the entire thing.'
b'There\xe2\x80\x99s that rumor about your having a portrait of yourself as a centaur. 100 percent not true. I wish it was true because it\xe2\x80\x99s such a cool story.'
b'What has Jennifer Lopez7 taught you about being a public figure? She\xe2\x80\x99s obviously skilled at it. I\xe2\x80\x99ve never met anyone who\xe2\x80\x99s more honest. She\xe2\x80\x99s so authentic and genuine. It was strange to see someone of such magnitude be so normal, be such a great mother and partner and friend. How can you be like this and then go perform in front of 80,000 people? But that\xe2\x80\x99s her superpower.'
b'Why has balancing your public and private selves in that way been more of a struggle for you? I don\xe2\x80\x99t know. I wish I did.'
b'How hard was the cultural transition from sports to business? There\xe2\x80\x99s financial language that\xe2\x80\x99s different, but in other ways, they\xe2\x80\x99re exactly the same. What you want to do is create a winning culture, where incentive packages are based on the team winning. If you\xe2\x80\x99re not careful and you put in the wrong incentive packages, you can create a culture where everyone is fighting for themselves. The same thing goes in baseball.'
b'There is that expectation in sports that players will sacrifice themselves for the benefit of the team. But if each professional athlete is his or her own business, aren\xe2\x80\x99t the personal incentives fundamentally at odds with the incentives of the team\xe2\x80\x99s management, who are rewarded for team performance? Or is the whole ethos of subsuming your individual self-interest into the team\xe2\x80\x99s a bunch of romantic horse crap perpetuated by those who have a vested interest in athletes\xe2\x80\x99 continuing to think that way?8 Look, I played for 22 years and won one championship.9 Dan Marino and Charles Barkley \xe2\x80\x94 they didn\xe2\x80\x99t have championships, and to this day I know they hear the echoes. I feared that. So \xe2\x80\x9909 was an amazing experience, but the other half was relief. But I also had already made a small fortune. It\xe2\x80\x99d probably be different if you asked me when I hadn\xe2\x80\x99t signed my contract.10 Then that becomes a question of would you rather hit .330 and not win or .270 and win? That\xe2\x80\x99s where it gets a little tricky.'
b'Because that batting-average difference equates to a difference of millions of dollars in salary? Tens of millions. But there are unique players that are truly all about winning. Johnny Damon, Derek Jeter, Andy Pettitte, Dustin Pedroia.'
b'Do you include yourself on that list? I do. I do. I also had an incredible passion to be great. But yeah, probably I do. That\xe2\x80\x99s why I moved over to third base from shortstop. That\xe2\x80\x99s an example of putting the team ahead of myself.'
b'Your life as a baseball player was so regimented. Do you miss that structure? I have as predictable a schedule as I can, but nothing will be as predictable as a baseball season. I was in love with that structure. I had a list of my 10 things I had to do, and I would check it every night before I went to bed to see how many I\xe2\x80\x99d done. I was maniacal about my work ethic. When I was about 19 years old, I played with a guy by the name of Joey Cora.11 He\xe2\x80\x99s 5-foot-7 on a good day, he had knee problems and I saw him arriving at the stadium at 11 in the morning for a 7 o\xe2\x80\x99clock game. I saw the way he took care of his body \xe2\x80\x94 all the work he did to get ready to play. And here I was a young shortstop hitting .358. I\xe2\x80\x99m going down the stretch competing for the M.V.P., and nothing hurt. I felt like I could rip through a wall, and the wall would hurt, right? God, those were the good old days. But I remember sitting down and watching Joey Cora, and I\xe2\x80\x99m like, His body hurts. He doesn\xe2\x80\x99t complain. He just gets to the clubhouse earlier and earlier. And I said, If I can take my God-given ability and have his type of hunger and desire, I\xe2\x80\x99ll take my chances.'
b'Do you still have a checklist you look at every night? I do. I\xe2\x80\x99m old school. I remember things better if I write them out. The other day, Jennifer said something brilliant at, like, 2 in the morning. I reached over to get my notebook, and everything falls on the floor. Then I grabbed it and wrote it down.'
b'What\xe2\x80\x99d she say? It was about Mariano Rivera. She said, \xe2\x80\x9cMo getting 100 percent12 tells you more about his greatness off the field than it does on the field.\xe2\x80\x9d I thought, That\xe2\x80\x99s so true. I played with him all these years, and I couldn\xe2\x80\x99t have come up with that.'
b'When you were playing, did you ever see another player and think he was better than you? If you take away my first year and my last season, I don\xe2\x80\x99t think I ever saw that.'
b'Would the answer be different if you\xe2\x80\x99d played against Barry Bonds? I played against Barry. Interleague.'
b'Do you look up to anyone in the business world the way, as a kid, you looked up to, say, Cal Ripken? Think about what Jamie Dimon has done at J.P. Morgan. Barry Sternlicht at Starwood. Jon Gray at Blackstone. Obviously, our Babe Ruth is Warren Buffett.'
b'Buffett\xe2\x80\x99s philanthropy is impressive. My passion in giving back is for education. I\xe2\x80\x99ve had an opportunity to co-teach a class at Stanford Business School.'
b'What was the class? Reputation management.'
b'Was the key lesson authenticity? That was definitely up there. And not being afraid of pivoting.'
b'Something a shortstop is good at. How did getting rich at a young age change your relationships with the people around you? You have a young kid who learned how to play baseball at the Boys & Girls Clubs. Then you climb through the system, you become the No. 1 draft pick. You bypass college. At 21, you get over $10 million in a contract, which is crazy. Then you get a contract that breaks the all-time record in sports. Usually journeys have an arc of many years, but this all happened to me in seven or eight years after high school. So it was a culture shock for me and those around me. There\xe2\x80\x99s no preparation for it.'
b'What were the effects of that culture shock? People around you think that you have all that cash. Whatever they read in the paper you signed for, they feel like someone came in a Brink\xe2\x80\x99s truck and dumped all the money in your garage. And for whatever reason, some people think, Where\xe2\x80\x99s my cut? When that doesn\xe2\x80\x99t happen for them, it can grow into resentment and disappointment.'
b'Let\xe2\x80\x99s revisit the question I was asking earlier. Before being suspended, was the idea of coming clean about P.E.D.s ever discussed? I\xe2\x80\x99ve taken the position of just owning everything. At some point, and maybe it\xe2\x80\x99s in the future, I feel like this is an answer I would like to give on-camera because I think people have to see my sincerity. I\xe2\x80\x99m giving it to you straight because I respect you and I don\xe2\x80\x99t want you to think that I\xe2\x80\x99m [expletive] you in any way. So that\xe2\x80\x99s why I\xe2\x80\x99d rather step away and say, \xe2\x80\x9cDavid, I\xe2\x80\x99d rather not answer that because I\xe2\x80\x99m not ready to give that truth yet.\xe2\x80\x9d Does that make sense?'
b'I think I understand what you\xe2\x80\x99re saying. What\xe2\x80\x99s the one piece of advice you have for other athletes trying to transition into business? You have to find people that are experienced, conservative, have alignment with you and have a moral compass. There are so many pitfalls along the way, and if someone doesn\xe2\x80\x99t have a moral compass, there\xe2\x80\x99ll be trouble.'
b'David Marchese is the Magazine\xe2\x80\x99s Talk columnist.'

b'Whenever Major League Baseball opens a season in Japan, count on the Oakland Athletics to show up. The regular season will start at the Tokyo Dome for the fifth time on Wednesday, and this is the third time in a row that the A\xe2\x80\x99s will be there.'
b'They are never the main draw, but they love it.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s cool how baseball is such a big part of their culture,\xe2\x80\x9d outfielder Stephen Piscotty said in Mesa, Ariz., a few days before the A\xe2\x80\x99s left spring training. \xe2\x80\x9cI can\xe2\x80\x99t wait. I was just so fired up when I heard we were going.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The A\xe2\x80\x99s are there, essentially, because the Seattle Mariners and Ichiro Suzuki need an opponent. The Mariners abruptly ended Suzuki\xe2\x80\x99s season last May after 15 lackluster games, but he will be active on Wednesday and Thursday in games that will start at 5:35 a.m. Eastern, and hoping to add to his career hits total of 4,367 in the majors and Japan.'
b'Oakland, meanwhile, is hoping to stage a revival of 2012, when its visit here began an improbable run to a division title \xe2\x80\x94 and a three-year playoff streak. The A\xe2\x80\x99s faced Seattle to begin that season and opened with the Boston Red Sox in Tokyo in 2008.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt gets you even closer,\xe2\x80\x9d Manager Bob Melvin said of the season-opening trip. \xe2\x80\x9cWe have some new guys here this year but we do have a core group that\xe2\x80\x99s been together, came up through the minor leagues together, has won together. All that plays, and there\xe2\x80\x99s value in that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The A\xe2\x80\x99s talk a lot about intangibles, which might seem odd for the team most responsible for the analytics wave that has washed across the game this century. But they improved to 97 wins last season, from 75 in 2017, so hear them out. The path to their improbable wild-card berth, closer Blake Treinen said, started with a selfless attitude.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhen everybody does that, a beautiful thing happens, and that\xe2\x80\x99s what happened with us last year,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI mean, nobody even guessed 80 wins. Nobody guessed 75, probably. You can stack everything up into analytics if you want, and there\xe2\x80\x99s a place for it, but there\xe2\x80\x99s also a place for heart.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Heart, yes \xe2\x80\x94 but Oakland\xe2\x80\x99s formula also includes home runs, stingy relief pitching and, especially, stellar defense from Matt Chapman and Matt Olson, cornerstones on the corners. Olson won a Gold Glove at first base and Chapman won it at third base, while adding a Platinum Glove for best overall fielder in the American League.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI haven\xe2\x80\x99t got it yet; I think they present it during the year and then you get to take it home,\xe2\x80\x9d said Chapman, 25. \xe2\x80\x9cBut I don\xe2\x80\x99t have a house, so it\xe2\x80\x99s going to go in my parents\xe2\x80\x99 front room, probably. They\xe2\x80\x99ll probably put the Gold Glove and the Platinum Glove in their house, and hopefully some more to come.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Last season was Chapman\xe2\x80\x99s first full year in the majors \xe2\x80\x94 except for a one-game injury rehabilitation assignment \xe2\x80\x94 as it was for Olson, who was the only A.L. player to appear in all 162 games.'
b'Olson\xe2\x80\x99s agility and long levers \xe2\x80\x94 he is 6 feet 5 inches \xe2\x80\x94 were a big help for Chapman and shortstop Marcus Semien. A reliable first baseman is perhaps more important for the A\xe2\x80\x99s than for any other team because their ballpark has the most foul territory in the majors, and a throw that skips past Olson would typically result in two extra bases.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI can\xe2\x80\x99t tell you how many times he saved an on-the-run play I made that I threw up the line, or he dug out,\xe2\x80\x9d Chapman said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s like 10 feet tall on the bag, but then he\xe2\x80\x99ll pick anything and go in the line; he\xe2\x80\x99s not afraid to sacrifice his body. I\xe2\x80\x99m thankful for him. I probably owe him some steak dinners, now that I think about it.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Only the Yankees and the Los Angeles Dodgers hit more homers last season than the A\xe2\x80\x99s, who bring back their top four home-run hitters: Khris Davis (the major-league leader with 48), Olson (29), Piscotty (27) and Chapman (24). But they added only Marco Estrada to a thin starting rotation, and Melvin would prefer not to use an opener, as he did in last fall\xe2\x80\x99s wild-card loss to the Yankees.'
b'That makes it essential for the A\xe2\x80\x99s to prevent runs with standout defense, and Chapman sets the standard.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s a freak athlete, to start,\xe2\x80\x9d Olson said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe gets to some things I had never seen before I played with him. He\xe2\x80\x99s consistent, he\xe2\x80\x99s hard-working. You can find him in batting practice every day, running himself tired taking ground balls. We always say he\xe2\x80\x99s like a dog, just out there having fun.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Chapman attended El Toro High School in Lake Forest, Calif., with Nolan Arenado of the Colorado Rockies, the perennial N.L. Gold Glove third baseman who is two years older. Both players were shortstops then, but Chapman said he closely followed top third basemen like Adrian Beltre, Evan Longoria and David Wright. To Melvin, Chapman already belongs in their class.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe arm strength, the ground that he covers, both on the ground and in the air \xe2\x80\x94 and at our ballpark, in the air is big, because it\xe2\x80\x99s down into the bullpen, it\xe2\x80\x99s over to the dugout,\xe2\x80\x9d Melvin said. \xe2\x80\x9cWith shifts, you put him at shortstop and you know he\xe2\x80\x99s going to cover the whole left side of the infield \xe2\x80\x94 and wants to cover the whole left side of the infield.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Added Melvin, who has played and managed in the majors for 25 seasons: \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t know that I\xe2\x80\x99ve been around as talented a defender as he is, probably ever.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Suzuki\xe2\x80\x99s return to the Mariners\xe2\x80\x99 active roster will command the most attention in the opening series, of course; he is 45 years old and a baseball treasure on two continents. But the most captivating, in-his-prime talent is probably Chapman, and the platinum glove so indispensable to his team.'

b'Eddie Rosario, the Minnesota Twins left fielder, can\xe2\x80\x99t remember the exact year, but he was a youth baseball player in his native Puerto Rico when he was given the choice of two jerseys: No. 21 or another number.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m not Roberto Clemente,\xe2\x80\x9d said Rosario, 27, who now wears one of the next-closest options, No. 20. \xe2\x80\x9cI can\xe2\x80\x99t wear that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'No. 21 is sacred in baseball, particularly to Puerto Ricans, because it was the longtime number of Clemente, the iconic player who hailed from the island. Even as a youngster in Guayama, Rosario knew of Clemente\xe2\x80\x99s importance, which led him to join the majority of Puerto Rican major leaguers in doing something that Major League Baseball hasn\xe2\x80\x99t: decline the use of No. 21 in an effort to essentially retire it.'
b'Of the 235 Puerto Rico-born players who have appeared in the major leagues since Clemente\xe2\x80\x99s death 47 years ago, only 16 have used No. 21 \xe2\x80\x94 and none in the past five seasons, according to Baseball Reference.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s very powerful,\xe2\x80\x9d said Luis Clemente, 52, one of Roberto Clemente\xe2\x80\x99s sons.'
b'In addition to Roberto Clemente\xe2\x80\x99s accomplishments on the field \xe2\x80\x94 a 15-time All-Star, 12-time Gold Glove Award winner, two-time World Series champion with the Pittsburgh Pirates and member of the 3,000-hit club \xe2\x80\x94 he was a fierce advocate for Latino players and against Jim Crow segregation. A year after he died in a plane crash on Dec. 31, 1972, while escorting earthquake relief from Puerto Rico to Nicaragua, Clemente became the first player from Latin America inducted into the Baseball Hall of Fame.'
b'On Monday and Tuesday, Major League Baseball celebrated Jackie Robinson, who broke the color barrier in baseball on April 15, 1947, by having every player wear his No. 42 jersey, which was retired in 1997 and remains the only one to receive that special honor by all 30 teams. Many Puerto Ricans believe the same M.L.B.-wide retirement should also go to Clemente, who also made his major league debut this week, on April 17, 1955.'
b'In the four decades since Clemente\xe2\x80\x99s death, there has been no shortage of movements, campaigns and petitions to retire No. 21. The argument is particularly strong now, as the percentage of Latino players has swelled to nearly 30 percent in the major leagues, and it is even higher in the minor leagues. M.L.B. has made greater efforts to honor the influence of Latinos in general, whether through TV commercials or the Ponle Acento (\xe2\x80\x9cPut an Accent on It\xe2\x80\x9d) campaign that has led to more authentic renderings of names on jerseys.'
b'At an event in San Juan, P.R., last year unveiling a memorial to Clemente, Gov. Ricardo A. Rossell\xc3\xb3 of Puerto Rico asked Commissioner Rob Manfred, who was also in attendance, to remove No. 21 from commission.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHis body of work speaks volumes, so I do think that, as Jackie Robinson represents greatness in baseball and so much more, so does Roberto Clemente, particularly for Latinos all over the world,\xe2\x80\x9d Rossell\xc3\xb3 said afterward. \xe2\x80\x9cSo I think it\xe2\x80\x99s the right time to retire No. 21.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b' Manfred has resisted the idea, saying that iconic players should be recognized in distinctive ways, and has repeatedly pointed to the prestigious Roberto Clemente Award, given annually to a player who embodies sportsmanship and community service, as M.L.B.\xe2\x80\x99s way of honoring Clemente. Manfred has called the award \xe2\x80\x9ctruly baseball\xe2\x80\x99s highest honor.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'With or without an official directive, many Puerto Rican players have essentially tried to retire the number themselves, passing up chances to use No. 21 throughout their lives. (Clemente\xe2\x80\x99s only major league team, the Pirates, retired No. 21.)'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNo Puerto Ricans will use the number because of Roberto Clemente,\xe2\x80\x9d Carlos Correa, 24, the Puerto Rican superstar shortstop of the Houston Astros who uses No. 1, said in Spanish. \xe2\x80\x9cThe way I see it: Roberto Clemente is a figure for Latinos just like Jackie Robinson was for African-Americans. Clemente didn\xe2\x80\x99t just break barriers but inspired other Latinos to get into baseball.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI never tried to use No. 21,\xe2\x80\x9d added his compatriot Edwin D\xc3\xadaz, 25, the Mets closer who uses No. 39. \xe2\x80\x9cThat is something where everybody can\xe2\x80\x99t use it.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Yadier Molina, the St. Louis Cardinals\xe2\x80\x99 star catcher, and Carlos Beltr\xc3\xa1n, a former star outfielder and current Yankees special adviser, have both won the Clemente Award, and the two Puerto Ricans have also steered away from using No. 21 during their careers.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou can use it to honor him or you can see it as something you don\xe2\x80\x99t want to touch, because the way he carried the No. 21 is hard for another player to do in the same way,\xe2\x80\x9d Beltr\xc3\xa1n said in Spanish. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s not impossible, but it\xe2\x80\x99ll be really hard. You\xe2\x80\x99ll always have that shadow of Clemente, and many players avoid using that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Clemente\xe2\x80\x99s legacy remains potent in Puerto Rico, where his likeness dots the island. Near a main entrance of Hiram Bithorn Stadium in San Juan, \xe2\x80\x9c#Retire21\xe2\x80\x9d is painted within a mural of a memorable Clemente image:  tipping his cap to the crowd at Three Rivers Stadium in Pittsburgh after notching the 3,000th and final hit of his career. In 2016, No. 21 was officially retired across the island, from the professional winter league named after Clemente down to the youth level.'
b'Not all players avoided the number. Outfielder Rub\xc3\xa9n Sierra, who spent most of his 20 major-league seasons with the Texas Rangers, and first baseman Carlos Delgado, who played 17 seasons, were among the few Puerto Rican-born players to wear No. 21 during their careers.'
b'Delgado said he used it in the minor leagues and for the 1996 season with the Toronto Blue Jays before turning it over to star pitcher Roger Clemens, a new acquisition and more senior player, in 1997. Delgado returned to No. 21 from 2006 through 2009, when he was with the Mets.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIn my case, the decision wasn\xe2\x80\x99t a hard one,\xe2\x80\x9d he said in Spanish in a phone interview. \xe2\x80\x9cI thought he was so important that this was a way to recognize him. I understand the other side of the coin, not using the number to honor him, but as long as you honor his memory and his career, I think it\xe2\x80\x99s O.K.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Even so, Delgado said he was in favor of retiring Clemente\xe2\x80\x99s number because his legacy was comparable to Robinson\xe2\x80\x99s. Delgado, who won the Clemente Award in 2006, said he wasn\xe2\x80\x99t sure why No. 21 hadn\xe2\x80\x99t been retired yet, but he wondered if M.L.B. might feel pressure to also retire a number of an illustrious player from Venezuela or the Dominican Republic, two countries that have produced many successful major leaguers.'
b'Luis Clemente, whose family has worked with M.L.B. on past initiatives involving his father and his legacy, has a different idea on honoring No. 21. He has advocated not only a number retirement but some sort of unique and visible recognition \xe2\x80\x94 such as a patch on the jersey or hat \xe2\x80\x94 to be worn by the previous year\xe2\x80\x99s Clemente Award winner; he hasn\xe2\x80\x99t had official talks with M.L.B. about the idea.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cMy uncle \xe2\x80\x94 my dad\xe2\x80\x99s only living brother \xe2\x80\x94 feels people will forget if they don\xe2\x80\x99t see the number,\xe2\x80\x9d Luis Clemente said. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t think that\xe2\x80\x99s necessarily true. But it has to go hand-in-hand\xe2\x80\x9d with a visible reminder.'
b'For now, so many current and former players have taken the matter into their own hands that to some, the issue is settled.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe recognize what he\xe2\x80\x99s done and we know that the number should be retired,\xe2\x80\x9d said Ricky Bones, 50, a former major league pitcher and coach from Guayama, P.R. \xe2\x80\x9cIn our hearts, it\xe2\x80\x99s retired.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'In search of a way to save his career, the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 newest reliever and his father built a pitching oasis uptown.'
b'Adam Ottavino, a former relief pitcher for the Colorado Rockies, warmed up last month at a facility he rents in Harlem from his father-in-law. He said it had helped him improve his velocity and cook up a devastating slider.CreditCreditMichael Owens for The New York Times'
b'Supported by'
b'By Matt Foley'
b'Photographs and Video by Michael Owens'
b'The ambient pop of a catcher\xe2\x80\x99s mitt greets you before you see the interior of the Lab. Inside the unmarked door on St. Nicholas Avenue in Harlem, past the canvas tarp blacking out the windows and around the ladder serving as a makeshift camera stand, awaits an 80-foot-long pitching mecca where the outside world quickly disappears. '
b'The hurried passers-by might think this place amiss, but the former shoe store two blocks from the Apollo Theater and beneath a Chuck E. Cheese\xe2\x80\x99s feels just right to the ballplayers who trek uptown to hone their craft. '
b'On a Wednesday in January, that group included Adam Ottavino, the facility\xe2\x80\x99s gatekeeper, host and a major league reliever for the past seven seasons; four minor league pitchers; and one Baruch College catcher. Ottavino\xe2\x80\x99s father, John, an actor based in Brooklyn, is also there.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThese guys are just a bunch of big kids,\xe2\x80\x9d said the older Ottavino, gesturing to the men aged 22 to 33. \xe2\x80\x9cI come in and clean the place once a week. If they can\xe2\x80\x99t find something, I usually know where it is.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'On this day, that meant finding a misplaced blue lacrosse ball that his son uses for warm-up exercises. On any other Wednesday, Adam Ottavino would be throwing off the portable pitching mound, but on the eve of the day his life would change, there was a bit too much at stake.'
b' \xe2\x80\x9cSomething good might be happening soon,\xe2\x80\x9d a coy Ottavino told the five fellow ballplayers who hope to follow in his footsteps. \xe2\x80\x9cI can\xe2\x80\x99t get injured today.\xe2\x80\x9d '
b'The next day, Jan. 17, Ottavino, a 33-year-old right-hander from Park Slope, completed a three-year, $27 million contract with the Yankees.'
b'At the Lab, Ottavino sat behind a laptop and a tripod, filming his friends with a small, blue 3,350-frame-per-second camera and giving advice between pitches. The cameras are part of the data-driven pursuit with which Ottavino has saved his career. Now, after a breakout 2018 season with the Colorado Rockies, he\xe2\x80\x99s spreading the word as he prepares for spring training, which opens Thursday. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou learn things in here, about preparation and practice, that you didn\xe2\x80\x99t even expect to pick up,\xe2\x80\x9d said Alex Katz, a St. John\xe2\x80\x99s alumnus now in the Chicago White Sox organization. When Katz finished throwing, one of the Lab\xe2\x80\x99s most loyal regulars, a 30-year-old left-hander named Andres Caceres, took the mound. A Queens native and veteran of independent leagues, Caceres is trying to perfect a cutter with tons of late movement.'
b' \xe2\x80\x9cWhatever it is, it\xe2\x80\x99s filthy,\xe2\x80\x9d said Ottavino, suggesting Caceres put more pressure on his pointer finger. '
b'Asked about his role as the veteran sage in a circle of peers still chasing their major league dreams, Ottavino was direct: He\xe2\x80\x99s no one\xe2\x80\x99s superior, nor has he cracked some magic code. Rather, he is still searching for ways to improve.'
b' \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t ever want to be the guy who\xe2\x80\x99s always telling people what they\xe2\x80\x99re doing right or wrong,\xe2\x80\x9d Ottavino said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut if I do have some insight, I try to be fair about sharing it and see if we can get each other better. I learn from these guys all the time.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'A die-hard Yankees fan, Ottavino was at David Wells\xe2\x80\x99s perfect game in 1998 and attended the team\xe2\x80\x99s Fanfest annually with his father. Ottavino played ball at the Youth Service League in Brooklyn and graduated from Berkeley Carroll School in Park Slope in 2003. Three years later, he was drafted by the St. Louis Cardinals in the first round out of Northeastern University. '
b'He made his debut with the Cardinals in 2010 and was claimed off waivers by Colorado in 2012. After missing most of two seasons because of Tommy John surgery, Ottavino struggled mightily in 2017. He logged a 5.06 earned run average and 39 walks in 53 1/3 innings and was left off the playoff roster. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI knew the next year was do or die for my career,\xe2\x80\x9d Ottavino said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut that\xe2\x80\x99s the stuff I really enjoy \xe2\x80\x94 attacking the root of the problem. It\xe2\x80\x99s better that I hit rock bottom because I wasn\xe2\x80\x99t holding on to anything I\xe2\x80\x99d done before.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'A power pitcher with a dominant slider, Ottavino decided his command and consistency needed fixing. Having spent time at Driveline \xe2\x80\x94 a data-driven performance training center in Washington State \xe2\x80\x94 he determined that videotaping every practice session would be his answer, rather than making adjustments based on \xe2\x80\x9cfeel\xe2\x80\x9d or opinion. Fully committed to coaching himself, he bought two cameras \xe2\x80\x94 a Rapsodo to measure spin rate and a high-speed Edgertronic SC2 that compresses each pitch into a slow-motion replay. Then he worked to become more fluent in the data. '
b'The resulting knowledge, he said, helped establish a consistent foundation and led to increased confidence. The only problem? Ottavino had nowhere to do any of this. His off-season throwing partner, the Mets starter Steven Matz, had moved away, and daily trips to a facility on Long Island ate up too much time that could be spent with his wife and two toddlers. '
b'In stepped his father-in-law, a developer with a vacant Harlem storefront for rent. After Ottavino, with his father\xe2\x80\x99s help, spent two weeks laying turf, buying equipment and learning to use the cameras, the Lab was in session and the real fun began. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf he didn\xe2\x80\x99t have this place,\xe2\x80\x9d John Ottavino said, \xe2\x80\x9cit might have been over for him.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Ottavino was one of the best relievers in baseball last season with a 2.43 E.R.A. and a career-best 112 strikeouts to 36 walks in 77 2/3 innings. He held right-handed batters to a devastating .142 average and ranked 12th in the majors with 12.98 strikeouts per nine innings. He shut down a Chicago Cubs rally in the National League wild-card game last season, proving capable of getting postseason outs. Can he do it in the Bronx?'
b'Ottavino said the time spent hidden in Harlem \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9cscheming in an evil lair,\xe2\x80\x9d he joked \xe2\x80\x94 had prepared him for the challenge. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou want to show up to spring training with a secret weapon,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'The topic of pitching at Yankee Stadium has often been discussed. In December, he boasted on a podcast that he \xe2\x80\x9cwould strike Babe Ruth out every time\xe2\x80\x9d because players these days are so much better prepared physically. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf I have a slow start, I\xe2\x80\x99ll never hear the end of it,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'The Lab, in its current state, will close for good this month. Ottavino, Katz, Caceres and the other honorary members will report to their respective clubs with new tricks to unveil, hoping to rescue or advance however much career they have left. '
b'Ottavino, his wife and the children are moving to the suburbs, where he said he would find a suitable space in Westchester County for another lab. So long as it\xe2\x80\x99s hidden, preferably in a dark basement. Or maybe a wooded cabin.'

b"NEW YORK \xe2\x80\x94 Chicago White Sox shortstop Tim Anderson didn't go into detail Friday about what he said during a bench-clearing fracas with Kansas City earlier in the week after a report that he directed a racial slur at Royals pitcher Brad Keller."
b'Anderson was suspended one game for his actions Wednesday. Tempers flared after Keller hit Anderson, who had celebrated an earlier home run, with a fastball. Keller was penalized five games by Major League Baseball and is appealing.'
b'ESPN, citing unidentified sources , said Anderson, who is black, called Keller, who is white, the N-word during the fray.'
b"Anderson, the AL's top hitter this season, declined to discuss what was said on the field. He sat out Friday night's game at Detroit."
b"A person familiar with the penalty told The Associated Press that Anderson's suspension was the result of his language, which was included in the umpires' postgame report. The person spoke on condition of anonymity because that detail was not made public."
b'"We\'re going to keep moving forward," Anderson said. "That happened a couple days ago, so we\'re going to keep having fun and keep playing with a lot of energy and a lot of confidence."'
b"Anderson indicated he didn't think an appeal was worth it."
b'"I think that\'s too much," he said. "I really just take this one day and use it as an off day."'

b'"Timmy is a good kid and an outstanding baseball player and an emotional player, and I\'ll stand by Timmy," he said.'

b"LOS ANGELES \xe2\x80\x94 Vin Scully joined the widow of Jackie Robinson to honor the player who broke baseball's color barrier during Robinson's centennial birthday celebration Monday night."
b'Scully greeted 96-year-old Rachel Robinson with a kiss after being introduced to the crowd, with Scully drawing the loudest cheers in a rare public appearance.'
b"He stood behind Rachel with his hands holding her arms during the national anthem at Dodger Stadium. They were joined by Robinson's daughter, Sharon, and son, David, who linked arms with their mother as they walked on the field."
b'Robinson became the first black player in Major League Baseball with the Brooklyn Dodgers on April 15, 1947. Scully began calling the team\'s games three years later, and the now-retired Hall of Fame announcer was friendly off the field with the man he called "Jack."'
b'Only 7.7% of current MLB players are black, according to MLB.'
b'"If not for Jackie Robinson, I probably wouldn\'t be here today playing baseball in the United States," said Cincinnati Reds outfielder Yasiel Puig, who came from Cuba to chase his pro aspirations. "That\'s the reason we respect this day."'
b'Robinson, who died at age 53 in 1972, would have turned 100 on Jan. 31.'
b'His No. 42 was worn by every major leaguer Monday. The number was retired around the league in 1997.'
b'"For me, it\'s a big opportunity and responsibility that I hold very dear to my heart," Dodgers manager Dave Roberts said. "To put this uniform on today and wear that number today, 42, it\'s always special."'
b'Colorado Rockies manager Bud Black recalled reading about Robinson as a youngster.'
b'"To this day I still read about him," Black said in San Diego. "What a pioneer. What a great example of a human being and what he meant to our country, and in the bigger picture, what he meant for all of us culturally, not only in baseball, but in society."'
b'In Minnesota, Toronto Blue Jays manager Charlie Montoyo started his pregame media session at 3:42 p.m. CDT in honor of Robinson.'
b'"That\'s probably one of the people in baseball I wish I would\'ve met," he said.'
b'At Dodger Stadium, the pregame ceremonies included 42 current and former Jackie Robinson Foundation scholars. Students from Cleveland Elementary, Washington Middle School and John Muir High \xe2\x80\x94 all attended by Robinson while growing up in nearby Pasadena \xe2\x80\x94 were on hand.'
b"Robinson's No. 42 was cut into the center field grass."
b"The Robinson siblings each tossed out first pitches. David's was a strike to Roberts, while Sharon's bounced on its way to catcher Russell Martin."
b"Sharon Robinson works as MLB's education programming consultant."
b'The Dodgers hosted an invitation-only 100th birthday celebration in the Stadium Club featuring a sneak preview of the Jackie Robinson Museum, set to open in December in New York City.'
b'Dodgers closer Kenley Jansen and former Dodger Matt Kemp, now with the Reds, came out to home plate to pose with Scully and the Robinson family before the game.'
b"Missing from this year's LA ceremonies was Don Newcombe, the third black pitcher in the major leagues when he was with the Brooklyn and later Los Angeles Dodgers. He and Robinson were among the first four black players named to an All-Star team. Newcombe died in February at age 92."
b'Chicago White Sox shortstop Tim Anderson hosted more than 75 kids for a screening of the Robinson biopic "42."'
b'"It\'s tough to watch it," Anderson said. "But it\'s brave on his part, for him to be that guy to go through that and just be a leader and basically break the barrier. A guy that I look up to and a guy that motivates me."'
b'The Seattle Mariners visited the Negro Leagues Baseball Museum in Kansas City on a recent road trip.'
b'"It takes a special person, a special man to go about it, to take as much backlash as he did and still did that in a professional manner," Mariners infielder Tim Beckham said. "It speaks a lot about Jackie Robinson."'
b'Major league players made a $100,000 grant to the Jackie Robinson Foundation in honor of his 100th birthday. It helps fund the college scholarship program run by the foundation, which was founded by Rachel Robinson.'

b'By Tyler Kepner'
b'SARASOTA, Fla. \xe2\x80\x94 The Baltimore Orioles won the first World Series of Mike Elias\xe2\x80\x99s lifetime in 1983, when he was 9 months old. They have not been back since.'
b'Elias, Baltimore\xe2\x80\x99s new general manager, grew up in Northern Virginia and remembers watching the Orioles at Camden Yards in the mid-1990s. Those teams were stuffed with future Hall of Famers \xe2\x80\x94 Cal Ripken Jr., Mike Mussina, Roberto Alomar \xe2\x80\x94 and twice made deep playoff runs.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI just remember you felt so close to the field, and the stadium was packed to the brim, and the passion of the town and the fan base was on full display,\xe2\x80\x9d Elias said on Thursday in his office at Ed Smith Stadium. \xe2\x80\x9cEven today, I can see how important this team is to the city and what a baseball city it is. The fan base is engaged and educated in a way you don\xe2\x80\x99t get in every market.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Last season, though, those fans stayed away from Camden Yards like never before. The Orioles, who ranked first or second in the American League in attendance from 1992 through 2000, were 14th last season, ahead of only Tampa Bay. Their average crowd size dropped below 20,000 per game as the Orioles went 47-115, a mind-bending 61 games behind the Boston Red Sox. No team had finished so far out of first place in 76 years.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou\xe2\x80\x99d be foolish to flush it away and not at least attempt to try to take something away from it,\xe2\x80\x9d first baseman Chris Davis said. \xe2\x80\x9cYou learn the most when you struggle and face challenges.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Davis, whose .168 average last year was the lowest ever for a player with at least 500 plate appearances, said he learned to be more open with teammates, to not let his frustration fester. The Orioles\xe2\x80\x99 owners learned it was time to finally rebuild, and Elias was the natural choice as the architect.'
b'Elias, who replaced Dan Duquette, was most recently the assistant general manager for the Houston Astros. He joined the Astros before the 2012 season, when they were the majors\xe2\x80\x99 worst team, and helped build them into champions. A former pitcher at Yale, Elias also helped the St. Louis Cardinals win a title while serving in a variety of scouting jobs.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cMike has the benefit of having seen two different, successful models that have both gone through a lot of transformation,\xe2\x80\x9d said Astros General Manager Jeff Luhnow, who was Elias\xe2\x80\x99s boss in St. Louis and Houston. \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s going to be able to identify, in a way that others might not be able to, what the Orioles actually need to do to be consistently good again.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In Baltimore, Elias faces two of the same problems he and Luhnow inherited in Houston: A struggling farm system and the absence of an analytics department. Some teams, like the Red Sox, employ a research and development staff of 15 or more people. The Orioles had no analysts until Elias brought Sig Mejdal from Houston as his assistant general manager for analytics.'
b'Mejdal, a former NASA researcher, thrives in baseball start-ups: He built the Cardinals\xe2\x80\x99 analytics department in the mid-2000s, when few teams besides the Oakland Athletics valued new metrics, and then joined the Astros with Luhnow and did it there, too.'
b'The success of those organizations, and others, makes it harder to exploit inefficiencies, and the Orioles\xe2\x80\x99 division rivals \xe2\x80\x94 the wealthy Red Sox and Yankees, plus the Tampa Bay Rays and the Toronto Blue Jays \xe2\x80\x94 are all committed to data. With other losing teams also tearing down, this is the most challenging project yet for Elias and Mejdal.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cBaseball is a lot different now than it was just seven years ago when we went to Houston,\xe2\x80\x9d Mejdal said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re in a division with some of the richest and most innovative teams in baseball, so simply bringing in better processes is not going to ensure a division title. If we do want to win one or a few, this is a mandatory change in the current environment.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Orioles are far from hopeless. They have not won a game beyond the divisional round since 1997, but they had the American League\xe2\x80\x99s best record from 2012 through 2016, reaching the postseason three times. The trick is sustaining a winner, and for that model, Elias cites the Cardinals, a mid-market franchise with 12 playoff appearances \xe2\x80\x94 and only one losing record \xe2\x80\x94 in the 2000s.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThey have done such a great job of not overextending themselves, or painting themselves into a corner,\xe2\x80\x9d Elias said. \xe2\x80\x9cYou have to make some difficult decisions and make your decisions well, which is a challenge on us as a front office, but it is possible to maintain a long, competitive state by having a quality organization, drafting well, making shrewd decisions, and not making emotional, irresponsible decisions when it comes to free agents or extensions.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'This year\xe2\x80\x99s Orioles team might not post another .290 winning percentage \xe2\x80\x94 only one team in franchise history was worse, in 1939, when they were the St. Louis Browns \xe2\x80\x94 but expectations are low. Elias has signed only one major league free agent, pitcher Nathan Karns, who missed last season with an elbow injury. The top returning Oriole, by wins above replacement last season, is Richard Bleier, who pitched all of 32\xe2\x85\x94 innings.'
b'The Orioles\xe2\x80\x99 emphasis is clearly on the future \xe2\x80\x94 establishing a much stronger presence in Latin America, drafting first over all this June, adding staffers to a lean front office. The major league roster is in flux.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s an open competition in a lot of ways, in a lot of places \xe2\x80\x94 on the mound, on defense,\xe2\x80\x9d said Brandon Hyde, the Orioles\xe2\x80\x99 rookie manager. \xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s a lot of spots that are open, and open in a great way.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Hyde, 45, was another fitting hire, to replace Manager Buck Showalter. Hyde spent the last seven seasons with the Chicago Cubs, another team with a deliberate rebuild that worked. He was a minor league field coordinator, player-development director and major league coach for the Cubs, who revived a dormant franchise with smart trades and draft choices.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cA lot of those young guys came a lot faster than we thought, too,\xe2\x80\x9d Hyde said. \xe2\x80\x9cThe same thing with Houston.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Cubs, the Astros and the Cardinals now come to camp every spring training expecting to compete for a championship. That goal seems far off for the Orioles, but at least they have the right blueprint.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think we\xe2\x80\x99ll look back maybe a year or two from now and see what we had this year, and it\xe2\x80\x99ll be kind of a special moment to see what we\xe2\x80\x99ve become,\xe2\x80\x9d pitcher Dylan Bundy said. \xe2\x80\x9cYou\xe2\x80\x99ve got to start somewhere, and it starts this year.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'By James Wagner'
b'Luke Heimlich, the former Oregon State star who had failed to land a job in professional baseball after the revelation that he had pleaded guilty to sexually molesting his 6-year-old niece when he was 15, quietly made his pro debut in Mexico on Tuesday.'
b'Even after Heimlich signed a deal with the Tecolotes de los Dos Laredos of the Liga Mexicana de B\xc3\xa9isbol last month, it was unclear whether he would be permitted to play for them: The president of the Mexican league immediately cast doubt on the approval of the contract, citing Heimlich\xe2\x80\x99s past conduct and the message the league might send by employing him. As recently as Monday, The Laredo Morning Times reported that the team said it was awaiting clearance from the league to use Heimlich.'
b'But a day later, Heimlich, 23, was on the mound facing the Algodoneros Union Laguna at the Estadio de la Revoluci\xc3\xb3n in Torre\xc3\xb3n, Mexico. He allowed two runs in a five-inning start and struck out five batters.'
b'The league had actually informed the Tecolotes on Saturday that Heimlich\xe2\x80\x99s contract had been authorized, the Tecolotes owner Jos\xc3\xa9 Antonio Mansur said in a phone interview on Wednesday. The league president, Javier Salinas, had not responded to repeated requests for comment since Saturday, when a line in the league\xe2\x80\x99s official transactions stated that Heimlich had been assigned to the Tecolotes. On Friday, Salinas had said in a message on WhatsApp that a decision on Heimlich\xe2\x80\x99s contract had not yet been made.'
b'Salinas had questioned the move when Heimlich signed with the Tecolotes in March, saying he had to \xe2\x80\x9cprotect the image of the league.\xe2\x80\x9d The team said it was attracted to Heimlich because of his low-90s fastball as a left-hander, and said it felt he deserved a chance at a pro career after serving his legal penalty. But the signing drew criticism from the victim\xe2\x80\x99s family, and Salinas indicated the league would have to closely examine it.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe player has to have irreproachable conduct and be a good representative of the team and the league,\xe2\x80\x9d he said last month. \xe2\x80\x9cLike any league, we have to verify that all of our entrants have good conduct. We are an example to a lot of boys and girls.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Tecolotes, who have an unusual arrangement with home stadiums on both sides of the U.S.-Mexico border, were the second professional team to sign Heimlich. In August, the Lamigo Monkeys in Taiwan reached a deal with the pitcher, but after public outcry, the Chinese Professional Baseball League declared that he could not play there because of his criminal background and the potential effect on the league\xe2\x80\x99s image.'
b'All 30 major league teams passed on drafting or signing Heimlich, although all were allowed to do so.'
b'Last May, in an interview with The New York Times, Heimlich denied that he had committed the crime he admitted to, saying he had pleaded guilty to quickly dispense with the case and for the sake of the family. The victim\xe2\x80\x99s mother, whose name is being withheld to protect her daughter\xe2\x80\x99s identity, has maintained that the girl\xe2\x80\x99s account is truthful.'
b'As part of a plea deal, reached when Heimlich was 16, one of two charges was dropped. He was placed on two years\xe2\x80\x99 probation, took court-ordered classes, wrote a letter apologizing to his niece and was forced to register for five years as a Level 1 sex offender, a designation the State of Washington uses for someone considered of low risk to the community and unlikely to become a repeat offender. His juvenile records are sealed.'
b'Mansur, the Tecolotes\xe2\x80\x99 owner, said the team and the league had either spoken with Heimlich or requested paperwork regarding his case. Last month, the league, which is affiliated with Minor League Baseball and is considered Class AAA, even took the unusual step of asking Heimlich to sign a letter vowing good behavior.'
b'When city officials in Laredo, Tex., learned of Heimlich\xe2\x80\x99s signing, they sent letters to the team notifying them of a city ordinance that prohibits sex offenders at city parks and Uni-Trade Stadium, where the Tecolotes play in Texas. The team provided records from Oregon that showed Heimlich no longer needed to register as a sex offender because his juvenile conviction was expunged, said Rafael Benavides, a spokesman for the city of Laredo.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cOur Laredo Police Department also confirmed that the player\xe2\x80\x99s background check reflects no conviction criminal history information in the Washington State Patrol files,\xe2\x80\x9d Benavides said in a statement. \xe2\x80\x9cAs it stands, the player is not required to register with the State of Texas and has an affirmative defense under our city ordinance.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Heimlich would have his first chance to play in Texas next week when the Tecolotes return from a road trip.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere is nothing that could have prevented him from signing in the league,\xe2\x80\x9d Mansur said in Spanish, adding, \xe2\x80\x9cin reality, I hope the past is left behind for the future.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'On Baseball'
b'By Tyler Kepner'
b'The Oakland Athletics were overjoyed to choose Kyler Murray with the ninth pick in the baseball draft last June.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe just don\xe2\x80\x99t see athletes like this on the baseball field very often,\xe2\x80\x9d their scouting director, Eric Kubota, said then, praising Murray\xe2\x80\x99s instincts despite his relative lack of baseball experience. \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s just a tremendous athlete, which can translate to the baseball field in a lot of ways. He has a chance to really be dominant on both the offensive end and from a defensive standpoint.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Kubota said the risk of Murray\xe2\x80\x99s playing quarterback at the University of Oklahoma was worth taking.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cFrankly, we\xe2\x80\x99re kind of excited to be an Oklahoma fan for 12 games,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'Everybody knows what happened next. Those 12 regular-season games led to the conference title game and the Orange Bowl, and by the end, Murray had more than 5,000 all-purpose yards, 54 overall touchdowns, a Heisman Trophy \xe2\x80\x94 and a new career path.'
b'Murray announced via Twitter on Monday that he was \xe2\x80\x9cfirmly and fully committing my life and time to becoming an N.F.L. quarterback.\xe2\x80\x9d His statement made no mention of baseball, the A\xe2\x80\x99s, or the $4.6 million deal he reached with them last June, with the promise to play only baseball after the 2018 college football season.'
b'The A\xe2\x80\x99s were the first team to hold formal workouts for pitchers and catchers on Monday \xe2\x80\x94 they started earlier than other teams, to prepare for a season-opening series in Japan with the Seattle Mariners on March 20 and 21 \xe2\x80\x94 and Murray will not be joining them. He will return $1.29 million of his $1.5 million signing bonus, according to ESPN, and will not collect the remaining $3.16 million that he was due to be paid next month.'
b'He had been assigned a locker in the clubhouse, and on Monday morning, Oakland officials had expressed hope that Murray would soon slip into his No. 73 jersey.'
b'Bob Melvin, the A\xe2\x80\x99s manager, said he was \xe2\x80\x9ccautiously optimistic\xe2\x80\x9d that Murray would choose baseball, according to the San Francisco Chronicle. Yet, realistically, those hopes had been dimming since Murray declared for the N.F.L. draft on Jan. 14. The A\xe2\x80\x99s retain his rights should Murray ever reconsider, but they will get no compensation pick for his defection. They gambled and lost \xe2\x80\x94 but baseball lost even bigger.'
b'Murray teased the possibility of playing both sports in a photo he posted to Twitter in November, re-enacting a ubiquitous Bo Jackson photo from the 1980s by posing shirtless with football pads on his shoulders and a baseball bat behind his back.'
b'But Jackson, of course, did not play quarterback, an all-consuming position that leaves no room for distraction. To maximize his appeal to teams \xe2\x80\x94 and his potential for success \xe2\x80\x94 Murray chose football exclusively, which most likely will bring him more money, at least at first, and definitely offers a quicker path to glory.'
b'The sports are fundamentally different in their development processes, of course. Almost every baseball player logs years in the minors, riding buses to remote outposts for a punishing daily test that is at least as much mental as physical. A first-round N.F.L. quarterback is typically hailed as the instant savior of his franchise.'
b'Murray\xe2\x80\x99s predecessor as Heisman Trophy winner and Oklahoma quarterback, Baker Mayfield, needed one month to establish himself as the starter for the Cleveland Browns. He sat the first two weeks, came off the bench in Week 3 and was starting for good by Sept. 30. What\xe2\x80\x99s more appealing to a 21-year-old athlete: the Mayfield plan, or a summer trying to hit sliders for an A\xe2\x80\x99s affiliate in Beloit, Wis., or Stockton, Calif.?'
b'Murray\xe2\x80\x99s uncle, Calvin Murray, offers an example of the uncertainties of life as a baseball prospect. The San Francisco Giants chose Calvin Murray with the seventh overall pick in the 1992 draft. He played more than 1,600 professional games, but fewer than 300 in the majors. The player taken one pick before Murray did just a bit better. His name was Derek Jeter.'
b'We\xe2\x80\x99ll probably never know what Kyler Murray could have been as a baseball player. He could always try the sport again if football fizzles, as Tim Tebow is doing with the Mets. But baseball, as an institution, does not give itself the best chance to attract an athlete like Murray, whose bonus potential was limited by the strict draft-slotting system instituted in 2012.'
b'The draft system has always incentivized losing, to some extent \xe2\x80\x94 in 2009 and 2010, the Washington Nationals plotted a new course by taking Stephen Strasburg and Bryce Harper first over all in consecutive drafts. But by awarding a fixed amount of bonus money to teams \xe2\x80\x94 with the worst team getting by far the largest allowance \xe2\x80\x94 the new rules have greatly encouraged protracted rebuilding.'
b'The Houston Astros understood this better than most, and became a perennial power by using the system to their advantage. They have spawned so many imitators that a record eight teams tallied 95 losses last season.'
b'The players\xe2\x80\x99 union has been dismayed by this trend, which has lessened demand \xe2\x80\x94 and therefore salaries \xe2\x80\x94 for veteran free agents. Murray\xe2\x80\x99s case shows another regrettable consequence. Perhaps if the A\xe2\x80\x99s had been able to offer more money to Murray last June, they could have kept him off the football field entirely.'
b'Instead, their $4.6 million bought only a half-measure, allowing Murray one final fling with an old flame. As it turns out, he fell truly, madly, deeply back in love. The A\xe2\x80\x99s get their ring back, but baseball is left at the altar.'

b'By Tyler Kepner'
b'PEORIA, Ariz. \xe2\x80\x94 Practice would not start for hours, but there was Randy Jones, the most durable pitcher in the sleepy half-century of the San Diego Padres, with his jersey buttoned all the way to the top. His floppy Rawlings glove, the very one he used in 1975, is older than General Manager A.J. Preller and Manager Andy Green. Jones has 100 career victories \xe2\x80\x94 plus another over throat cancer, two years ago \xe2\x80\x94 and seems eager for more.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m just so encouraged,\xe2\x80\x9d said Jones, 69, as he surveyed the Padres\xe2\x80\x99 locker room at the Peoria Sports Complex the other morning. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s so much more fun. The competition is real here \xe2\x80\x94 and there are expectations, which is what you need.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'After claiming one of the most prized free agents in Manny Machado this off-season, the Padres are facing something rare for their franchise: high expectations. They have lost more games than any other franchise since they started play in 1969, and have managed just 14 winning seasons, no championships and one lingering stereotype.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThat laid-back atmosphere of San Diego \xe2\x80\x94 these players have got to get beyond that; they\xe2\x80\x99ve got to stay focused,\xe2\x80\x9d said Jones, who won a Cy Young Award and holds the team record for starts and innings. \xe2\x80\x9cOver the 50 years I\xe2\x80\x99ve watched this organization, that might be a challenge, a little bit. It\xe2\x80\x99s just San Diego itself. Keeping that intensity, it takes a little more work in San Diego than maybe some other cities.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Intensity should not be a problem anymore. The Padres rocked the industry last month with the huge contract for Machado, 26, a slugger with two Gold Gloves at third base. The right side of their infield also arrived through free agency: first baseman Eric Hosmer, who signed last year, and second baseman Ian Kinsler. Those two have played in five World Series combined; they do not take losing well.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe don\xe2\x80\x99t play baseball games to develop, we play baseball games to win them,\xe2\x80\x9d said Kinsler, after hitting a homer, stealing a base and scoring twice in an exhibition victory on Thursday. \xe2\x80\x9cWe all play the game a certain way, and that\xe2\x80\x99s what we want to bring.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'So the Padres play with an edge now. They also might have a strong lineup \xe2\x80\x94 or at least a lineup that should not finish last in the National League in on-base percentage and first in strikeouts, as it did last year.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThis is a very real offense we have here,\xe2\x80\x9d left fielder Wil Myers said. \xe2\x80\x9cTwo years ago we had three Rule 5 guys, and now we have Manny Machado and Eric Hosmer. It\xe2\x80\x99s a completely different flip of what\xe2\x80\x99s happened here over the years, and it\xe2\x80\x99s exciting.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Even with all the offensive potential, the Padres still lack a modern-day Randy Jones. No current Padre worked more than 130 major-league innings last season. For all the money they invested in Machado, the Padres added only one starter in free agency: Garrett Richards, who had Tommy John surgery last summer and will probably not pitch this season, signed for two years and $15.5 million.'
b'Green and Preller said the Padres might be creative in how they allocate innings this season; they engineered a few shorter starts last year that seemed to work well. Four starters rank as consensus top-100 prospects \xe2\x80\x94 Logan Allen, MacKenzie Gore, Adrian Morejon and Chris Paddack \xe2\x80\x94 but only Allen has pitched above Class AA.'
b'Preller, who made his reputation as a sharp-eyed, aggressive scout, said his senior scouting advisers had raved about the Padres\xe2\x80\x99 pitching depth, reassuring him the organization was especially well-stocked.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThey\xe2\x80\x99d never seen as much pitching in one spot, in one system, at one time,\xe2\x80\x9d Preller said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re going to bank on those guys developing. We understand some guys may not reach their ceiling, but from our standpoint, when you have the numbers we feel like we\xe2\x80\x99re going to have, some guys are going to be better than we think they\xe2\x80\x99ll be, and they\xe2\x80\x99ll step up and take those spots. So we\xe2\x80\x99re going to give those guys an opportunity.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'As Preller spoke, on a patio above the practice fields, another young pitcher, Cal Quantrill, stopped by to chat excitedly about the action on his sinker. Quantrill has also been a top-100 prospect, like another Padres right-hander, Anderson Espinoza. Analysts adore the future Padres \xe2\x80\x94 Baseball America, ESPN, Fangraphs and MLB.com all rank San Diego\xe2\x80\x99s farm system as the best in the game.'
b'This is a source of pride for Preller, but only as a means to producing the kind of consistently competitive team San Diego has never had.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt definitely wasn\xe2\x80\x99t the goal of anyone in the organization to say, \xe2\x80\x98We\xe2\x80\x99ve got one of the better farm systems in the game,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI think what that enables you to do \xe2\x80\x94 from a trade standpoint, competition, depth, having answers if you have injuries \xe2\x80\x94 that\xe2\x80\x99s more important than looking up and saying, \xe2\x80\x98You\xe2\x80\x99ve got a farm system.\xe2\x80\x99 Fans want to see it at the major league level. Now our job is to try to convert that to major-league wins.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The thriving system was critical to affording the contracts of Machado, Hosmer and Myers, who will combine to earn $75.5 million each season from 2020 through 2022. The Padres expect high-impact, low-cost hitters to surround them, including shortstop Fernando Tatis Jr., right fielder Franmil Reyes and catcher Francisco Mejia.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhen we took over a few years ago, I thought it was going to take a few years to build it the right way,\xe2\x80\x9d said Preller, who joined the Padres in August 2014. \xe2\x80\x9cBut I think we\xe2\x80\x99re in position now to start being competitive as a club, and not just have it as a one-year blip \xe2\x80\x94 year in and year out, we\xe2\x80\x99ve got more answers than questions.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'For now, though, there are many more questions than answers. The Padres are still a last-place team trying to stop a string of eight consecutive losing seasons, the longest stretch of futility since the brown-and-gold beginnings of this woebegone franchise.'
b'The Padres \xe2\x80\x94 who will, at last, bring back their brown uniforms next season \xe2\x80\x94 have hope. Now they must justify it.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe haven\xe2\x80\x99t done enough to warrant being talked about,\xe2\x80\x9d Green said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut there\xe2\x80\x99s conviction in here that we\xe2\x80\x99re going to start doing some things. We\xe2\x80\x99ve got work to do to prove that.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'By David Waldstein and Brad Lefton'
b'Ichiro Suzuki, the unique and pioneering superstar who amassed 4,367 hits in 28 professional baseball seasons across two continents, announced his retirement on Thursday, concluding one of the most remarkable careers in the history of sports.'
b'Suzuki, who is destined for a place in the Hall of Fame, told his Seattle Mariners teammates the news in Japan before their regular-season game against the Oakland Athletics at the Tokyo Dome. The news filtered out to the crowd and around the world after the Kyodo News Service reported it during the game.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAfter nine years playing in Japan and entering my 19th season in America, I am announcing my retirement,\xe2\x80\x9d Suzuki said in Japanese after the game, at a ballroom packed with reporters in a hotel adjacent to the stadium. \xe2\x80\x9cI can\xe2\x80\x99t describe how fortunate I feel to have my career conclude in the uniform of the Seattle Mariners.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'A day after he had become the oldest position player to start a season-opening game in the American League, Suzuki started Thursday\xe2\x80\x99s game in right field and batted ninth. After going hitless in four at-bats, he took his position in right field to start the bottom of the eighth inning.'
b'Seattle Manager Scott Servais then came onto the field to make a lineup change. With that, the other eight Seattle players quickly retreated to the dugout, leaving Suzuki a vast, green pathway to the third base bench, and he jogged unobstructed to thunderous applause from the sellout crowd.'
b'Upon leaving the field for the last time, Suzuki received emotional embraces from each teammate in front of the dugout, including tearful ones from second baseman Dee Gordon and countryman Yusei Kikuchi, who grew up idolizing Suzuki and who had just made his debut as a starting pitcher in the major leagues.'
b'The biggest embrace awaited him inside the dugout. Ken Griffey Jr., a Hall of Famer and a beloved Mariners icon, made his way to the bench in street clothes to offer his support.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIchiro has had an unbelievable career,\xe2\x80\x9d Griffey said. \xe2\x80\x9cNot only in the U.S., but here in Japan. What he has done to cross barriers and bring countries together is unbelievable.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'[Keeping Score: Ichiro Suzuki Is Not Baseball\xe2\x80\x99s Hit King. He Is So Much More.]'
b'Kikuchi was barely 1 year old when Suzuki made his professional debut for the Orix BlueWave in 1992. Within two years, Suzuki had established his greatness, swatting 210 hits in 130 games in 1994 and flashing a level of speed and athleticism on the bases and in the outfield that major league scouts had rarely seen.'
b'Suzuki was long destined to become the first position player from Japan to play in Major League Baseball, and although he did not make it to the United States until he was 27, he still collected the 23rd-most hits in major league history.'
b'Bobby Valentine, the former Mets manager, faced Suzuki in Japan in 1995 as manager of the Chiba Lotte Marines. Before Suzuki joined the Mariners in 2001, Valentine, then with the Mets, called the outfielder one of the top five players in the world. But in that sensational rookie season, in which Suzuki batted .350 and became the second player to win the American League Rookie of the Year and Most Valuable Player Awards in the same season, Valentine corrected himself.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI was wrong,\xe2\x80\x9d Valentine said at the time. \xe2\x80\x9cHe is one of the top two.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Barry Bonds won the National League M.V.P. that year.'
b'Yankees General Manager Brian Cashman, who brought Suzuki to New York via a trade in 2012, issued a statement on Thursday calling him one of the greatest players in history.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe has been married to this game for virtually his entire life,\xe2\x80\x9d Cashman said in the statement, \xe2\x80\x9crefining and perfecting his craft \xe2\x80\x94 and the relationship has been a beautiful one.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Known for his strict regimens and year-round routine of stretching, conditioning and batting practice \xe2\x80\x94 he allowed himself only two days off in the winter \xe2\x80\x94 Suzuki had at least 200 hits in each of his first 10 major league seasons, including 2004, when he set a record with 262. He won two batting titles, was named to 10 All-Star teams and won 10 Gold Glove awards as he dazzled fans with his powerful and accurate arm from the outfield.'
b'In 2016, while playing for the Miami Marlins, Suzuki tripled for his 3,000th hit. In his 18 seasons in the United States, he compiled 3,089 hits.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cCompared to what I achieved today, records like 10 years of 200 hits are small,\xe2\x80\x9d Suzuki said Thursday after the Mariners\xe2\x80\x99 5-4 win in 12 innings. \xe2\x80\x9cTo think that I became inactive last May and despite no games to play in since then, I maintained my focus on coming back this season and was able to play in real games yesterday and today, that is truly something I am proud of. I\xe2\x80\x99m sure in time, my records will be broken, but I find it hard to believe anyone will achieve the level of focus I did on this goal since last May.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Suzuki was extremely meticulous as a player, carrying his specially made bats in a black dehumidifier case to ensure they maintained a precise weight and level of moisture. He had a carefully planned diet to preserve his wiry frame \xe2\x80\x94 though that often included cheeseburgers for lunch \xe2\x80\x94 and he tracked his weight by the half-pound. Everything in his routine was done for a purpose, and that usually meant getting hits in games.'
b'Suzuki was also recognized for his fashion sense, including some outlandish outfits that would have teammates gawking. He charmed many of them with his wily sense of humor and well-timed off-color expressions in English. He speaks his second language fluently, but he kept Turner, his interpreter, on hand to make certain his thoughts were always precisely conveyed.'
b'Toward the end of the 2014 season, his last one with the Yankees, he told his teammates that he wanted to play until he was 50. He got close, but after he joined the Mariners for a second stint in 2018, he played just 15 games before the team shut him down as a player. Ever the pioneer, he transitioned into a new role as a uniformed adviser who took batting practice but was not allowed on the bench.'
b'He continued to maintain his fitness and prepare for games as he always did as a player, knowing that with an expanded roster for this opening series in Japan, he would be given the chance to play in the first two games of 2019 in his home country.'
b'Suzuki was hitless in five at-bats and drew one walk in the two games against the A\xe2\x80\x99s in Japan, finishing his major league career with a .311 batting average and 1,420 runs scored over 2,653 games. As for his future plans, he said he could not envision himself coaching or managing at the professional level.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t have the patience for that,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI could, however, see myself doing something with kids or somehow trying to knock down the barriers that prevent professionals from working with amateurs in Japan.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'As for what he\xe2\x80\x99ll do in the immediate future?'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI definitely don\xe2\x80\x99t plan on taking it easy,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m not one to sit still. I\xe2\x80\x99m sure I\xe2\x80\x99ll do my usual training tomorrow.\xe2\x80\x9d'
