b'By Richard Goldstein'
b'Mel Stottlemyre, the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 pitching ace in their lean years of the late 1960s and early \xe2\x80\x9970s and later the longtime pitching coach for Mets and Yankees teams that won the World Series, died on Sunday in a Seattle hospital. He was 77.'
b'His wife, Jean Stottlemyre, said the cause was complications of multiple myeloma, a type of blood cancer for which he had been treated for many years. At his death he also had the flu and pneumonia, she said. Stottlemyre, who grew up in Washington State, lived in the Seattle area.'
b'Stottlemyre made his last visit to Yankee Stadium in June 2015, when the Yankees surprised him by dedicating a Monument Park plaque in his honor when he attended their annual Old-Timers\xe2\x80\x99 Day gathering. The tribute came after their former second baseman Willie Randolph received a plaque as scheduled.'
b'Stottlemyre, walking with the aid of a cane, told the crowd, \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s been a thrill over the years for me to wear this uniform.\xe2\x80\x9d He said that if it was to be his last Old-Timers\xe2\x80\x99 Day, he would \xe2\x80\x9cstart another baseball club, coaching up there, whenever they need me.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Arriving at Yankee Stadium in August 1964, Stottlemyre posted a 9-3 record while helping the Yankees win a fifth straight pennant. He then faced Bob Gibson, the St. Louis Cardinals\xe2\x80\x99 future Hall of Fame pitcher, three times in the World Series.'
b'The Yankees were beaten by the Cardinals in seven games, but Stottlemyre became an anchor of their pitching staff. In his 11 seasons with the Yankees, a long stretch of largely lean years after decades of dominance, he was one of their few bright spots. A right-hander featuring a superb sinkerball, he was a five-time All-Star and a three-time 20-game winner.'
b'Stottlemyre coached the Mets\xe2\x80\x99 pitchers for 10 seasons, including their 1986 World Series championship year, and the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 pitchers for another 10, during which he won four World Series championship rings. He was being treated for multiple myeloma, which affects plasma cells, for much of his time as the Yankees pitching coach.'
b'Stottlemyre was the quiet type, but even as a rookie pitcher he possessed uncommon poise.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHere\xe2\x80\x99s a 21-year-old kid nobody knew coming out of nowhere with this great arm and super control who has all the confidence \xe2\x80\x94 not a big head, mind you, but a quiet self-assurance \xe2\x80\x94 of a Whitey Ford,\xe2\x80\x9d his teammate Tom Tresh was quoted as saying in the oral history \xe2\x80\x9cBombers\xe2\x80\x9d (2002), by Richard Lally.'
b'Years later, Stottlemyre was admired by the pitchers he coached for his optimism and his ability to relate to them. The Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 David Cone once said that Stottlemyre anticipated how pitchers liked to be treated. Stottlemyre, in turn, said he had benefited from talking with his sons Todd and Mel Jr., both of whom pitched in the major leagues. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s like he never got older,\xe2\x80\x9d Cone said of Stottlemyre.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhen you\xe2\x80\x99re struggling, he\xe2\x80\x99s always there for you,\xe2\x80\x9d the relief pitcher Mariano Rivera told the New Jersey newspaper The Record in October 1998, after the Yankees defeated the San Diego Padres to begin their string of three straight World Series titles.'
b'Dwight Gooden remembered how Stottlemyre came to the mound and steadied him when he was two outs away from a no-hitter against the Seattle Mariners at Yankee Stadium in May 1996. Gooden had walked two batters and thrown a wild pitch to Jay Buhner, putting runners on second and third with the Yankees leading by 2-0.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s something about his demeanor \xe2\x80\x94 so trusting, so trustworthy \xe2\x80\x94 that makes you want to tell him the truth,\xe2\x80\x9d Gooden said in his memoir, \xe2\x80\x9cHeat\xe2\x80\x9d (1999), written with Bob Klapisch.'
b'Gooden recalled Stottlemyre using his nickname while telling him: \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m not taking you out, Doc. I\xe2\x80\x99m just here to give you a breather. This game is yours, Doc. Yours unless you tell me you can\xe2\x80\x99t go anymore.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'When Gooden insisted that he still had it, Stottlemyre told him, \xe2\x80\x9cGo get him.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Gooden struck out Buhner and got Paul Sorrento to pop up to Derek Jeter, the shortstop. The no-hitter was his.'
b'Stottlemyre\xe2\x80\x99s fellow coach Don Zimmer recalled that after Stottlemyre revealed he had multiple myeloma in April 2000, he remained strong and steady while coaching the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 pitchers for most of the regular season, even as he received chemotherapy.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe was a rock,\xe2\x80\x9d Zimmer said in \xe2\x80\x9cZim: A Baseball Life\xe2\x80\x9d (2001), written with Bill Madden.'
b'After a stem-cell transplant in September 2000, Stottlemyre could not return to the Yankees that season, since he risked contracting an infection. When the Yankees beat the Mets in the World Series, Zimmer called Stottlemyre at his home.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhen Mel answered the phone, he sounded ecstatic,\xe2\x80\x9d Zimmer remembered. \xe2\x80\x9cLater on that night, I found out that Mel\xe2\x80\x99s brother had died earlier in the day of a brain tumor. He never said a word about it on the phone because he didn\xe2\x80\x99t want to ruin the night for the rest of us. That\xe2\x80\x99s what kind of a person he is.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Melvin Leon Stottlemyre was born on Nov. 13, 1941, in Hazleton, Mo., and grew up in Mabton, Wash., the son of a construction worker. He was signed by the Yankee organization in 1961 out of what was then Yakima Valley Junior College (now Yakima Valley College) in Washington State.'
b'When Stottlemyre joined the Yankees, Ford, the Hall of Fame left-hander, became his mentor. When Ford hurt his shoulder pitching in the 1964 World Series opener, the Yankees rested much of their hopes on Stottlemyre. He beat Gibson in Game 2, pitched to a no-decision in Game 5 and was the loser in Game 7.'
b'The Yankees never returned to the World Series during Stottlemyre\xe2\x80\x99s playing career, but he became one of the American League\xe2\x80\x99s leading pitchers.'
b'He had a 20-9 record in 1965, when he led the A.L. in complete games, with 18, and innings pitched, with 291. The Yankees were beginning to fade by then, finishing sixth in what was then a 10-team league. Stottlemyre won 12 games and lost 20 in 1966 when they finished last for the first time since 1912. But he rebounded to go 21-12 in 1968 and 20-14 in 1969.'
b'In June 1974, while pitching against the California Angels, Stottlemyre tore his rotator cuff. Over the winter, he was advised by the Yankees to rest until at least May 1. When they released him at the end of spring training, he was stunned. The move was made by the team\xe2\x80\x99s general manager, Gabe Paul, but Stottlemyre was convinced that the Yankees owner George Steinbrenner had been behind it, and it left him embittered.'
b'Stottlemyre retired with a record of 164-139 and an earned run average of 2.97 before turning to a second career as a pitching coach. But a family tragedy took him away from baseball for a time and ultimately colored his already bittersweet feelings toward Yankees management.'
b'In March 1981, Stottlemyre\xe2\x80\x99s son Jason died of leukemia a few days after his 11th birthday. Stottlemyre left his post as a roving pitching instructor for the Mariners the next year to be with his family. Two decades later, reflecting on the possibility of a connection between his multiple myeloma and his son\xe2\x80\x99s leukemia, Stottlemyre thought back to radiation treatments he had received on his shoulder from the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 team doctor in the late 1960s as a means of reducing calcification. A radiologist had advised him to stop the treatments because of potential health consequences, and he eventually did so despite what he said were reassurances from the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 medical staff that the radiation would not harm him.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve become convinced it played a role in both of the diseases,\xe2\x80\x9d Stottlemyre said of the radiation in his memoir, \xe2\x80\x9cPride and Pinstripes\xe2\x80\x9d (2007), written with John Harper. \xe2\x80\x9cThe medical care the Yankees provided was not up to the standards you\xe2\x80\x99d expect in professional sports, and certainly not from one of the most successful sports franchises in history.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'After a break from baseball, Stottlemyre became the Mets\xe2\x80\x99 pitching coach in 1984, Gooden\xe2\x80\x99s rookie season. He did not tinker with the mechanics of the immensely gifted Gooden, but counseled him on how to handle the spotlight and saw himself as something of a father figure.'
b'When the Mets defeated the Boston Red Sox in the 1986 World Series, Stottlemyre oversaw an outstanding pitching staff featuring Gooden, Bob Ojeda, Sid Fernandez, Ron Darling, Roger McDowell and Jesse Orosco.'
b'Stottlemyre was fired at the end of the 1993 season and was the Houston Astros\xe2\x80\x99 pitching coach for two seasons before being asked by Steinbrenner to return to the Yankees. Stottlemyre had torn up invitations to the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 Old-Timers\xe2\x80\x99 Days for two decades in anger over what he considered the bad faith the team showed by releasing him in 1975. But he decided to accept the offer, joining the staff of the new Yankees manager, Joe Torre, when he came to believe that Paul, the general manager, not Steinbrenner, had been responsible for letting him go.'
b'The Yankees won the World Series in 1996, then captured consecutive championships from 1998 to 2000, the year Stottlemyre began treatments for multiple myeloma.'
b'Stottlemyre guided pitching staffs that included Cone, Rivera, Andy Pettitte, Roger Clemens, Mike Mussina, David Wells and Gooden, who was coming back from battles with drug abuse. Stottlemyre left the Yankees after the 2005 season and was replaced by Ron Guidry, their former star left-hander.'
b'Stottlemyre was the Mariners\xe2\x80\x99 pitching coach in 2008, but he was not retained when Don Wakamatsu replaced Jim Riggleman as manager the next season.'
b'In addition to his wife, the former Jean Mitchell, he is survived by a brother, Jeff; a sister, Joyce Lawerence; his sons, Mel Jr. and Todd; and eight grandchildren. Todd Stottlemyre pitched for 14 seasons in the major leagues. Mel Jr., who pitched for one season, became the Miami Marlins\xe2\x80\x99 pitching coach in December 2018 and had formerly been in that post for the Arizona Diamondbacks and the Mariners.'
b'By his last few seasons with the Yankees, Stottlemyre had cemented his reputation as an outstanding pitching coach. But his resentment of Steinbrenner resurfaced in the face of criticism from him when the team was unable to make it back to the World Series. Stottlemyre was also irked by what he saw as undue interference from Billy Connors, the Yankees pitching adviser who worked out of the team\xe2\x80\x99s facilities in Tampa, Fla., and was close to Steinbrenner. (Connors died last June at 76.)'
b'In an interview with USA Today in May 2005, Steinbrenner complained that Stottlemyre had not been improving the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 pitching staff. But Torre was quick to defend Stottlemyre, who had been alongside him on four championship teams. On Monday, Torre, in a statement, called Stottlemyre \xe2\x80\x9ca role model to us all and the toughest man I have ever met.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Because of an editing error, an earlier version of this obituary misstated the year USA Today published an interview George Steinbrenner. It was 2005, not 2015.'
b'Daniel E. Slotnik contributed reporting.'

b'BALTIMORE \xe2\x80\x94 As the longest-tenured Yankees player on their roster, Brett Gardner has gone through disappointing seasons, playoff years, World Series-title runs, and all the quirks that a 162-game campaign can offer. So when it comes to perspective, he may have the most.'
b'And even Gardner, 35, cannot recall a time, especially only a week into the season, that 11 of his teammates have been on the injured list.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cMan,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, pausing as he tied his cleats in the visitors\xe2\x80\x99 clubhouse at Camden Yards. \xe2\x80\x9cI can\xe2\x80\x99t tell you if there\xe2\x80\x99s been that many on the I.L. at once. But just as far as guys going down with something all within a few days of each other, it can be frustrating.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Between the suddenly packed trainers\xe2\x80\x99 room and the field, the start to the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 2019 season has been just that: frustrating. Among the preseason World Series favorites, the Yankees dropped the first two series of the year to the rebuilding Baltimore Orioles and Detroit Tigers, teams that lost a combined 213 games last year \xe2\x80\x94 and could easily top that total this season. The first two home runs of Aaron Judge\xe2\x80\x99s season and a go-ahead three-run blast by Clint Frazier in the eighth inning helped the Yankees overcome mistakes in a 6-4 win over the Orioles on Saturday, improving their record to 4-4.'
b'Eight games, of course, is just a blip in the baseball season, and the Yankees are not the only team expected to contend that has sputtered out of the gate: The defending champion Boston Red Sox started 2-8 thanks to pitching woes and mental mistakes; the Chicago Cubs are hitting but not pitching, which has led to a 2-6 start; the Houston Astros, the 2017 World Series winners, had scored just 24 runs, good for only a 4-5 record.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a very long season,\xe2\x80\x9d Gardner said before the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 win on Thursday. \xe2\x80\x9cIf you went 2-4 during a week sometime in May or June, it might not be a big deal. But when it\xe2\x80\x99s the first six games of the season, obviously it\xe2\x80\x99s all we have to judge ourselves at this point. Spring training is over.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'When the Yankees left their spring training home in Tampa, Fla., though, they already had an alarming number of key players recovering from injuries: shortstop Didi Gregorius (elbow surgery last year), relief pitcher Dellin Betances (right shoulder inflammation), outfielders Aaron Hicks (back stiffness) and Jacoby Ellsbury (hip surgery last year), and starting pitchers Luis Severino (right shoulder soreness) and C. C. Sabathia (off-season knee and heart operations).'
b'Since opening day, they have been joined on the I.L. by third baseman Miguel Andujar (torn right labrum), outfielder Giancarlo Stanton (left biceps strain) and shortstop Troy Tulowitzki (left calf strain). Altogether, that\xe2\x80\x99s 11 players and more than $87 million in 2019 salaries on the I.L. \xe2\x80\x94 more than the entire opening day payrolls of the Pittsburgh Pirates, Miami Marlins, Tampa Bay Rays and Orioles, according to Cot\xe2\x80\x99s Baseball Contracts.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s really been crazy,\xe2\x80\x9d Tulowitzki said, adding later, \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve never seen anything like it.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Injuries are inevitable during a long season, especially for a player like Tulowitzki \xe2\x80\x94 a 34-year-old returning from a year-and-a-half absence because he has been hurt. And even with their towering list of hobbled players, the Yankees can take some encouragement from recent history.'
b'The last major league team to have this many players on the I.L. six games into the season was the 2016 Los Angeles Dodgers, according to Nathan Currier of the injury-tracking site ManGamesLost.com. Buoyed by a deep, $250 million roster, the Dodgers went on to win the National League West and advance to the N.L. Championship Series that year despite setting a record with 28 players on the I.L.'
b'So, really, it could always be worse for the Yankees. At one point last June, the Los Angeles Angels had 15 players out with injury. And reinforcements are on the way: Sabathia, Betances and perhaps even Stanton are expected to return this month. Hicks is only now resuming baseball activities, so he could return closer to May, when Severino is also expected to be back. Andujar\xe2\x80\x99s injury is the most concerning for the team; if he does not respond well to rehabilitation, he could need season-ending surgery.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThose are some big pieces we\xe2\x80\x99re missing,\xe2\x80\x9d starting pitcher James Paxton said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99ll be great to get those guys back when we do get them back. But for right now, I\xe2\x80\x99m confident going into battle with the guys we have. We\xe2\x80\x99ve got some guys that are grinders.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Yankees were proud of their improved depth entering this season, having bolstered the pitching staff and added infielder D. J. LeMahieu, a Gold Glove-winning everyday second baseman with the Colorado Rockies who was signed to be a jack-of-all-trades bench player in New York. But the Yankees did not expect to reach so far into that depth this early. After Tulowitzki went down, the only healthy infielder on the 40-man roster to call up was Thairo Estrada, the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 19th-ranked prospect, who missed most of last season because he was shot in the right hip during a robbery attempt in his native Venezuela during the winter. Estrada\xe2\x80\x99s stay in the major leagues lasted one game, as the Yankees swapped his spot for infielder Giovanny Urshela, a stout defender with some past major league experience who will play a lot of third base.'
b'The star infielder Manny Machado, a free agent this off-season, would help the Yankees immensely now. But they decided over the winter that his asking price was too high \xe2\x80\x94 he eventually signed with the San Diego Padres for what was a record $300 million over 10 years \xe2\x80\x94 and they could spread their money around with various additions while relying on Gleyber Torres, Andujar, LeMahieu, and Tulowitzki.'
b'The result was an opening day payroll of nearly $204 million \xe2\x80\x94 less than what it was in 2015 ($218 million) and 2016 ($226 million), according to Cot\xe2\x80\x99s Baseball Contracts. (The Yankees are over the $206 million luxury-tax threshold because that takes into account the entire 40-man roster, and yearly salaries are calculated differently.)'
b'That roster \xe2\x80\x94 the second-most expensive in the majors, behind the Red Sox \xe2\x80\x94 has hobbled out of the gate, but Manager Aaron Boone has maintained the long view.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re always capable of going on a roll,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s a matter of time. That\xe2\x80\x99s a matter of us starting to click all together and getting some guys hot collectively in the lineup and getting our pitchers settled in. Even banged up, I\xe2\x80\x99m confident we can go on a run at any point.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Underlying concerns remain even among the healthy members of the roster. While closer Aroldis Chapman\xe2\x80\x99s velocity is slowly trending up, his fastball velocity (through the small sample of four games) was at 96.5 miles per hour entering Saturday \xe2\x80\x94 more than 2 m.p.h. slower than last season and 4 m.p.h. slower than 2017. Pitchers sometimes take time to build their velocity during the colder months, but Chapman has used his slider more than ever. He pitched around a single for a save on Saturday.'
b'On offense, the team is without a portion of the lineup that accounted for 119 of a major-league-record 267 home runs last year \xe2\x80\x94 Andujar, Gregorius, Hicks and Stanton. With capable but less powerful hitters filling in, Boone said, the Yankees may have to rely on speed and contact for now.'
b'And there\xe2\x80\x99s catcher Gary Sanchez, who is hoping to bounce back from the worst all-around season of his career and an off-season operation on his nonthrowing shoulder. He had a team-leading three home runs but also four throwing errors, six stolen bases allowed and a few base-running blunders himself.'
b'Given the drain of talent to the I.L., the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 margin for error has shrunk. Defensive and baserunning errors loom larger. The lineup cannot strike out a team-record 18 times or strand base-runners at one of the worst rates in baseball and expect to win.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cObviously with all the injuries, there\xe2\x80\x99s more pressure on us,\xe2\x80\x9d said Luke Voit, the designated hitter, who had been slumping before he blasted a three-run homer in Thursday\xe2\x80\x99s win. \xe2\x80\x9cJust trying to do too much instead of being myself. At the end of the day, it\xe2\x80\x99s going to come around. I just had to smile and have fun.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Yankees could always look to outside additions to patch holes. But in the meantime, the team will need role players to contribute more than expected and its standouts to pull their weight. LeMahieu leads the Yankees in hitting (11 for 24). Torres, as he did at times last year, carried the Yankees to victory on Thursday with two critical home runs. First baseman Greg Bird, Voit, Sanchez and Gardner had batting averages less than .227. Judge has struck out a team-high 16 times. Frazier, who missed most of last year because of a concussion, had not hit a major league home run since July 28, 2017, before Saturday.'
b'The Yankees have plenty of reasons to remain optimistic: Sixteen of their remaining 21 games in April are against teams with losing records in 2018. And before Voit helped calm a frustrated team with his three-run blast on Thursday, he joked with his teammates that a needed contributor was returning from injury.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m officially taking my bat off the I.L.,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'

b'PHILADELPHIA \xe2\x80\x94 Greg Harris, 52, and his son Thomas, 9, wearing matching Bryce Harper jerseys, settled into their seats at Citizens Bank Park more than two hours before the Philadelphia Phillies opened their season against the Atlanta Braves on Thursday afternoon.'
b'They weren\xe2\x80\x99t Harris\xe2\x80\x99s usual seats: A longtime season-ticket holder, he had sold those, in Section 120, between home and first base, at a premium soon after the Phillies acquired Harper last month.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI sold them for today because somebody paid me $400 a ticket for them,\xe2\x80\x9d Harris said. \xe2\x80\x9cSo we\xe2\x80\x99re sitting upstairs. I was willing to make that sacrifice.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'This is the level of excitement brought to the Phillies by the acquisition of Harper, the final piece to an off-season that began with the team\xe2\x80\x99s principal owner, John Middleton, vowing to spend \xe2\x80\x9cstupid\xe2\x80\x9d money and that ended with the Phillies as a fashionable pick to win the National League and perhaps even their first World Series since 2008.'
b'While acquisitions like J.T. Realmuto, Jean Segura, Andrew McCutchen and David Robertson laid the groundwork for the outsize expectations, Harper\xe2\x80\x99s signing sent what had been an Eagles-first town to a level of baseball craziness not seen for a long time \xe2\x80\x94 at least not in this decade, since the run of the Chase Utley-Ryan Howard-Jimmy Rollins Phillies ended.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhen I was at school, my teacher comes up to me, and she\xe2\x80\x99s like: \xe2\x80\x98I just got a Yahoo Sports notification. And then she was like, \xe2\x80\x98Calm down, calm down, calm down.\xe2\x80\x99 We\xe2\x80\x99re like: \xe2\x80\x98We\xe2\x80\x99re not calming down. Do you realize how big that is?\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The hype has certainly not been lost on Phillies Manager Gabe Kapler, who had to move his pregame media availability from the dugout to his office to accommodate the crush of reporters on hand for Harper\xe2\x80\x99s debut. (The reporters were split into two groups to make the size of the room work.) But he isn\xe2\x80\x99t worried about its effect on Harper, who has been treated like baseball\xe2\x80\x99s savior since he first landed on the cover of Sports Illustrated as a teenager.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think if there\xe2\x80\x99s anybody equipped to handle that conversation without me, it\xe2\x80\x99s Bryce Harper,\xe2\x80\x9d Kapler said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s a guy well equipped for this moment, for the biggest stage, the brightest lights. b'\xe2\x80\x9cThey only had adult sizes, so we had to order his online,\xe2\x80\x9d Greg Harris said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut we got them immediately. We were part of the record-breaking shirt sales.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'On Baseball'
b'By Tyler Kepner'
b'PHOENIX \xe2\x80\x94 Maybe the faucets were just a little rusty. Spring training games are well underway, but, finally, baseball has opened up its money spigot.'
b'After a winter notable for a sluggish free-agent market that still includes a handful of prominent unsigned players, cash is now flowing to the major leagues\xe2\x80\x99 top stars. On Thursday, Bryce Harper became the latest in a string of players to set a new salary standard, reaching a free-agent deal with the Philadelphia Phillies for 13 years and $330 million, the most ever guaranteed to a baseball player.'
b'Last week, Manny Machado became the first free agent to earn a $300 million contract when he signed a 10-year deal with the San Diego Padres. On Wednesday, the Colorado Rockies made Nolan Arenado the game\xe2\x80\x99s highest-paid position player on an annual basis, at $32.5 million per season on an eight-year, $260 million extension.'
b'There were others receiving extensions this week: Yankees outfielder Aaron Hicks (seven years, $70 million) and St. Louis Cardinals starter Miles Mikolas (four years, $68 million). And while Arizona Diamondbacks pitcher Zack Greinke still claims the highest average annual value ($34.44 million per year on his six-year, $206.5 million deal), Harper stands alone for the richest overall contract.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m happy for him, and I\xe2\x80\x99m happy for all players to see him get compensated fairly,\xe2\x80\x9d said the Milwaukee Brewers\xe2\x80\x99 Ryan Braun, a former National League most valuable player who earns $21 million per season.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cFor all of us as players, we want to see our best players sign the biggest contracts, and frankly I think the whole last week has been really positive for baseball players, if you look at Aaron Hicks, Miles Mikolas and Nolan Arenado,\xe2\x80\x9d Braun continued. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s been a bit of a contentious off-season, but I think for all of us as players it\xe2\x80\x99s been an encouraging week to see all these guys compensated with contracts they\xe2\x80\x99ve earned and deserve.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Harper\xe2\x80\x99s deal, which was confirmed by a person with direct knowledge of it who spoke on the condition of anonymity because the Phillies had not yet announced it, eclipses the 13-year, $325 million contract extension Giancarlo Stanton signed with the Miami Marlins before the 2015 season, two years before he was traded to the Yankees \xe2\x80\x94 Harper\xe2\x80\x99s favorite team as he grew up in Las Vegas.'
b'While the Yankees declined to pursue Harper, investing instead in pitching this winter, he attracted significant interest from the Los Angeles Dodgers and the San Francisco Giants, fueling speculation that he preferred to play on the West Coast. As it turns out, his Phillies contract does not even include an opt-out clause \xe2\x80\x94 the escape hatch the agent Scott Boras popularized more than 18 years ago in Alex Rodriguez\xe2\x80\x99s first free-agent deal, with the Texas Rangers.'
b'But Harper, 26, wanted clarity on his future, Boras said, and did not want the chance to opt out.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe wanted to go to one city, stay there, build a brand and identity and recruit players,\xe2\x80\x9d Boras said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe wants to tell players: \xe2\x80\x98Come play with me.\xe2\x80\x99 He knows it will help winning more if he\xe2\x80\x99s with one team the whole time.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In Philadelphia, that comment comes with a two-word translation: Mike Trout. Born and raised in southern New Jersey, where he still lives, Trout will be eligible for free agency after the 2020 season. Trout, 27, has won two Most Valuable Player Awards with the Los Angeles Angels and is the consensus best player in baseball.'
b'A comparison of all the Major League Baseball players who signed contracts of at least $100 million.'
b'Harper has one M.V.P. award, from 2015 with the Washington Nationals, who drafted him first over all in 2010. He has made six All-Star teams, and he recovered from a slow start last season to hit .249 with 34 home runs, producing career highs in runs batted in (100) and walks (130). But poor defensive metrics in right and center field \xe2\x80\x94 the result of a 2017 knee injury, Boras said \xe2\x80\x94 gave him just 1.3 wins above replacement, according to Baseball Reference.'
b'Boras called Harper \xe2\x80\x9cthe most iconic figure in the game,\xe2\x80\x9d but said the low WAR, more than any other factor, complicated the pursuit of the kind of contract Harper sought.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s hard to get the length of contract the player wanted,\xe2\x80\x9d Boras said. \xe2\x80\x9cI could have done 10 years with opt-outs, but that\xe2\x80\x99s not what he wanted.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI could have done $42 or $43 million in A.A.V. on a short-term deal,\xe2\x80\x9d Boras continued, referring to average annual value. \xe2\x80\x9cYou really want to serve your client\xe2\x80\x99s interest.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Phillies stayed away from Boras\xe2\x80\x99s clients for years, the bitter residue of a failed negotiation in 1997 with outfielder J.D. Drew, their first-round draft choice. But with John S. Middleton as principal owner, the Phillies have now signed a prominent Boras client in each of the last two spring trainings. Last March, Middleton signed Jake Arrieta, a former Cy Young Award winner, for three years and $75 million.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cJohn Middleton came out two times to Las Vegas to meet with Bryce,\xe2\x80\x9d Boras said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s a guy that illustrated to Harp that he\xe2\x80\x99s about winning. He\xe2\x80\x99s very involved with his franchise \xe2\x80\x94 and I love the fact that Bryce plays so well in that ballpark and sees the ball so well there.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Of the four stadiums in which he has played the most games \xe2\x80\x94 Nationals Park, Marlins Park, the Mets\xe2\x80\x99 Citi Field and the Phillies\xe2\x80\x99 Citizens Bank Park \xe2\x80\x94 Harper has the highest on-base-plus-slugging percentage in Philadelphia, at .930. He has hit 14 home runs there, his most at any park outside Washington.'
b'While Harper has generally struggled in Los Angeles (.670 O.P.S.) and San Francisco (.588), the value of the Phillies\xe2\x80\x99 contract, understandably, was the major factor. The Giants could have sold Harper on becoming the next Barry Bonds \xe2\x80\x94 as a left-handed, free-agent slugger still on the front end of his prime \xe2\x80\x94 but they sensed the Phillies would get him.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cA lot of people thought that\xe2\x80\x99s where he was going,\xe2\x80\x9d said Giants Manager Bruce Bochy, who met with Harper in the first of the Giants\xe2\x80\x99 visits, in early February. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t think there\xe2\x80\x99s anybody who\xe2\x80\x99d say they wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t like to have a guy like that in the lineup. But I think we all felt that it seemed like that\xe2\x80\x99s the direction he was heading.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Bochy added: \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t allow myself to really think about it, because you can\xe2\x80\x99t be disappointed. You don\xe2\x80\x99t want these guys disappointed. I tell them, \xe2\x80\x98You\xe2\x80\x99ve got to be thankful for what you have versus what you don\xe2\x80\x99t have.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'What Harper has is a new address in Philadelphia \xe2\x80\x94 and the richest contract in baseball history, a victory for him and his peers.'
b'An earlier version of this article misstated the average annual salary for Nolan Arenado. It is $32.5 million per season, not $33.5 million.'

b'On Baseball'
b'By Tyler Kepner'
b'This was always the logical blueprint for Mike Trout, the greatest and least complicated player in baseball. Trout would not sell himself short financially, but he also would not draw out the process of determining his future. He and the Los Angeles Angels would wait for Bryce Harper to set a contract record in free agency, and then make a deal that would break it.'
b'That is what has happened, apparently, with Trout and the Angels finalizing a 10-year, $360 million contract extension with no opt-outs, a deal that will bring the Angels\xe2\x80\x99 total commitment to nearly $430 million for Trout over the next 12 seasons, through 2030.'
b'The agreement, which was first reported by ESPN, is expected to be formalized soon, according to two people who had been briefed on it but were not authorized to comment publicly. It is the fourth megadeal reached this spring training, following those for Nolan Arenado (eight years, $260 million with the Colorado Rockies), Manny Machado (10 years, $300 million with the San Diego Padres) and Bryce Harper (13 years, $330 million with the Philadelphia Phillies).'
b'Those contracts did little to quell the angst of the players\xe2\x80\x99 association about the relatively subdued state of the overall free agent market. The union has become so suspicious of ownership that it has moved some camp visits outside of clubhouses this spring training, for fear of possible surveillance inside team facilities. The union is dismayed at the lackluster bidding for the sort of midlevel free agents who until recently had generated much more interest on the open market.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhat we\xe2\x80\x99ve seen the last couple of years, we haven\xe2\x80\x99t seen before,\xe2\x80\x9d Tony Clark, the union\xe2\x80\x99s executive director, said on Sunday, citing \xe2\x80\x9ca climate that we don\xe2\x80\x99t think is sustainable for the industry as a whole.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The deals for Arenado, Machado and Harper, though, showed that teams still place a premium on elite talent \xe2\x80\x94 and Trout, 27, is the best of the best. The most similar players in history at his age, according to Baseball Reference, are the Hall of Famers Frank Robinson, Ken Griffey Jr. and Mickey Mantle. Trout has won two American League Most Valuable Player Awards and has been the runner-up four times. He has a .307 career average and is the majors\xe2\x80\x99 active leader in on-base plus slugging percentage, at .990.'
b'Trout\xe2\x80\x99s contract had been set to expire after the 2020 season, and Harper had publicly pushed for Trout to eventually join him in Philadelphia, where Trout attends Eagles games in the off-season, traveling from his nearby hometown, Millville, N.J. But the Angels emphasized to Trout the benefits of keeping his work and home lives separate, and promoted the idea of being a one-team icon in a place where he has thrived.'
b'In an interview this month at the Angels\xe2\x80\x99 training camp in Tempe, Ariz., Trout seemed content with the team\xe2\x80\x99s new manager, Brad Ausmus, and its other off-season additions.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s like a whole new start,\xe2\x80\x9d Trout said. \xe2\x80\x9cI think the biggest thing is injuries. We\xe2\x80\x99ve got to stay healthy, top to bottom, stay on the field and see where it goes. The chemistry\xe2\x80\x99s great, a lot of new faces, a lot of new coaches, meeting a lot of new people. Everybody\xe2\x80\x99s been great so far.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Angels have reached the playoffs with Trout just once, when they were swept by Kansas City in a 2014 division series. But the team is far from hopeless, with a 584-550 record in Trout\xe2\x80\x99s seven full seasons and a farm system that ranks No. 6 over all, according to Baseball Prospectus. Their stadium lease in Anaheim runs through 2020, so they could, in theory, open a new ballpark before Trout retires.'
b'A comparison of all the Major League Baseball players who signed contracts of at least $100 million.'
b'Since wildly overpaying for Albert Pujols and Josh Hamilton early in this decade, the Angels have added high-impact players like shortstop Andrelton Simmons, outfielder Justin Upton and the two-way star Shohei Ohtani. General Manager Billy Eppler signed catcher Jonathan Lucroy and pitchers Cody Allen, Trevor Cahill and Matt Harvey to one-year deals this winter, and he has steadily modernized the way the Angels use technology.'
b'Still, the Houston Astros are the dominant team in the A.L. West, and Trout could have used his clout to publicly demand that the organization do more to close the gap. He never has, he said in a 2017 interview in Anaheim, because he believes in Eppler and his lieutenants.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThey\xe2\x80\x99re doing a good job, trying to put the players in the right spots,\xe2\x80\x9d Trout said then. \xe2\x80\x9cYou\xe2\x80\x99ve got to trust it. There\xe2\x80\x99s only so much that they can do.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Had Trout played out his deal, the noise around his future would only have intensified, surely an unappealing prospect for a player who never courts controversy. Yet Trout is not exactly withdrawn. He is readily accessible to reporters, he is an active \xe2\x80\x94 if benign \xe2\x80\x94 presence on social media, and he might lead the league in signing autographs.'
b'Trout has a few endorsement deals but does not spend much time promoting his personal brand, a source of frustration for Major League Baseball, which would rather its best player showed more interest in marketing. To Trout, though, that has never made much sense.'
b'Trout has always seemed to recognize how good he has it, with little incentive to disrupt that life. He is dominant on the field and respected off it; comfortable with the direction of his franchise; happy in both Southern California and Southern New Jersey; and extremely well paid. Who could ask for more?'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf you were Mike Trout,\xe2\x80\x9d his agent, Craig Landis, once asked, \xe2\x80\x9cwould you really wake up in the morning and say, \xe2\x80\x98I\xe2\x80\x99ve got to start changing things\xe2\x80\x99?\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It was a rhetorical question, of course, and Trout has now answered with a resounding no. You cannot blame him, and you cannot be surprised.'

b'Acuna, last season\xe2\x80\x99s National League Rookie of the Year, is hitting .579 with seven runs, three homers and eight R.B.I. over his last five games. Freeman began the day leading the league in on-base percentage; he has reached safely in Atlanta\xe2\x80\x99s first 14 games.'
b'The Braves went ahead, 8-4, in the second off reliever Corey Oswalt on R.B.I. by Freeman, Acuna, Markakis and Swanson. Markakis\xe2\x80\x99s first home run of the season made it 9-4 in the fourth. Oswalt allowed six hits and five runs in three and two-thirds innings.'

b'Advertisement'
b'Supported by'
b'By James Wagner'
b'PHILADELPHIA \xe2\x80\x94 While writing a sermon in September, Cheryl Pyrch, the pastor of Summit Presbyterian Church, needed an assist. On the topic of greatness and Jesus Christ, she wanted to open with recollections of greats in other spheres.'
b'She didn\xe2\x80\x99t have to look very far for a source.'
b'Having encountered Wilt Chamberlain in passing almost 40 years ago, she decided he was the great she wanted to highlight. And details of his career \xe2\x80\x94 four Most Valuable Player Awards, seven N.B.A. scoring titles \xe2\x80\x94 were close at hand, literally and figuratively through Sports Reference, a monolith of sports data websites that just happens to rent space from the church.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI didn\xe2\x80\x99t know all this in 1980,\xe2\x80\x9d Pyrch told the congregation as she described Chamberlain\xe2\x80\x99s awards during the Sunday service. \xe2\x80\x9cI got it yesterday from a Sports Reference website.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The ubiquitous Sports Reference family of websites \xe2\x80\x94 Baseball-Reference.com, Basketball-Reference.com, Pro-Football-Reference.com, Hockey-Reference.com, and so on \xe2\x80\x94 are some of the most popular sports almanacs on the internet.'
b'They draw users of all kinds, from people casually searching for a trivia answer to owners of professional teams. Aided by an overhaul of its mobile website, Sports Reference\xe2\x80\x99s founder and president, Sean Forman, said the group of sites drew one billion page views last year, a record for the company.'
b'Sports Reference, however, does not have the gleaming offices or huge staff of a digital titan. It has 11 full-time employees and is headquartered on the third floor of a building at Summit Presbyterian in Philadelphia, behind the 100-year-old main church and above the gymnasium, which is often used as a day care center.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWalking through it to come in and out, sometimes you\xe2\x80\x99re going through 3-year-olds tossing balls,\xe2\x80\x9d said Mike Kania, 38, who eight years ago became one of the company\xe2\x80\x99s first employees. \xe2\x80\x9cI worked for AOL for a long time where we had a badge to scan at the front door, people there and a front desk. It\xe2\x80\x99s a lot different from that.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It is, in fact, a point of pride among Sports Reference employees that the sites have grown from humble beginnings into oft-used resources. Until late last year, Forman, 47, was cleaning the office and taking out the trash. (He has since hired the church\xe2\x80\x99s janitor to take over those duties.)'
b'They are among the most popular sports-related sites. Basketball-Reference trails only NBA.com, while Pro-Football-Reference is second to NFL.com, according to SimilarWeb. Nearly two decades after Forman created Baseball-Reference, it ranks third among baseball sites, behind MLB.com and MLBTradeRumors.com. (Baseball-Reference, however, is the top draw in Forman\xe2\x80\x99s stable.)'
b'The sites are not just for casual fans. J.J. Redick, the Philadelphia 76ers guard, pays for an advertising-free Basketball-Reference subscription. John Henry, the principal owner of the Boston Red Sox and Liverpool F.C., uses Baseball-Reference\xe2\x80\x99s Play Index to manage statistical searches. Scott Boras, the well-known baseball agent, donated $100 to the company during its infancy because he had relied on the site\xe2\x80\x99s data while negotiating a contract for Andruw Jones, Forman said.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI use it daily,\xe2\x80\x9d said Thad Levine, the Minnesota Twins general manager, although his team, like many others, generates its own advanced and proprietary data.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe went so far as to hire one of their back-end programmers,\xe2\x80\x9d added Levine, referring to Hans Van Slooten, who oversaw Baseball-Reference until June, when the Twins hired him for their front office.'
b'The sites are still expanding and developing. Forman said he envisioned Basketball-Reference eventually surpassing Baseball-Reference in traffic as a result of the data revolution in the N.B.A. And over the summer, Sports Reference began another major undertaking: a soccer website, FBref.com, which the company hopes will be as comprehensive as its other sites. In a twist from its current offerings, the company is planning to make the soccer site bilingual, with English and Spanish versions.'
b'The sites are painstakingly tweaked for updates and corrections. Some errors are reported through the dozens of emails the company receives daily. One came from the mother of Casey Fossum, a former major league pitcher. She wrote to say that her son\xe2\x80\x99s birth date was wrong. It was corrected.'
b'Other requests reveal the reach of Sports Reference.'
b'A pitching coach sent an email asking that his Italian league statistics be added to his page so that his players would stop teasing him about being a bad pitcher. A woman wrote in to say that she was dating a person who claimed to be a former N.F.L. player but that she could not find him on Pro-Football-Reference. She wanted to know if that was because of an oversight or a lie.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI tried to let her down as gently as possible,\xe2\x80\x9d said Mike Lynch, 37, whose official title with the company is managing stathead. \xe2\x80\x9cI said something like, \xe2\x80\x98If he was cut in training camp, we wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t necessarily have a record of him playing in a regular season game.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Sports Reference started with Baseball-Reference in 2000, when Forman, looking to avoid work on his doctoral dissertation on applied mathematical and computational sciences at the University of Iowa, began building a website from the CD-ROM that accompanied the printed Total Baseball encyclopedias. He hoped to make historical data more accessible.'
b'Forman, who has contributed to The New York Times\xe2\x80\x99s baseball coverage in the past, expanded his endeavor by creating Sports Reference in 2004. Three years later he formalized loose affiliations with Pro-Football-Reference (founded by Doug Drinen in 2000) and Basketball-Reference (founded by Justin Kubatko in 2004). Kubatko left Sports Reference in 2013 because of what he called \xe2\x80\x9ccreative differences.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In 2007, Forman still fit the stats nerd stereotype, working out of the basement of his home and staying up until 1 a.m. updating or improving the website. The year before, he had left his full-time job of six years \xe2\x80\x94 professor of mathematics and computer science at St. Joseph\xe2\x80\x99s University \xe2\x80\x94 because it was too hard to juggle both. He also needed a better place to work.'
b'So Forman turned to his church, which had space to rent.'
b'Sports Reference\xe2\x80\x99s seven websites are usually updated automatically, mostly from official feeds of statistics that the company pays for. Some data, such as roster transactions or salary information, is input manually, and there are always bugs to fix.'
b'Once you get beyond the basics, however, the information on the sites runs the gamut of sources.'
b'They include a collection of old college media guides acquired from a single collector and a professor in Britain who supplies statistics of independent baseball leagues. The sites also add some things just for fun, such as Oddibe McDowell\xe2\x80\x99s page listing his utility bills from 2011 and part of 2012, in reference to a series of articles by Deadspin.'
b'Sports Reference\xe2\x80\x99s goal is to become more comprehensive, even as sports leagues increasingly privatize their data. Eventually, the company hopes to charge for advanced features and to become less dependent on advertising, which currently generates 95 percent of the sites\xe2\x80\x99 revenue. As of now, the only advanced tool that requires a paid subscription is Baseball-Reference\xe2\x80\x99s Play Index. (Don\xe2\x80\x99t worry: The page for the former Met Keith Hernandez\xe2\x80\x99s mustache will live forever.)'
b'That the little company in her church has become so important, with leading sports websites, earned a laugh from Pyrch. She had been to the sites once or twice, including the time she did sermon research.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think that both myself and most of the congregation would not realize what kind of a powerhouse Sports Reference is,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t really know a lot about numbers or computers, but one billion is a lot.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'To the Sports Editor: '
b'Re \xe2\x80\x9cFor Jackie Robinson\xe2\x80\x99s Centennial, a Display of Rarely Seen Photographs,\xe2\x80\x9d Jan. 31: In my 80s now. The special section about Jackie Robinson is a forever treasure.'
b'In my boyhood in Logansport, Ind., a childhood friend of my father\xe2\x80\x99s was Johnny (Red) Corriden, who made the big leagues and was a Brooklyn Dodgers coach in the 1940s. At the end of the season, he would stop by our home in Logansport, and each visit Red would say, \xe2\x80\x9cHere Johnny\xe2\x80\x9d and present me with a brand-new official major league baseball.'
b'This writer, only 7 when this started and 1,000 miles from Brooklyn, became a lifelong Dodgers fan. Along came 1946, and Robinson was at Montreal. Everything possible was read about him, and then came 1947. (Corriden by then was a Yankees coach.)'
b'My local drugstore for some wild reason had a Jackie Robinson comic book for sale. With 10 cents from my allowance, I got the comic book and was reading it on the front porch when my father, a white man born in 1891, saw me with it and said, \xe2\x80\x9cSon, it\xe2\x80\x99s all right that you root for that colored and all right that you read that comic book, but do not let anyone know about this.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'For a 10-year-old who believed that his parents were always right, there was stunning mystification. In the early spring of 1947, we rode the train to Chicago to see the Dodgers play the Cubs. We had good seats near the visitors\xe2\x80\x99 dugout (somehow Corriden arranged this, even though he was with the Yankees).'
b'As not everyone knows, Robinson played first base his rookie year. When he stepped out of the dugout, in the Dodgers\xe2\x80\x99 traveling grays, and made his pigeon-toed trot to first base, all at once two things were known by me: My all-time sports hero was right before my eyes, and my father had feet of clay.'
b'This watershed moment has affected my views about civility forever. On the 40th anniversary of Robinson\xe2\x80\x99s rookie year, I sent a short note to Rachel Robinson, Jackie\xe2\x80\x99s widow, simply stating that his heroism had reached and forever touched a 10-year-old a thousand miles away.'
b'John F. Dunn'
b'Decatur, Ill.'
b'To the Sports Editor:'
b'My fanatical loyalty to the distant Brooklyn Dodgers led to many fights and much peer mockery (as the Dodgers lost too many World Series) when I was 6 in a 1950 Larchmont, N.Y., neighborhood of Yankees fans.'
b'Jackie Robinson, my hero, ran faster, hit more cannily, executed double plays and taunted opposition pitchers and infielders with greater skill, guts and swagger than anyone else in the game (to the best of my unstatistical knowledge). Stealing home, to my later Little Leaguer\xe2\x80\x99s mind, was nearly impossible, but Robinson succeeded 20 times and attempted even more.'
b'At first, I did not know his race. I did not understand such categories. He was just the greatest ballplayer. A little older, I knew better and learned that getting to first base was only one of the difficulties that faced my American hero (in every sense of that word).'
b'So when \xe2\x80\x9cnext year\xe2\x80\x9d became \xe2\x80\x9cthis year\xe2\x80\x9d (some readers will understand that phrase), tears came to my eyes. When the Dodgers moved to L.A., it happened again. When Jackie Robinson died young, I wept. When I read The Times\xe2\x80\x99s special section, once more I cried.'
b'Donald Lateiner'
b'Delaware, Ohio'
b'To the Sports Editor:'
b'As deserving as Jackie Robinson is of all the attention he has received, it is a shame that Larry Doby is all but ignored. Doby broke the color barrier in the American League two months after Robinson broke in with the Dodgers. He faced all the same difficulties as Robinson, overcame all the same hurdles and persevered to have a great career, helping Cleveland win the 1948 World Series. Yet we see no biopics or retrospectives of Doby. No. 42 has been retired from baseball, but No. 14 goes unhonored. Perhaps playing in New York is the reason for the difference. But whatever the reason, there is no doubt that Doby is in fact deserving of recognition to the same degree as Robinson.'
b'Mark B. Cohn'
b'Naples, Fla.'

b'On Baseball'
b'By Tyler Kepner'
b'The St. Louis Cardinals went three long seasons without a playoff berth. To rouse themselves from this interminable slumber, they traded for a former All-Star who had played his entire career for a West division team, winning multiple Gold Gloves but never reaching the World Series. The player was facing the end of his contract, but the Cardinals hoped to persuade him to stay for many years.'
b'This is true of Paul Goldschmidt now. Nineteen years ago, it was true for Jim Edmonds.'
b'The latter partnership worked quite well: Edmonds, who had come up with the Angels, signed a long-term contract during his first season in St. Louis, led the Cardinals to a division title and eventually helped them win a World Series. The Gold Gloves and All-Star selections kept coming for Edmonds, who earned the coveted red sports coat last summer as a member of the team\xe2\x80\x99s Hall of Fame.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s Cardinal baseball, it\xe2\x80\x99s the Midwest, it\xe2\x80\x99s one of the best places to play in the country, and you find that out from Day 1,\xe2\x80\x9d said Edmonds, now a guest instructor and broadcaster for the Cardinals. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a different time, a different era and I don\xe2\x80\x99t know what the players are going through now, but hopefully he likes it and blends in. It\xe2\x80\x99s also an organizational thing, too. Do they really want to keep him, and how does he play this year?\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Cardinals, who last reached the postseason in 2015, very much want to keep Goldschmidt, a six-time All-Star first baseman with three Gold Gloves. They acquired him from the Arizona Diamondbacks last Dec. 5 for pitcher Luke Weaver, catcher Carson Kelly, infielder Andy Young and a draft pick, finally landing the high-impact slugger they\xe2\x80\x99ve been missing.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAnytime you complete a deal, there\xe2\x80\x99s always some level of satisfaction, especially this magnitude of player \xe2\x80\x94 but, really, the excitement\xe2\x80\x99s going to come when he gets introduced at Busch Stadium,\xe2\x80\x9d said John Mozeliak, the Cardinals\xe2\x80\x99 president of baseball operations. \xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s a lot leading up to that, but I think he\xe2\x80\x99s going to realize that St. Louis is a very special place and ultimately one that we want him to someday call home.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Mozeliak has not yet spoken with Goldschmidt or his agent, Casey Close, about a contract extension \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9cBoth sides will know when the time is right,\xe2\x80\x9d he said \xe2\x80\x94 and Goldschmidt declined to comment on his future. Any answer he could give would be incomplete, because he has not yet experienced life as a Cardinal.'
b'The team has finished second in the National League in attendance in each of the last six seasons \xe2\x80\x94 behind the Los Angeles Dodgers \xe2\x80\x94 and has a 15-year streak of drawing at least 3 million fans. The Diamondbacks have not reached 3 million fans since 2002, when Goldschmidt was a high school freshman near Houston.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s a ton of support for the Cardinals organization, for the players there,\xe2\x80\x9d Goldschmidt said. \xe2\x80\x9cThey love their team. There\xe2\x80\x99s high expectations from the fans, and rightfully so. Hopefully we\xe2\x80\x99ll play well, give them a good show and find a way to win a lot of games.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Cardinals last won the World Series eight years ago, a fact they emphasized on printouts taped by the clubhouse door Monday, when they held their first full-squad workout of spring training. The sheet listed a few goals \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\x9ctrust, prepare, execute, celebrate\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 and included three columns of championship years, with a conspicuously blank line beneath 2011.'
b'Only one player from that World Series roster, catcher Yadier Molina, remains on the team. The Cardinals have stayed above .500 ever since \xe2\x80\x94 and even won a pennant in 2013 \xe2\x80\x94 but rivals have passed them by.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s tough, man,\xe2\x80\x9d said second baseman Kolten Wong, who has played six seasons in St. Louis. \xe2\x80\x9cFor me, all I knew when I first got to the big leagues was playoffs every single year. To go from that to not making it the past three years, I\xe2\x80\x99m itching to get back. Everyone deserves to get back, and our fans deserve it more.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In the seven seasons since 2011 \xe2\x80\x94 Albert Pujols\xe2\x80\x99s last in St. Louis before signing with the Angels as a free agent \xe2\x80\x94 no Cardinals player has hit 30 home runs with a .900 on-base plus slugging percentage in the same season. This has been done 67 times in those seasons by 39 different players \xe2\x80\x94 including four times by Goldschmidt.'
b'Yet Goldschmidt, 31, is more than a power hitter. He has a .297 career average and five seasons of at least 15 stolen bases, plus the three Gold Gloves. Before reporting to camp, he spoke with coaches on the phone about the finer points of base running.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe actually initiated those, and they\xe2\x80\x99re not short conversations, and they\xe2\x80\x99re not forced,\xe2\x80\x9d Manager Mike Shildt said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe loves it, he\xe2\x80\x99s a baseball guy, and he\xe2\x80\x99s got the details.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The Cardinals turned to Shildt, an organizational lifer, after firing Mike Matheny as manager last July. The players responded with a late push for a playoff spot, finishing with 88 victories and a renewed sense of identity.'
b'As an organization well-known for attention to fundamentals, it was startling for the Cardinals to lead the majors in errors. Yet they committed in the second half to strong defenders like Wong at second and Harrison Bader in center field, and in the winter they stabilized their bullpen with a two-year, $25 million deal for Andrew Miller.'
b'Wherever he has gone recently \xe2\x80\x94 Boston, Baltimore, the Yankees, Cleveland \xe2\x80\x94 Miller\xe2\x80\x99s teams have made the playoffs. The Cardinals have their three-year drought, but Miller has a six-year streak. He believes it will continue.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhen you\xe2\x80\x99re at the stage of your career that I am, that\xe2\x80\x99s where you tend to find yourself,\xe2\x80\x9d Miller said. \xe2\x80\x9cThe teams that seek you out, that\xe2\x80\x99s their intention: \xe2\x80\x98Not next year, not five years down the road, but this year.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'This year \xe2\x80\x94 for now \xe2\x80\x94 is the extent of the Cardinals\xe2\x80\x99 future with Goldschmidt. In time, their owners will put a value on how much they want to keep him. On opening day in St. Louis, the fans will start their effort, too.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cTalking about it is hard to sell,\xe2\x80\x9d Mozeliak said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut experiencing it is different.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'Yankees 7, Orioles 2'
b'By James Wagner'
b'Glorious daydreams abound on opening day, when each team\xe2\x80\x99s slate is clean and the season\xe2\x80\x99s inevitable trials and tribulations haven\xe2\x80\x99t yet piled up. But the images of winning a pennant and hoisting the World Series trophy are far more realistic for some \xe2\x80\x94 the 2019 Yankees included.'
b'Their season of high expectations, at the tail end of a championship-less decade, began Thursday afternoon with a booming first chapter. With a formula they expect to ride often this year, the Yankees toppled the Baltimore Orioles, 7-2, behind power hitting and pitching.'
b'Designated hitter Luke Voit provided the bulk of the power by smashing the team\xe2\x80\x99s first home run of the season, a three-run shot in the first inning. He drove in another run when he was hit by a pitch with the bases loaded in the fifth, ultimately accounting for four runs with a blast and a bruise.'
b'There was more offense to come after his homer, but Voit\xe2\x80\x99s contributions proved more than enough against the rebuilding Orioles in front of a crowd of 46,928 at Yankee Stadium.'
b'Masahiro Tanaka, starting because of a shoulder injury to the ace Luis Severino, earned his first opening-day victory in four tries as a Yankee. He allowed two runs, one earned, and struck out five batters over five and two-thirds innings, then stepped aside for the onslaught that is the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 new and improved bullpen.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt was an ideal way to go about a game, as far as pitching goes,\xe2\x80\x9d Tanaka said.'
b'There was little anxiety for the pitching staff thanks to the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 potent lineup. After setting a major league record with 267 home runs last season, the Yankees predicted they would top that this year.'
b'With two home runs in their first game, they are on a pace to do so. First baseman Greg Bird also homered, to right-center field in the eighth inning. The blast helped cancel out a few boos for Bird, who had struck out in each of his first three at-bats.'
b'But on Thursday, at least, it all started with Voit. About a year ago, he was with the St. Louis Cardinals\xe2\x80\x99 Class AAA team in Memphis. The Yankees, needing a first baseman because of injuries and underperformance, saw Voit as an undervalued player and acquired him in a minor trade in July.'
b'Given a chance to play, he proved crucial to the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 playoff push. He hit 14 home runs in 39 games and started all of the Yankees\xe2\x80\x99 playoff games. He battled Bird for the first-base job this year, but both ended up on the opening-day roster thanks to a nagging back injury to center fielder Aaron Hicks.'
b'And on Voit\xe2\x80\x99s first major league opening day, the Yankees trusted him with the power spot of the lineup, fourth, behind his fellow sluggers Aaron Judge and Giancarlo Stanton. After Judge and Stanton singled off Orioles starter Andrew Cashner, Voit came up and saw a low slider on his fifth pitch. Listed at 6 feet 3 inches and 225 pounds, Voit and his powerful swing sent the ball over the center-field fence.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cTo have that first opening day and hit a home run is pretty special,\xe2\x80\x9d Voit said, \xe2\x80\x9cand something I\xe2\x80\x99ll remember for the rest of my life.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'A couple of caveats should be noted with the victory: It was against the Orioles, who had the worst record in baseball last season. On the other hand, this Yankees squad is not yet whole.'
b'Pitcher C. C. Sabathia is serving a five-game suspension stemming from an incident in which he threw at Jesus Sucre last fall and will have to spend addition time on the injured list, as he is still building up from off-season operations on his heart and a knee. He is expected to return sometime in April, which is when reliever Dellin Betances and Hicks are also supposed to be back. Severino is out until May. Shortstop Didi Gregorius is expected back from elbow surgery over the summer.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a long season,\xe2\x80\x9d Yankees Manager Aaron Boone said after Thursday\xe2\x80\x99s win. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd I\xe2\x80\x99d tell you that if I walked in here and we lost the game. So, sure, we want to get off to a good start and play our best baseball.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He added: \xe2\x80\x9cBut one game sometimes, either way, doesn\xe2\x80\x99t necessarily bleed into anything. I look for individuals trying to get a few firsts out of the way so you can settle into the routine and grind of the season so it becomes more normal.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'With this core of players, the Yankees have shown tantalizing potential. They fell one game short of the World Series in 2017 but were bounced in a 2018 American League division series by the Boston Red Sox, their fierce rivals and the eventual champions.'
b'Once the Yankees were sent packing last October, Judge said he couldn\xe2\x80\x99t bring himself to the watch the rest of the postseason. His 2019 goals include winning the A.L. East, which the Yankees haven\xe2\x80\x99t done since 2012, and advancing further in the playoffs.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s always on your mind, especially starting a new season,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'To reach that goal, the Yankees tried to build up their pitching staff. This winter, they traded prospects for starting pitcher James Paxton and spent $140 million, most of it either re-signing or adding starting pitchers J.A. Happ and Sabathia, and relief pitchers Zack Britton and Adam Ottavino.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe won 100 games last year, and we\xe2\x80\x99re even better than we were last year,\xe2\x80\x9d Stanton said.'
b'Glimpses showed on Thursday. Ottavino, a newcomer who grew up a Yankees fan in Brooklyn, struck out three batters with his wicked arsenal over one and a third innings. He was followed by Britton, who worked around a walk and a hit for a scoreless eighth inning. Closer Aroldis Chapman had little issue in the ninth to close out the first of what the Yankees hope is many more wins.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cSo many things factor into reaching a World Series,\xe2\x80\x9d said shortstop Troy Tulowitzki, another newcomer, who went 1 for 4. \xe2\x80\x9cIt has to come together. You go through ups and down during the season, and it\xe2\x80\x99s all about how you kind of ride that ship. This team has the talent but that\xe2\x80\x99s only half the battle.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'Supported by'
b'By Reuters'
b"(Reuters) - The New York Yankees are Major League Baseball's most valuable team for a 22nd consecutive year, according to the annual list published by business magazine Forbes."
b'The 27-time World Series champion, which has held the top spot since Forbes began tracking MLB team finances in 1998, is worth $4.6 billion, the publisher said in a statement on Wednesday.'
b"The figure is up 15 percent from a year ago and more than double the league's average value."
b'The Los Angeles Dodgers ($3.3 billion), reigning World Series champion Boston Red Sox ($3.2 billion), Chicago Cubs ($3.1 billion) and San Francisco Giants ($3 billion) rounded out the top five.'
b"The average MLB team is now worth $1.8 billion, an 8 percent increase from last year, due in large part to a continued escalation in the value of the sport's media rights."
b'"The fact that Fox has agreed to pay almost 50 percent more for its national media deal with MLB beginning with the 2022 season shows that baseball content has significantly increased in value," said Mike Ozanian, assistant managing editor at Forbes.'
b' (Reporting by Frank Pingue in Augusta, Georgia; editing Mike Harrison)'
